Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
beginner
6 min
Mudarabah: Definition, Legitimacy, and Legal Nature
Introduces the Book of Mudarabah with linguistic derivation and legal basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definition of mudarabah, identify its legitimacy based on taqrir, and explain the legal nature of the capital as amanah and the mudarib's role as agent and partner upon profit.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is a partnership of capital and labor, legitimized by prophetic confirmation and the Companions' practice.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi concept of mudarabah (silent partnership). We begin with the linguistic origin of the term, then explore the legal basis that makes it a valid and recommended transaction. Finally, we examine the legal nature of the capital in the mudarib's hands and the consequences if the contract becomes invalid or the mudarib transgresses. Understanding these foundational principles is essential before studying detailed rulings.

Guided Path
1
Trace the linguistic derivation
Identify the Arabic root of 'mudarabah' (ض ر ب) and its connection to traveling. Note the alternative term 'qirad' used by the Hijazis and its meaning of 'cutting'.
The term emphasizes the mudarib's effort and movement.
2
Establish the legal basis
The text states mudarabah is legislated due to need, citing the Prophet’s taqrir (tacit approval) and the Companions’ practice. This is a proof of permissibility in Hanafi usul.
Taqrir is a source of law (dalil).
3
Determine the nature of the capital
The capital given to the mudarib is a trust (amanah), not a debt or collateral. The mudarib is an agent (wakil) in transactions.
If profit occurs, the mudarib becomes a partner (sharik).
4
Identify consequences of irregularity or transgression
If the mudarabah becomes invalid (fasid), it transforms into a hire contract (ijarah) and the mudarib receives market wage. If the mudarib violates terms, he becomes a guarantor (damin) for the capital.
This shows the protective nature of the contract.

Source Text

بمعنی قطع ہے اور صاحب مال اپنا کچھ مال کاٹ کر مضارب کو دیتا ہے۔ نیز یہ باہم بدلہ دینے کے لئے بھی آتا ہے۔ برج بن مسہر طائی کا شعر ہے۔ ايل هداك الله ای بنی اب نــــــــــارضك الامـــــوال والــــود بـيـــنــــــا من الناس يسعـى سـعـيـنـا ويـقـارض كان القلوب راضهالك رائض . اے دوست خدا تجھ کو راہ پر لائے ۔ لوگوں سے پوچھ کہ کون سی ایک باپ کی اولاد ہم جیسی کوشش اور معاملہ کرتی ہے۔ ہم تجھ سے آپس میں مالوں اور دوستی کا معاملہ کرتے ہیں۔ گویا ہمارے دلوں کو تیرے لئے کسی درست کنندہ نے درست کر دیا ہے۔ مضاربہ کا لغوی معنی وجه تسمیه، حکم شرعی الْمُضَارَبَةِ مُشْتَقَةٌ مِنَ الضَّرْبِ فِى الْأَرْضِ سُمّى بِهِ لِاَنَّ الْمُضَارِبِ يَسْتَحِقُ الرِّبْحَ بِسَعْيِهِ وَعَمَلِهِ وَهِيَ مَشْرُوعَةٌ لِلْحَاجَةِ إِلَيْهَا فَإِنَّ النَّاسَ بَيْنَ غَنِى بِالْمَالِ غَبِى عَنِ التَّصَرُّفِ فِيْهِ وَبَيْنَ مُهْتَدِ فِي التَّصَرُّفِ صَفْرِ الْيَدِ عَنْهُ فَمَسَّتِ الْحَاجَةُ إِلَى شَرْعِ هَذَا النَّوْعِ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ لِيَنْظَمَ مَصْلِحَةَ الْغَنِي وَالذِكِى وَالْفَقِيرِ وَالْغَنِي وَبُعِثَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَالنَّاسُ يُبَاشِرُونَهُ فَقَرَّرَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ وَتَعَامَلَتْ بِهِ الصَّحَابَةُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ ثُمَّ الْمَدْفُوعُ إِلَى الْمُضَارِبِ اَمَانَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ لِأَنَّهُ قَبَضَهُ بِأَمْرِ مَالِكِهِ لَا عَلَى وَجْهِ الْبَدَلِ وَالْوَثِيقَةِ وَهُوَ وَكِيلٌ فِيهِ. لأَنَّهُ يَتَصَرَّفُ فِيهِ بِأَمْرِ مَالِكِهِ وَإِذَا رَبِحَ فَهُوَ شَرِيكَ فِيهِ لِتَمَلْكِهِ جُزْءاً مِنَ الْمَالِ بِعَمَلِهِ فَإِذَا فَسَدَتِ ظَهَرَتِ الْإِجَارَةُ حَتَّى اسْتَوجَبَ الْعَامِلُ أَجْرَ مِثْلِهِ وَإِذَا خَالَفَ كَانَ عَاصِبًا لِوُجُودِ التَّعْدِي مِنْهُ عَلَى مَالِ غَيْرِهِ ترجمہ مضاربت ضرب فی الارض سے مشتق ہے۔ یہ نام اس لئے رکھا گیا کہ مضارب اپنی سعی و کوشش سے نفع کا مستحق ہوتا ہے اور یہ مشروع ہے۔ اس کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے کیونکہ بعض لوگ مال سے غنی اور اس میں تصرف سے بدرائے ہوتے ہیں۔ اور بعض لوگ تصرف میں راہ یاب اور مال سے خالی ہاتھ ہوتے ہیں۔ پس اس قسم کے تصرف کے مشروع ہونے کی ضرورت واقع ہوئی۔ تاکہ عقلمند و بے وقوف اور تو نگر و فقیر کی مصلحتیں منظم ہوسکیں۔ اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم مبعوث ہوئے۔ اس حال میں کہ لوگ یہ معاملہ کرتے تھے۔ پس آپ نے ان کو اس پر برقرار رکھا اور صحابہ کرام نے بھی اس پر عمل کیا ہے۔ پھر مضارب کو جو مال دیا گیا وہ اس کے قبضہ میں امانت ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے مالک کے حکم سے قبضہ کیا ہے۔ بطریق عوض
Book of Mudarabah. Translation: This book is about the explanation of mudarabah. ... Explanation: After settlement, he is explaining the rulings of mudarabah, because mudarabah is similar to settlement in that in both, the substitute comes from one side. Mudarabah linguistically is mufa'alah from darb fi al-ard, meaning walking and travelling on earth. Allah says: 'And others traveling in the land seeking from the bounty of Allah.' Al-Raghib said: al-darb fi al-ard means going therein, and it is by foot. This contract is called mudarabah because the mudarib travels on earth mostly to gain profit, and through his effort and work he becomes entitled to profit. The people of Hijaz call it muqaradah and qirad, because qard means cutting, and the owner cuts some of his property and gives it to the mudarib. It also comes in the meaning of exchanging. Poem of Birj bin Mus-hir al-Ta'i: ... (translation of poem) ... The lexical meaning, reason of naming, legal ruling: Mudarabah is derived from darb fi al-ard; it is named thus because the mudarib becomes entitled to profit through his effort and work. It is legislated due to the need for it. For people are either wealthy with money but ignorant of managing it, or skilled in management but empty-handed. So there is a need to legislate this type of transaction to organize the interests of rich and poor, clever and simple. The Prophet (Allah bless him and give him peace) was sent and people were practicing it, so he confirmed them upon it. The Companions (Allah be pleased with them) also practiced it. Then the capital given to the mudarib is a trust in his hand, because he took possession by order of its owner, not as a substitute or collateral. He is an agent in it, because he transacts in it by the owner's order. If he profits, he is a partner in it because he owns a part of the capital through his work. If it becomes invalid, then the contract of hire manifests, so the worker becomes entitled to his like wage. If he violates (the terms), he becomes a guarantor (liable) due to transgression on another's property.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Mudarabah (Silent Partnership) in Ashraf al-Hidayah. The author provides the linguistic derivation: mudarabah comes from 'darb fi al-ard' (traveling on earth), because the mudarib (working partner) travels to engage in trade. It is also called qirad or muqaradah among the Hijazis. The legal ruling is that mudarabah is legitimate (mashru'ah) due to necessity: some people have capital but lack business acumen, others have skills but no capital. The legislation balances their interests. Evidence includes the Prophet's (ﷺ) confirmation (taqrir) of the practice among the people, and the Companions' continued practice. The text then explains the legal nature of the capital: it is a trust (amanah) in the mudarib's hands, because he takes it by permission, not as a substitute. He is an agent (wakil) in transacting, and if there is profit, he becomes a partner (sharik) by earning a share through his work. If the mudarabah becomes invalid (fasid), then the contract transforms into a hire (ijarah), and the worker becomes entitled to the market wage (ujr al-mithl). If the mudarib violates the terms, he becomes a guarantor (damin) due to transgression. This establishes the fundamental principles of the mudarabah contract in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A contract where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital and the other (mudarib) provides labor, with profit shared according to an agreed ratio.
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner who manages the capital and is entitled to a share of the profit.
قراض (qirad): Synonym for mudarabah, used by the people of Hijaz.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal nature of the capital in the hand of the mudarib according to the text?
A) A debt owed to the mudarib
B) A trust (amanah) in the mudarib's possession
C) A loan from the owner
D) A collateral for the owner

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is a legitimate partnership contract based on trust and agency, with the mudarib becoming a partner upon profit and a guarantor upon transgression.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate

Nature and Ruling of Mudarabah
Explaining the derivation, legislative basis, and legal nature of mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the derivation, legislative basis, and legal nature of mudarabah, and identify the Hanafi ruling on the mudarib's liability when he violates.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is a trust-based partnership in profit, but a violating mudarib becomes a guarantor.

This passage from al-Hidayah explains that mudarabah derives from darb (traveling for trade) and was legislated to serve the needs of both capital owners and skilled workers. It then analyses the mudarib's multiple legal capacities—trustee, agent, and partner—and finally addresses a dispute over the violator's liability: the Hanafi school (majority) holds he is a guarantor, while a minority view (Ali, Hasan, Zuhri) disagrees.

Guided Path
1
Trace the linguistic derivation
Identify that mudarabah comes from darb fi al-ard (traveling for trade), because the mudarib earns profit through his effort and travel.
The term is also called qirad in Hijaz.
2
Identify the legislative basis
Note the need: some have capital but lack skill, others have skill but lack capital. The Prophet (saw) approved the practice, and the Companions practiced it, making it permissible.
Proof: prophetic taqrir and ijma amali of Sahaba.
3
Map the mudarib's capacities
Before profit: capital is amanah (trust). The mudarib is a wakil (agent). After profit: he becomes a sharik (partner) in the profit.
These three capacities are distinct.
4
Examine the effect of a fasid contract
If the mudarabah is invalid, it becomes an ijarah, and the mudarib is entitled to ujr al-mithl (market wage for his work).
This protects the worker even if the contract fails.
5
Engage the dispute on violation
If the mudarib violates the owner's instructions, he becomes a ghasib (usurper) and is liable for the capital. The minority view (Ali, Hasan, Zuhri) says he is not liable because he is a partner; the Hanafi majority view holds liability.
The thamarah: liability for losses due to violation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْمُضَارَبَةِ مُشْتَقَةٌ مِنَ الضَّرْبِ فِى الْأَرْضِ سُمّى بِهِ لِاَنَّ الْمُضَارِبِ يَسْتَحِقُ الرِّبْحَ بِسَعْيِهِ وَعَمَلِهِ وَهِيَ مَشْرُوعَةٌ لِلْحَاجَةِ إِلَيْهَا فَإِنَّ النَّاسَ بَيْنَ غَنِى بِالْمَالِ غَبِى عَنِ التَّصَرُّفِ فِيْهِ وَبَيْنَ مُهْتَدِ فِي التَّصَرُّفِ صَفْرِ الْيَدِ عَنْهُ فَمَسَّتِ الْحَاجَةُ إِلَى شَرْعِ هَذَا النَّوْعِ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ لِيَنْتَظِمَ مَصْلِحَةَ الْغَنِي وَالذِكِى وَالْفَقِيرِ وَالْغَنِي وَبُعِثَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَالنَّاسُ يُبَاشِرُونَهُ فَقَرَّرَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ وَتَعَامَلَتْ بِهِ الصَّحَابَةُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ ثُمَّ الْمَدْفُوعُ إِلَى الْمُضَارِبِ اَمَانَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ لِأَنَّهُ قَبَضَهُ بِأَمْرِ مَالِكِهِ لَا عَلَى وَجْهِ الْبَدَلِ وَالْوَثِيقَةِ وَهُوَ وَكِيلٌ فِيهِ. لأَنَّهُ يَتَصَرَّفُ فِيهِ بِأَمْرِ مَالِكِهِ وَإِذَا رَبِحَ فَهُوَ شَرِيكَ فِيهِ لِتَمَلْكِهِ جُزْءاً مِنَ الْمَالِ بِعَمَلِهِ فَإِذَا فَسَدَتِ ظَهَرَتِ الْإِجَارَةُ حَتَّى اسْتَوجَبَ الْعَامِلُ أَجْرَ مِثْلِهِ وَإِذَا خَالَفَ كَانَ عَاصِبًا لِوُجُودِ التَّعْدِي مِنْهُ عَلَى مَالِ غَيْرِهِ
Mudarabah is derived from darb (striking/going) on the earth. It is so named because the mudarib becomes entitled to profit through his effort and work. It is legislated due to the need for it, for people are between the wealthy in property who are ignorant of its management and the skillful in management who are empty-handed. So the need arose to legislate this type of transaction to organize the interests of the rich and the intelligent, the poor and the rich. The Prophet (peace be upon him) was sent while people were practicing it, and he confirmed them in it, and the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) practiced it. Then the capital given to the mudarib is an amanah (trust) in his hand because he took possession by the owner's command, not by way of exchange or security. He is an agent (wakil) in it because he acts in it by the owner's command. When he earns profit, he becomes a partner (sharik) in it because he becomes owner of a part of the property through his work. If it becomes invalid (fasid), the contract of hire becomes apparent, so the worker is entitled to the wage of his like (ujr al-mithl). And if he violates, he is a usurper (ghasib) due to his transgression on another's property.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explains the nature and ruling of mudarabah. It begins with the linguistic derivation: mudarabah comes from darb fi al-ard, meaning traveling on earth for trade, because the mudarib (worker) earns profit through his effort. The term mudarabah is used because the mudarib often travels to earn profit. In the Hijaz, it is called muqaradah or qirad. The legal ruling is that it is permissible (mashru'ah) due to societal need: some people have capital but lack business skills, while others have skills but no capital. Mudarabah allows both to benefit. The legitimacy is also established by the Prophet's (peace be upon him) approval (taqrir) of such transactions that occurred during his time, and by the continuous practice of the Companions (ra). The passage then describes the legal nature of the capital in the mudarib's hands in three capacities: 1) Amanah (trust) – before any action, the capital is a trust; if lost without negligence, no guarantee. 2) Wakil (agent) – the mudarib acts on behalf of the owner. 3) Sharik (partner) – once profit is earned, he becomes a partner in that profit. If the mudarabah becomes fasid (invalid) due to some defect, then the transaction is treated as an ijarah (hire), and the mudarib is entitled to the market wage for his work, regardless of profit. If the mudarib violates the owner's instructions, he becomes a ghasib (usurper) and must guarantee the capital. Regarding the last point, there is a dispute: Imams al-Shafi'i and Ahmad (in one narration) agree that the violator is a guarantor, while a report from Ali (ra), Hasan al-Basri, and al-Zuhri holds that the partner in profit is not a guarantor. However, the majority view, and the relied-upon position, is that he is a guarantor.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudārabah): A contract of partnership in profit where capital is from one party and work from the other.
مضارب (mudārib): The party providing the work (manager/worker) in a mudarabah contract.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The capital provider/owner of the money in a mudarabah.
أمانة (amānah): Trust; the capital in the mudarib's hand is a trust, meaning no guarantee for loss without negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a valid mudarabah, what is the legal status of the capital in the hands of the mudarib before any profit is earned?
A) Amanah (trust)
B) Qard (loan)
C) Wakalah (agency)
D) Shirkah (partnership)

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is a permissible trust-based partnership in profit; violation nullifies trust and triggers guarantee.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
beginner

Formal Definition of Mudarabah and Its Conditions
Defining mudarabah and its profit-sharing condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mudarabah and distinguish it from bida'ah and qard.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is a partnership in profit where capital and labor combine; if profit is unshared, it is not mudarabah.

The passage from al-Hidayah provides a tight definition of mudarabah (commenda) as a contract that establishes a partnership in profit. It emphasizes that profit must be shared between the capital provider and the worker, clarifying what does and does not constitute a valid mudarabah arrangement. Understanding this definition is essential for distinguishing mudarabah from similar contracts.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definition
Identify the key components: the contract (ʿaqd) leads to partnership (shirkah), with capital (māl) from one side and work (ʿamal) from the other. The purpose is partnership in profit (shirkah fī al-ribḥ).
Focus on the phrase 'الشَّرُكَةُ فِي الرِّبْحِ' – partnership in profit.
2
Extract the profit-sharing condition
The text states that mudarabah does not exist without this sharing ('لَا مُضَارَبَةَ بِدُونِهَا'). It then contrasts two extreme cases: if all profit is for the capital owner, it is bida'ah; if all is for the worker, it is qard.
The condition is that profit cannot be wholly allocated to one party.
3
Apply the distinction
Test scenarios: (1) profit shared → mudarabah; (2) all profit to capital owner → bida'ah; (3) all profit to worker → qard. Recognize that only with shared profit does the contract qualify as mudarabah.
This distinction is crucial for correct contract classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ الْمُضَارَبَةُ عَقْدٌ يَقَعُ عَلَى الشَّرُكَةِ بِمَالٍ مِنْ اَحَدِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ وَمُرَادُه الشَّرْكَةُ فِي الرِّبْحِ وَهُوَ يُسْتَحَقُ بِالْمَالِ مِنْ اَحَدِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ وَالْعَمَلُ مِنَ الْجَانِبِ الْآخِرِ وَلَا مُضَارَبَةَ بِدُونِهَا أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الرِّبْحَ لَوْ شَرَطَ كُلَّهُ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ كَانَ بِضَاعَة وَلَوْ شَرَطَ جَمِيْعُهُ لِلْمُصَارِبِ كَانَ قَرْضًا.
He said: Mudarabah is a contract that falls on partnership with capital from one of the two parties. Its meaning is partnership in profit, and profit is earned through the capital from one party and the work from the other. There is no mudarabah without this. Do you not see that if all the profit is stipulated for the capital owner, it is a bida'ah (commenda), and if all of it is stipulated for the mudarib, it is a loan (qard).
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage provides the formal legal definition of mudarabah from the text of al-Hidayah. It states that mudarabah is a contract (ʿaqd) that leads to partnership (shirkah) between two parties. One party provides capital (mal) from one side, and the other provides work (ʿamal) from the other side. The goal is partnership in profit: profit is earned through the combination of capital and labor. The definition excludes arrangements where all profit goes to one party. If all profit is given to the capital owner, the contract is called bida'ah (commenda), which is a type of gratuitous agency where the agent works without any share in profit (or for a fixed wage if agreed). If all profit is given to the worker, it is a qard (loan) because the capital owner is essentially lending his money without any return, and the worker keeps all earnings. This distinction is crucial to differentiate mudarabah from other similar contracts. The essence of mudarabah is the shared profit between the capital provider and the worker.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudārabah): A contract for partnership in profit where capital is from one party and work from the other.
بضاعة (biḍāʿah): A commenda where the capital owner gives money to an agent to trade, but all profit belongs to the owner; the agent works voluntarily or for a fixed wage.
قرض (qarḍ): A loan contract where the borrower receives money and is obligated to repay the principal; any profit from using the money belongs to the borrower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition, if the capital owner stipulates that all profit goes to him, what is the contract called?
A) Mudarabah
B) Bida'ah
C) Qard
D) Shirkah

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah requires profit to be shared; if profit is wholly allocated to one party, the contract is either bida'ah or qard, not mudarabah.

Valid Capital in Mudarabah: Goods and Debt
Explaining conditions of valid capital in mudarabah with three scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of capital validity in mudarabah and identify why the third scenario is disputed among Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Mudarabah capital must be valid for partnership; debt owed by the mudarib triggers an intra-Hanafi dispute on agency validity.

In this passage, we examine what constitutes valid capital for a mudarabah contract. The text presents three scenarios: mudarabah with goods (sold first), with a third-party debt, and with a debt owed by the mudarib himself. The first two are valid by consensus, but the third reveals an important intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding agency and the nature of the capital.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three capital scenarios
Read the passage and list each scenario: (1) goods given with instruction to sell and then use proceeds, (2) instruction to collect a debt owed by a third party and then work with it, (3) instruction to work with a debt that the mudarib himself owes.
The first two are ruled valid; the third is disputed.
2
Understand the reasoning for validity of scenarios 1 and 2
Note that in scenario 1, the mudarabah is added to a valid agency (tawkeel) and hiring (ijarah), which together form a valid mudarabah. Scenario 2 is analogized to scenario 1.
The key concept is that the combination of agency and hire is valid.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on scenario 3
Determine Abu Hanifa's objection: the agency (tawkeel) to collect from oneself is invalid, as established in sales. Then examine the companions' view: they see it as eventually becoming a mudarabah with goods when the mudarib purchases goods.
This is a legitimate difference based on the nature of the initial capital.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the arrangement is invalid from the start. Under the companions, it becomes valid and transforms into a mudarabah with goods once the mudarib buys something for the owner.
Later fatwa practice often adopts the companions' view for ease of transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا تَصِحُ إِلَّا بِالْمَالِ الَّذِي تَصِحُ بهِ الشَّرْكَةُ وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ بَيَانُهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَلَوْ دَفَعَ إِلَيْهِ عَرْضًا وَقَالَ بِعَه وَاعْمَل مُضَارَبَةٌ فِي ثَمَنِهِ جَازَ لِأَنَّهُ يَقْبَلُ الْإِضَافَةَ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ تَوْكِيْلٌ وَإِجَارَةً فَلَا مَانِعَ مِنَ الصَّحَّةِ وَكَذَا إِذَا قَالَ لَهُ اِقْبِضُ مَا لِي عَلَى فُلَانِ وَاعْمَل بِهِ مُضَارَبَةٌ جَازَ لِمَا قُلْنَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ اعْمَل بِالدَّيْنِ الَّذِي فِى ذِمَّتِكَ حَيْثُ لَا يَصِحُ الْمُضَارَبَةُ لِاَنَّ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لَا يَصِحُ هَذَا التَّوْكِيلُ عَلَى مَامَرَّ فِي الْبُيُوعِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَصِحُ لَكِنَّ يَقَعُ الْمِلْكُ فِي الْمُشْتَرَىٰ للْآمِرِ فَتَصِيرُ مُضَارَبَةٌ بِالْعَرْضِ.
He said: It is only valid with capital that is valid for partnership, and its explanation has preceded. If he gives him goods and says, 'Sell them and work as a mudarabah with their price,' it is permissible because it accepts the addition [of the mudarabah contract] from the perspective that it is an agency and a hiring, so there is no obstacle to validity. Similarly, if he says to him, 'Collect what is owed to me from so-and-so and work with it as a mudarabah,' it is permissible for what we said. Contrary to if he says, 'Work with the debt that is in your liability,' for it is not valid mudarabah because according to Abu Hanifa, such an agency is not valid as passed in the chapter of sales, and according to the two companions it is valid, but ownership of the purchased commodity falls for the orderer, so it becomes a mudarabah with goods.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the capital used in a mudarabah contract. It first reiterates that the capital must be of a type that can be used in a valid partnership (shirkah), which typically means currency (gold or silver) or something that can be valued and possessed. The explanation of this condition has been given earlier in the text. The passage then addresses three scenarios: 1) If the capital owner gives goods ('ard, commodities) to the mudarib and says, 'Sell them and then work with the proceeds as a mudarabah,' it is permissible. The reason is that the instruction to sell is an agency (tawkil), and the agreement to work for a share of profit is a form of hire (ijarah) in the sense of jua'l (reward for work). Since the combination of agency and hire is valid, the mudarabah is valid. 2) If the owner says to the mudarib, 'Collect the debt that is owed to me from so-and-so, and then work with it as a mudarabah,' it is also valid because it is similar to the previous case. 3) If the owner says, 'Work with the debt that you owe me' (i.e., the mudarib himself is in debt to the owner), then according to Abu Hanifa, the mudarabah is not valid. His reasoning is that such an agency (tawkeel to collect from oneself) is not valid, as established in the chapter of sales. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), it is valid. They argue that the mudarib, when he works, will buy goods for the owner, and ownership of those goods will be for the owner, effectively making it a mudarabah with goods. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The relied-upon position in later Hanafi practice is often the view of the two companions, as it facilitates transactions.

Key Terms
عرض ('araḍ): Goods, commodities (other than currency), such as merchandise.
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; the contract of mudarabah is a type of partnership in profit.
وكيل (wakīl): Agent; the mudarib acts as an agent for the capital owner in the mudarabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is mudarabah invalid when the capital is a debt owed by the mudarib to the capital owner?
A) Because the mudarib cannot be both debtor and agent
B) Because the debt is not a tangible asset
C) Because profit cannot be shared from debt
D) Because the owner does not have possession

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah capital must be capable of partnership; a debt owed by the mudarib creates an intra-Hanafi dispute, but the relied-upon view considers it valid by transforming into goods.

Legitimacy of Mudarabah: Proof from Need and Prophetic Practice
Establishing the legal basis of Mudarabah through need and precedent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two proofs for the legitimacy of Mudarabah in the Hanafi school and explain how each proof establishes the ruling.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is legislated through public need and prophetic tacit approval—two distinct proofs.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary establishes that Mudarabah is a valid contract. The commentator presents two arguments: a rational need-based justification and a textual proof from prophetic practice. Understanding this dual proof structure is essential for appreciating how Hanafi scholars derive rulings for financial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first proof: rational need
The passage notes that some people have capital but cannot trade, while others are skilled traders but lack capital. Mudarabah fulfills the needs of both, making it necessary. This is a rational (ma'qul) basis for legislation.
This proof is based on maslahah (public interest) and darurah (necessity).
2
Identify the second proof: prophetic tacit approval
The passage states that after the Prophet's ﷺ mission, people continued practicing Mudarabah and the Prophet did not forbid it. This constitutes a Sunnah Taqririyyah (tacit approval), a binding proof in Hanafi usul.
Taqrir is a type of sunnah where the Prophet's silence indicates approval.
3
Recognize the companion consensus
Many prominent Companions (Umar, Ibn Umar, etc.) practiced Mudarabah, and no one objected. This strengthens the proof, implying a form of ijma (consensus).
Companion practice without rejection is considered a strong indicator in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Synthesize the proofs and ruling
Combining the rational need and the prophetic taqrir, the Hanafi school concludes that Mudarabah is permissible (ja'iz) and recommended due to social benefit.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) but with a recommendation (mandub) because it helps fulfill communal needs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح... قوله وهى مشروعة مضاربت کا جواز اس لئے ہے کہ لوگوں کو اس کی ضرورت بھی ہے۔ کیونکہ بعض لوگ مالدار ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن خود کاروبار نہیں کر سکتے اور بعض اچھے خاصے بیوپاری ہوتے ہیں لیکن مال سے کورے ہوتے ہیں۔ پس عقد مضاربت کی مشروعیت ضروری ہے۔ تا کہ غنی اور فقیر سب کی ضروریات پوری ہو سکیں۔
قوله وبعث النبي ... الخ ۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کی بعثت کے بعد بھی لوگ یہ معاملہ کرتے رہے۔ اور آپ نے منع نہیں فرمایا۔ نیز حضرت عمرؓ، ابن عمر، ابو موسیٰ اشعری، ابن مسعود، عباس بن عبدالمطلب، حکیم بن حزام، جابر بن عبد اللہ و دیگر صحابہ بھی اس پر عمل پیرا ہیں اور کسی نے اس کا انکار نہیں کیا۔
Commentary: He said, 'And it is legislated.' The permissibility of Mudarabah is because people have need of it. For some people are wealthy but cannot do business themselves, and some are good merchants but lack capital. So the legislation of the contract of Mudarabah is necessary, so that the needs of both the rich and the poor may be fulfilled. He said, 'And the sending of the Prophet...' etc. Also because after the Prophet's ﷺ mission, people continued this practice, and he did not forbid it. Also Umar, Ibn Umar, Abu Musa al-Ashari, Ibn Mas'ud, Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib, Hakim ibn Hizam, Jabir ibn Abdullah, and other Companions practiced it, and no one rejected it.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Hidayah's statement that Mudarabah is legislated. It opens by stating the rationale: there is a social need for Mudarabah because some have capital but no business skill, while others have skill but no capital. This mutual need makes the contract beneficial. The proof (dalil) is twofold: first, the tacit approval of the Prophet ﷺ — people engaged in Mudarabah after his mission and he did not prohibit it, which constitutes a Sunnah Taqririyyah (tacit approval). Second, the practice of many prominent Companions and the absence of any objection, which indicates a form of Ijma (consensus). Thus, the ruling is that Mudarabah is a valid and recommended contract.

Key Terms
مضاربت (mudarabah): A contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared as agreed.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The capital provider in a mudarabah contract, also known as the investor.
مضارب (mudarib): The worker/manager in a mudarabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It was practiced by the Sahaba only.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is a legitimate contract proven by public need and the Prophet's tacit approval, making it a recommended form of partnership in the Hanafi school.

The Four Legal Statuses of the Mudarib
Explains the changing legal status of the mudarib during the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four legal statuses of the mudarib (amin, wakeel, shareek, ajir) and state the condition that triggers each status.

Core Idea
The mudarib's legal status shifts with his actions: trustee before work, agent during work, partner after profit, hireling in an invalid contract.

In the Hanafi school, the mudarib (entrepreneur in a mudarabah partnership) does not have a single legal capacity; his status evolves as the contract progresses. Understanding these statuses is essential for determining liability, profit entitlement, and the consequences of a defective contract. This passage from Al-Hidayah clearly delineates the four phases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time phases
The passage mentions four distinct moments: before any action, after starting work, after earning profit, and when the contract becomes fasid.
These phases are sequential in a valid contract, plus the fasid scenario as an exception.
2
Name the legal status at each phase
For each phase, the mudarib is given a specific legal classification: amin, wakeel, shareek, or ajir.
Memorize these terms: أمين, وكيل, شريك, أجير.
3
Note the legal consequence for each status
For each status, the passage states the mudarib's liability or entitlement: no liability (amin), liability passes to rabb al-mal (wakeel), profit share (shareek), fair wages (ajir).
Focus on who bears loss and what the mudarib receives.
4
Contrast the fasid scenario
The last status (ajir) applies only when the mudarabah is fasid. Compare it with the valid statuses.
In fasid, the mudarib is not a partner; he is merely a hired worker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ثم المدفوع .... مضارب جو مال لیتا ہے اس میں وہ قبل از تصرف امین ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ مالک کی اجازت سے بلا مبادلہ و وثیقہ مال پر قابض ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر مال ہلاک ہو جائے تو مضارب پر تاوان نہیں۔ اور عمل کرنے کے بعد وکیل ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ رب المال کے حکم سے تصرف کرتا ہے۔ پس جو ذمہ داری اس کو لاحق ہوگی وہ رب المال کو بھی لاحق ہوگی۔ اور نفع حاصل ہونے کے بعد شریک ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے عمل کے ذریعہ مال کا مالک ہو چکا۔ اور جب کسی وجہ سے مضاربت فاسد ہو جائے تو اجیر کے درجہ میں ہوتا ہے کہ اس کو اس کی محنت کی مزدوری ملتی ہے خواہ تجارت میں نفع ہو یا نہ ہو۔
He said, 'Then the money given...'. The mudarib, in the money he takes, before any action, he is an amin (trustee) because he takes possession of the property with the owner's permission without exchange or security. So if the property is destroyed, the mudarib is not liable. After he begins work, he becomes a wakeel (agent) because he acts by the order of the capital owner, and any liability that befalls him also falls upon the capital owner. After profit is earned, he becomes a shareek (partner) because through his work he has become owner of a portion of the property. And when the mudarabah becomes fasid (defective) for some reason, he becomes like an ajir (hireling), entitled to wages for his work, whether the trade yields profit or not.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage explains the three distinct legal statuses a mudarib assumes during the course of a valid mudarabah contract. Before initiating any trade, he is an amin (trustee) holding the capital as a trust, not liable for losses unless negligent. Once he begins trading, he becomes a wakeel (agent) of the capital owner, so that all contractual effects bind the capital owner. When profit is realized, he becomes a shareek (partner) with ownership of his agreed share of profit. If the mudarabah becomes fasid (e.g., due to an invalid condition), then the mudarib is treated as an ajir (hireling) and receives fair wages for his labor, regardless of profit. This demonstrates the Hanafi approach of analyzing contractual relationships through different legal capacities.

Key Terms
امین (amin): A trustee who holds property without liability for loss unless negligent; the mudarib is an amin before starting work.
وکیل (wakeel): Agent acting on behalf of the capital owner; the mudarib becomes wakeel when he starts trading.
اجیر (ajir): A hireling entitled to wages; the mudarib in a fasid contract is like an ajir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal status of the mudarib before he begins any trade?
A) Wakeel
B) Ajir
C) Shareek
D) Amin

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's legal capacity evolves with each phase of the contract, reflecting the Hanafi precision in defining rights and liabilities.

The Liability of a Violating Mudarib: Majority vs. Minority View
Dispute over mudarib liability upon violation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mudarib liability upon violation, identify the opposing view, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
A mudarib who violates instructions becomes a ghasib and is liable for losses.

This lesson examines a classical fiqh dispute: when a mudarib oversteps the capital owner's explicit instructions, does he become personally liable for any loss? The Hanafi school, joined by Shafi‘i and Ahmad, answers yes, while a minority led by Hasan al-Basri and Imam Zuhri disagrees. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the boundaries of trust and liability in mudarabah contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the Hanafi position
Identify the key facts: mudarib acts contrary to the capital owner's order (e.g., buys a prohibited item). The Hanafi ruling: the mudarib becomes a ghasib (usurper) and is liable (daman) because of ta‘addi (transgression).
The ruling applies only if the mudarib knew of the restriction and deliberately violated it.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Minority scholars (Hasan al-Basri, Zuhri, and a riwayah from Ali) hold that the mudarib is not liable. Their proof: the mudarib is a partner in profit, and partnership implies sharing both gain and loss, so liability does not attach.
The opposing view relies on a narration from Ali ibn Abi Talib.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that ta‘addi terminates the trust element. Once the mudarib disobeys, he is no longer acting as a partner but as a trespasser; hence the partnership rationale ceases, and liability arises.
The key conceptual shift is from amin (trustee) to ghasib (usurper).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the property is lost after violation, the Hanafi holds the mudarib personally responsible to compensate; the minority view would not hold him liable.
This affects whether the capital owner bears the loss or the mudarib replaces it.
5
Note the tarjih (relied-upon position)
The Hanafi position, supported by the majority of scholars (including Shafi‘i and Ahmad in one narration), is the mufta bihi. The cautionary principle protects the capital owner's property.
This tarjih is confirmed in the Hanafi works like Al-Hidayah and Radd al-Muhtar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وہہ۔ قال الشافعي و احمد في رواية ..... اور اگر مضارب نے رب المال کے حکم کے خلاف کیا مثلا ایسی چیز کی خرید و فروخت کی جس سے رب المال نے منع کر دیا تھا تو وہ غاصب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ غیر کے مال میں تعدی پائی گئی۔ لہذا مضارب پر ضمان لازم ہوگا۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ اور اکثر اہل علم اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ حضرت علی سے مروی ہے کہ ربح کے شریک پر ضمان نہ ہو گا۔ حسن بصری اور امام زہری اسی کے قائل ہیں۔
A remark. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad (in one narration) said: If the mudarib acts contrary to the capital owner's order, e.g., buys or sells something the owner prohibited, then he becomes a usurper (ghasib) because there is transgression on another's property, and therefore the mudarib becomes liable. The three Imams and most scholars hold this view. It is narrated from Ali that the partner in profit is not liable. Hasan al-Basri and Imam Zuhri hold this view.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents a legal dispute. When a mudarib violates explicit instructions from the capital owner (e.g., trading in a prohibited commodity), the majority of scholars including the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad (in one narration) rule that the mudarib becomes a ghasib (usurper) and must compensate for any loss because he overstepped his authority and committed transgression. They base this on the principle that acting without permission on another's property creates liability. A minority view, attributed to Ali ibn Abi Talib, Hasan al-Basri, and Imam Zuhri, holds that the mudarib is not liable since he is a partner in profit. The Hanafi position, aligned with the majority, is that the mudarib's violation transforms his status from trustee to guarantor; this is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
غاصب (ghasib): One who takes or uses property without right, becoming liable for compensation.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression beyond authorized limits of action.
امین (amin): Trustee; one who holds property with permission and is not liable for accidental loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a mudarib disobeys the capital owner's instructions?
A) He remains a trustee without liability.
B) He becomes a ghasib and is liable for losses.
C) He becomes a partner and shares losses.
D) The contract becomes void automatically.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib who violates the capital owner's instructions becomes a ghasib and must compensate any resulting loss, a position that protects the capital owner and is adopted by the majority of scholars.

Definition and Conditions of Mudarabah
Defining Mudarabah and specifying the type of capital required

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Mudarabah, identify its two essential conditions, and distinguish it from bida'ah and qard.

Core Idea
Mudarabah requires profit sharing: without it, the contract is bida'ah or qard.

This lesson presents the classical Hanafi definition of Mudarabah. It is a contract of partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, and profit is shared. The passage also clarifies what happens if profit is not shared. Understanding this definition is essential to avoid confusing Mudarabah with other contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their contributions
Recognize that Mudarabah involves two parties: one provides capital (rabb al-mal) and the other provides labor (mudarib). The capital owner does not work, and the worker does not contribute capital.
2
Understand the essential element: partnership in profit
The core of Mudarabah is shirkah fi al-ribh (partnership in profit). The profit is shared according to a pre-agreed ratio. This sharing is what distinguishes Mudarabah from other contracts.
If no profit sharing is stipulated, the contract is not Mudarabah.
3
Distinguish by profit allocation
The passage gives two scenarios: if all profit goes to the capital owner, it becomes bida'ah (a mere bailment without profit for the worker); if all profit goes to the worker, it becomes qard (loan) because the worker effectively owns the capital and bears all risk.
These contrasts help clarify the boundaries of Mudarabah.
4
Recognize the capital condition
Mudarabah is valid only with capital that is suitable for a valid partnership (shirkah). According to the Hanafi school, this typically means gold and silver currency (dirhams and dinars), though there are details about other types.
This condition ensures that the capital is fungible and can be shared in profit/loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ الْمُضَارَبَةُ عَقْدٌ يَقَعُ عَلَى الشَّرُكَةِ بِمَالٍ مِنْ اَحَدِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ وَمُرَادُه الشَّرْكَةُ فِي الرِّبْحِ وَهُوَ يُسْتَحَقُ بِالْمَالِ مِنْ اَحَدِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ وَالْعَمَلُ مِنَ الْجَانِبِ الْآخِرِ وَلَا مُضَارَبَةَ بِدُونِهَا أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الرِّبْحَ لَوْ شَرَطَ كُلَّهُ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ كَانَ بِضَاعَة وَلَوْ شَرَطَ جَمِيْعُهُ لِلْمُصَارِبِ كَانَ قَرْضًا. قَالَ وَلَا تَصِحُ إِلَّا بِالْمَالِ الَّذِي تَصِحُ بهِ الشَّرْكَةُ وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ بَيَانُهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ.
ترجمہ مضاربت ایسا عقد ہے جو مال کے ساتھ شرکت پر واقع ہوتا ہے اور مراد شرکت ربح میں ہے اور وہ مال کے ذریعہ مستحق ہوتا ہے اور دوسری جانب سے کام ہو۔ اس شرکت کے بغیر مضاربت نہیں ہوتی۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر نفع کا سب کچھ رب المال کے لئے شرط ہو تو یہ بضاعت ہو جائے گا اور اگر تمام نفع مضارب کے لئے شرط ہو تو قرض ہو جائے گا۔ اور مضاربت صحیح نہیں ہوتی مگر اسی مال سے جس سے شرکت صحیح ہوتی ہے۔ جس کا بیان پہلے گزر چکا۔
He said: Mudarabah is a contract that occurs for partnership with capital from one side, its purpose being partnership in profit. It is earned through capital from one side and labor from the other side. There is no Mudarabah without it. Do you not see that if all profit is stipulated for the capital owner, it becomes bida'ah; and if all is stipulated for the mudarib, it becomes qard. He said: It is not valid except with the same type of capital as that with which partnership is valid, and its explanation has preceded.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage gives the canonical definition of Mudarabah. It is a contract of partnership (shirkah) where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, and the profit is shared between them as agreed. The essential element (rukn) is the partnership in profit. If the profit is entirely assigned to the capital owner, the contract is not Mudarabah but bida'ah (a gratuitous bailment for trading). If profit is entirely for the worker, it is a qard (loan) because the worker becomes owner of the whole profit. The second condition is that the capital must be of a type that can form the basis of a valid partnership (shirkah), i.e., generally gold and silver dirhams and dinars according to the majority, though there is detail in other texts. This definition highlights the mutual sharing nature of Mudarabah.

Key Terms
بضاعت (bida'ah): A bailment where capital owner entrusts goods to another for trade without sharing profit; here the worker gets no profit.
قرض (qard): A loan; here it means the worker becomes owner of the capital and bears all profit and loss.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership in profit; the essential element of Mudarabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The contract is still Mudarabah but invalid.
B) It becomes a bida'ah.
C) It becomes a qard.
D) The contract is void and the worker gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is partnership in profit: without profit sharing, it is not Mudarabah.

Mudarabah with Commodities: The Legal Trick (Hila) of Prior Sale
Ruling with proof for a legal trick in Mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi legal trick for conducting Mudarabah with commodities and identify the role of idafah (deferment) in its validity.

Core Idea
Mudarabah with commodities is invalid directly, but valid via selling first and using the price — because Mudarabah accepts idafah as a mix of agency and hire.

In the Hanafi school, Mudarabah capital must be liquid currency (dirhams/dinars). But what if someone only has commodities? Al-Hidayah provides a practical legal stratagem (hila): the capital owner gives the commodity to the mudarib to sell, and then the proceeds become capital for a new Mudarabah. This works because Mudarabah is a hybrid of agency (wakalah) and hire (ijarah), both of which can be deferred (idafah) to a future time. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and an important intra-Hanafi disagreement when the debt is owed by the mudarib himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recall that the Hanafi school requires Mudarabah capital to be in gold or silver currency. Commodities are not acceptable as capital directly, creating a problem for someone who only possesses goods.
This is established earlier in Hidayah; the current passage provides a solution.
2
State the legal trick (hila)
The capital owner gives the commodity to the mudarib with instructions: 'Sell this, and then conduct Mudarabah with the proceeds.' The sale is a separate transaction; the Mudarabah begins after the sale with liquid capital.
The trick avoids the prohibition by making the actual Mudarabah capital liquid.
3
Explain the proof: idafah (deferment)
Mudarabah is analyzed as a combination of wakalah (agency) and ijarah (hire). Both of these contracts can be deferred (idafah) to a future date. Therefore, the Mudarabah can start after the sale event, making it valid.
Unlike sales, which cannot be deferred, wakalah and ijarah accept idafah by consensus in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on debt from mudarib
If the capital owner says: 'Work with the debt that you owe me,' Abu Hanifa deems it invalid because the agency to collect from oneself is not valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it valid, but then ownership of purchased goods vests in the capital owner, effectively making it a Mudarabah with a commodity — again requiring the same trick.
This shows how the school maintains internal consistency even when there is disagreement.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
A farmer with wheat wants a Mudarabah. He gives wheat to a trader: 'Sell this wheat and use the money as Mudarabah capital.' The trader sells, gets cash, then invests as Mudarabah. This is valid. Similarly, if someone is owed a debt by a third party, he can say: 'Collect my debt and use it as Mudarabah capital.' This too is valid.
The trick is widely accepted and mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح: مضاربت بالاسباب کی صحت کا حیلہ قوله ولو دفع إليه عرضا .... الخ ۔ یہ بات اوپر معلوم ہو چکی کہ شیخین کے نزدیک دراہم دنانیر کے علاوہ اسباب وغیرہ میں مضاربت صحیح نہیں۔ اس کا مطلب یہی ہوا کہ اگر کسی کے پاس صرف اسباب ہو اور وہ مضاربت کرنا چاہے تو اس کی کوئی صورت نہیں ۔ صاحب ہدایہ اس کے جواز کا حیلہ ذکر کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی اسباب ہی سے مضاربت کرنا چاہے تو اس کے جواز کی صورت یہ ہے کہ کسی کو اسباب دے کر یہ کہے کہ اس کو فروخت کر کے جو دام حاصل ہوں ان سے مضاربت کر ۔ اس طرح مضاربت صحیح ہو جائے گی۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ مضاربت توکیل و اجارہ ہونے کی حیثیت سے آئندہ زمانہ کی طرف اضافت کو قبول کرتی ہے۔
If he gave him a commodity and said, 'Sell it and conduct Mudarabah with its price,' it is permissible because it accepts idafah (deferment) in that it is a combination of agency (wakalah) and hire (ijarah), so there is no obstacle to validity. Similarly if he said, 'Collect what is owed to me from so-and-so and conduct Mudarabah with it,' it is permissible for what we said. Unlike if he said, 'Work with the debt that is in your liability,' where Mudarabah is not valid, because according to Abu Hanifa this agency is not valid as passed in the Book of Sales, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is valid, but ownership of the purchased item vests in the orderer, so it becomes Mudarabah with a commodity. Commentary: The legal trick for the validity of Mudarabah with commodities: He said, 'If he gave him a commodity...' etc. It has been established above that according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) Mudarabah is not valid with commodities other than dirhams and dinars. This means that if someone only has commodities and wants to do Mudarabah, there is no way. The author of Hidayah mentions a legal trick for its validity: if one wants to do Mudarabah with commodities, the permissible method is to give the commodity to someone and say, 'Sell it and then do Mudarabah with the proceeds.' Thus Mudarabah becomes valid. The reason is that Mudarabah, being a combination of agency and hire, accepts idafah (deferment) to a future time.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical problem: according to the Hanafi school, the capital in Mudarabah must be dirhams and dinars (gold/silver currency), not commodities. So someone with only goods cannot directly enter a Mudarabah contract. The Hidayah provides a legal trick (hila): the capital owner gives the commodity to the mudarib not as capital but as a sale item, with instructions to sell it and then use the proceeds as capital for Mudarabah. This works because Mudarabah, being a contract that includes agency (wakalah) and hire (ijarah), can be deferred (idafah) to a future time. So the actual Mudarabah begins after the sale. The same principle applies to collecting a debt from a third party: the mudarib collects it and then uses it as capital. However, if the debt is owed by the mudarib himself, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa does not permit it because the agency to collect from oneself is invalid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad permit it, but then ownership of purchased goods vests in the capital owner, resulting in Mudarabah with a commodity (which is then subject to the same trick). This passage illustrates how later Hanafi jurists used hila to reconcile strict rules with practical needs.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible end while avoiding a legal obstacle.
اضافت (idafah): Deferment of a contract to a future time; here Mudarabah can be deferred because it includes wakalah and ijarah which allow idafah.
توکیل و اجارہ (tawkeel wa ijarah): Agency and hire; Mudarabah is considered a combination of these two contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates Mudarabah with commodities through the hila of prior sale, relying on the principle that Mudarabah accepts idafah (deferment) as it is a composite of wakalah and ijarah.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Definition of Mudarabah and Its Essential Elements
Defines mudarabah and its essential profit-sharing condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mudarabah and identify the condition that distinguishes it from similar contracts.

Core Idea
Profit must be shared in mudarabah; otherwise it is not a valid mudarabah contract.

This lesson examines the Hanafi definition of mudarabah (qirad). The text defines the essential elements and clarifies the crucial requirement of profit-sharing. Understanding this definition is key to distinguishing mudarabah from other contracts like bida'ah and qard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition components
Extract the three parts: capital provider, labor provider, and profit sharing.
These are the core elements that constitute mudarabah.
2
Recognize the essential condition
Note that profit sharing is the decisive element; without it, the contract is not mudarabah.
This is the key legal differentiator.
3
Analyze the two exceptions
Consider what happens if profit is not shared: if all profit goes to rabb al-mal, it becomes bida'ah; if all to mudarib, it becomes qard.
These exceptions are derived from the profit-sharing condition.
4
Apply the definition
Test a scenario: if all profit goes to one party, the contract changes from mudarabah to another type.
Application reinforces the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح قوله الْمُضَارَبَةِ عقد اصطلاح شرع میں مضاربت اس عقد کو کہتے ہیں۔ جس میں ایک کی جانب سے مال ہو اور دوسرے کی جانب سے عمل ہو اور نفع میں دونوں شریک ہوں۔ جس کی جانب سے مال ہو اس کو رب المال اور جس کی جانب سے عمل ہو اس کو مضارب اور جو مال دیا جائے اس کو مال مضاربت کہتے ہیں۔ شرکت مذکورہ کے بغیر مضاربت نہیں ہوتی۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر کل نفع کی شرط رب المال کے لئے ہو تو مضارب مستبضع ہوگا۔ یعنی عقد مضاربت نہ رہے گا بلکہ عقد بضاعت ہو جائے گا۔ اور مضارب رب المال کے حق میں محسن شمار ہوگا۔ اور اگر کل نفع مضارب کے لئے شرط ہو تو وہ مستعقرض ہو گا گویا اس نے رب المال سے مال بطور قرض لے لیا۔
Explanation of the saying: 'Al-Mudarabah is a contract.' In Shariah terminology, mudarabah is a contract in which capital comes from one side and labor from the other, and both share in the profit. The owner of capital is called rabb al-mal, the worker is called mudarib, and the capital given is called mal al-mudarabah. Mudarabah does not occur without the mentioned partnership. So much so that if all profit is stipulated for the rabb al-mal, the mudarib becomes mustabdi' (an agent for investment), meaning it is no longer a mudarabah contract but becomes a bida'ah contract, and the mudarib is considered a benefactor toward the rabb al-mal. And if all profit is stipulated for the mudarib, then he becomes mustaqrid (a borrower), as if he took the capital from the rabb al-mal as a loan.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement. It first defines the mudarabah contract, identifying the parties and the nature of the contract: one party provides capital (rabb al-mal), the other provides labor (mudarib), and profit is shared between them. It then clarifies that the essential element of mudarabah is the partnership in profit. If the entire profit is allocated to one party, the contract ceases to be mudarabah. If all profit goes to rabb al-mal, the mudarib becomes an agent for investment (mustabdi') under a bida'ah contract, and he is rewarded by God but not entitled to any profit. If all profit goes to mudarib, it becomes a loan (qard), and the mudarib is obliged to return the capital. Thus, mudarabah is only valid when profit is shared proportionally between the parties.

Key Terms
مضاربت (mudārabah): A contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared according to agreement.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The owner of the capital in a mudarabah contract.
مضارب (muḍārib): The worker or manager who invests the capital in a mudarabah contract.
بضاعت (biḍāʿah): A contract where the agent (mustabdi') invests without entitlement to profit, considered benevolent.
مستعقرض (mustaqriḍ): One who takes a loan; in the context, the mudarib is considered a borrower if all profit is his.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A valid mudarabah
B) A bida'ah contract
C) A loan (qard)
D) A void contract

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is only valid when profit is shared; otherwise it becomes bida'ah or qard.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Condition of Capital in Mudarabah
Explains valid capital types for mudarabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for valid capital in mudarabah and identify the intra-madhhab and cross-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Mudarabah capital must be currency; goods or measured items are invalid.

Mudarabah is a contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor. But not any property can serve as capital—the Hanafi school requires it to be a specific type of money. This passage explains exactly what qualifies, the internal difference among Hanafi imams, and how this compares to other schools. Understanding this condition is essential for anyone dealing with Islamic investment contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The passage discusses the condition (shart) for a valid mudarabah contract: the capital must be of a certain type. Determine what the act is and what is being conditioned.
The act is the mudarabah contract; the condition relates to the capital (ra's al-mal).
2
Locate the Hanafi position
Find the ruling of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and the view of Imam Muhammad. Note the difference: the two shaykhs require gold/silver coins (dirhams/dinars), while Imam Muhammad allows current coins (fulus ra'ij).
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the two shaykhs.
3
Trace the proof
The passage cites ijma (consensus) as the main proof, mentioning that al-Dhakhirah explicitly reports consensus. Understand the weight of ijma as a dalil in Hanafi usul.
Ijma is qat'i al-thubut; it gives certainty to the ruling.
4
Examine the cross-madhhab dispute
The passage contrasts the Hanafi view with Imam Malik (who allows commodities) and Ibn Abi Layla (who allows measured/weighed items). Understand the basis of their disagreement.
The Hanafi response: commodities and measured items cannot be divided proportionally for profit-sharing.
5
Determine the practical consequence
What happens if capital is given in a non-currency form? The mudarabah becomes invalid and defaults to a different contract (bida'ah or loan). This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

قوله ولا تصح الا بالمال ... الخ مضاربت اس مال سے صحیح ہوتی ہے جس سے شرکت صحیح ہے۔ اور وہ شیخین کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ راس المال در اہم یا دن نیر ہوں۔ امام محمد اور اشہب مالکی کے یہاں فلوس رائجہ سے بھی بیح ہے۔ ان کے ماسوا سے جائز نہیں۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں بلکہ ذخیرہ میں اس پر اجماع کی صراحت ہے۔ شیخ سغناقی نے لکھا ہے کہ عروض و اسباب ہمارے نزدیک راس المال ہونے کے قابل نہیں۔ برخلاف امام مالک کے۔ ایسے ہی کیلی اور وزنی اشیاء ہیں۔ برخلاف ابن ابی لیلی کے۔ لیکن بقول شیخ کا کی کتب مالکیہ میں عروض سے عدم جواز ہی معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ بلکہ جواہر مالکیہ میں تو یہاں تک ہے۔ انه لايجوز بالنقرة التي ليست مضروبة اذا كان التعامل بالمسكوك
The saying: 'And it is only valid with capital...' etc. Mudarabah is valid with the capital with which partnership (shirkah) is valid. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), that capital is dirhams or dinars. According to Imam Muhammad and Ashhab al-Maliki, it is also valid with current coins (fulus ra'ij). It is not valid with anything else. The three imams (Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad) also hold this view; rather, in al-Dhakhirah, there is explicit mention of consensus on this. Shaykh al-Sighnaqi wrote that commodities and goods (urud wa asbab) are not valid as capital in our school, contrary to Imam Malik. Similarly, measured and weighed items are not valid, contrary to Ibn Abi Layla. But according to Shaykh [?], in the Maliki books, non-currency is impermissible. Rather, in Jawahir al-Malikiyyah it is stated: 'It is not permissible with silver that is not minted if the dealings are with coins.'
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the condition of the capital in mudarabah. It states that mudarabah is only valid with the same type of property that is valid for the contract of partnership (shirkah). According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (the two shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the capital must be dirhams (silver coins) or dinars (gold coins), i.e., currency at the time. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Ashhab (a Maliki) permit mudarabah with current coins (fulus ra'ij, which were copper coins used for exchange). However, the relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs. The author also notes that there is a consensus of three imams (likely Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad) on this restriction, and al-Dhakhirah reports an explicit consensus. Then it mentions that commodities and goods are not valid as capital in the Hanafi school, contrary to Imam Malik. Similarly, measured and weighed items are not valid, contrary to Ibn Abi Layla. The passage also references Maliki sources that indicate even unminted silver is not permissible if the dealing is with minted coins. Thus, the Hanafi position is clear: mudarabah capital must be in the form of currency (gold, silver, or current coins according to some).

Key Terms
راس المال (ra’s al-māl): The capital provided by the rabb al-mal in a mudarabah contract.
عروض (ʿurūḍ): Commodities or goods that are not currency.
فلوس رائجہ (fulūs rā’ijah): Current coins, typically copper coins used as money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A car worth $10,000
B) 10,000 Saudi Riyals in currency
C) 100 liters of olive oil
D) 50 grams of gold in the form of jewelry

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah capital must be in the form of currency (dirhams/dinars or, per Imam Muhammad, fulus); using commodities or measured items invalidates the contract in the Hanafi school.

The Legal Stratagem (Hila) for Mudarabah with Commodities
Presents a legal stratagem for mudarabah with commodities, with objections and a preferred explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hila for mudarabah with commodities, explain the initial reasoning and its critique, and identify the preferred justification from al-Kafi.

Core Idea
For mudarabah with commodities, first sell them — the hila makes the contract valid by using the sale proceeds as capital.

This passage presents a practical hila from al-Hidayah for forming a mudarabah when the capital is only commodities. Normally, commodities are invalid as capital, but through agency to sell first, the proceeds become valid capital. The passage also critiques the original reasoning and offers a stronger justification from al-Kafi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Problem
Recognize that mudarabah with commodities is invalid because capital must be dirhams or dinars. This sets up the need for a hila.
The two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold this view.
2
Learn the Stratagem (Hila)
The hila: the capital owner gives goods to the mudarib as an agent to sell, then after sale uses the proceeds as mudarabah capital.
This is mentioned in al-Hidayah.
3
Examine the Initial Reasoning
The initial justification claims mudarabah comprises wakalah and ijarah, both allow future attachment, so mudarabah can be attached to the future sale.
This reasoning is from al-Hidayah's author.
4
Critique the Reasoning
Analyze the three objections: mudarabah does not include ijarah; the whole is not necessarily consistent with parts; wakalah and ijarah are not parts of mudarabah but rulings.
The commentator raises these to show the initial reasoning is weak.
5
Adopt the Preferred Explanation
From al-Kafi: the mudarabah is attached to the thaman (valid capital) and future attachment is allowed because mudarabah can be wakalah, wadi'ah, or ijarah.
This is the sounder basis for the hila.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لیکن یہ تعلیل کئی وجہ سے مخدوش ہے۔ اول تو اس لئے کہ یہاں مدعی صورت مذکورہ میں عقد مضاربت کا صحیح ہونا ہے اور مضاربت صحیحہ اجارہ پر مشتمل نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس کے منافی ہوتی ہے۔ دوم اسلئے کہ عدم مخالفت کل کا لزوم ممنوع ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بات قطعی طور پر معلوم ہے کہ گل بہت سے احکام میں اپنے اجزاخار جیہ عقلیہ کے خلاف ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ دیکھ لو کہ واحد اثنین کا جز ہے۔ حالانکہ اول فرد ہے نہ کہ زوج اور ثانی زوج ہے نہ کہ فرد ۔ علاوہ ازیں مضاربت و وکالت اور اجارہ میں بہت سے احکام کے اندر مخالفت محقق ہے مثال وکیل نہ مستحق ربح ہوتا ہے اور نہ اسمیں موکل کے ساتھ شریک ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ مضارب میں یہ دونوں باتیں ہوتی ہیں اسی طرح اجیر مستحق اجرت ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مستحق ریح اور مضارب اسکے برعکس ہے سوم اسلئے کہ وکالت اور اجارہ میں مضاربت کے جز ہونے کا احتمال ہی نہیں ہے۔ وکالت میں تو اس لئے کہ یہ با تفاق فقہاء احکام مضاربت میں سے ایک حکم ہے اور حکم شئی خارج از شئی اور اس پر مرتب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ رکن رہا اجارہ سودہ بھی بعض کے نزدیک احکام مضاربت میں سے ایک حکم ہے۔ پس تعلیل کی بہتر توضیح صاحب کافی نے کی ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں اس نے مضاربت کو اسپاپ کی طرف مضاف نہیں کیا بلکہ اس کے شمن کی طرف مضاف کیا ہے اور ثمن سے مضاربت کی صحت میں کوئی اشکال ہی نہیں۔ رہی اضافت الی استقبل سودہ اس لئے جائز ہے کہ مضاربت، وکالت یا ودیعت یا اجارہ ہے اور ان میں سے کوئی ایک بھی صحت اضافت سے مانع نہیں ہے۔
The legal stratagem for the validity of mudarabah with goods. The saying: 'And if he gives him goods...' etc. It has been known before that according to the two shaykhs, mudarabah is not valid with goods and other things besides dirhams and dinars. This means that if someone only has goods and wants to do mudarabah, there is no way for it. The author of al-Hidayah mentions a stratagem for its permissibility: if someone wants to do mudarabah with only goods, the way for its permissibility is that he gives goods to someone and says: 'Sell this, and then do mudarabah with the proceeds (thaman) you obtain.' In this way, the mudarabah will be valid. The reason is that mudarabah, being a combination of agency (wakalah) and hire (ijarah), can be attached to a future time. The explanation from the authors of al-Nihayah and al-'Inayah is that the mudarabah contract comprises wakalah and ijarah, and each of these accepts attachment to the future. Therefore, the contract that comprises both (i.e., mudarabah) will also be able to be attached, so that the whole is not contrary to its parts. The form of attaching agency to the future is that if someone says: 'I make you my agent tomorrow to sell this slave of mine,' then he becomes an agent for selling tomorrow and after, not before. And the form of attaching ijarah is that he says: 'I hire you to work tomorrow,' the ijarah will be concluded after tomorrow.

But this reasoning is objectionable for several reasons. First, because here the claim is that in the mentioned case the mudarabah contract is valid, and a valid mudarabah does not comprise ijarah; rather it is contrary to it. Second, the necessity of the whole not being contrary to its parts is not accepted, because it is definitively known that the whole is in many rulings contrary to its external intellectual parts. For example, one is a part of two, yet one is odd and not even, while two is even and not odd. Moreover, there is actual opposition between mudarabah and both wakalah and ijarah in many rulings. For example, the agent (wakil) is not entitled to profit nor is he a partner with the principal, whereas the mudarib has both these qualities. Similarly, the hired person (ajir) is entitled to wages, not profit, while the mudarib is the opposite. Third, there is no possibility that wakalah and ijarah are parts of mudarabah. As for wakalah, because it is, by consensus of jurists, one of the rulings of mudarabah, and a ruling is external to the thing and supervenes upon it, not a pillar. As for ijarah, it too is one of the rulings of mudarabah according to some. Therefore, the better explanation is given by the author of al-Kafi: that in the mentioned case, the mudarib did not attach mudarabah to the goods (asbab) but attached it to their price (thaman), and there is no problem in the validity of mudarabah with the price. As for attachment to the future, it is permissible because mudarabah is wakalah or wadi'ah or ijarah, and none of these prevent the validity of attachment.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) for making mudarabah valid when the capital is in the form of commodities (asbab), which are normally not acceptable as capital according to the two shaykhs. The stratagem is to first appoint the mudarib as an agent to sell the goods, and then with the sale proceeds (thaman), the mudarabah is formed. The author of al-Hidayah explains this based on the idea that mudarabah comprises agency and hire, and both can be attached to a future time. However, the commentator then raises objections to this reasoning, pointing out that valid mudarabah does not actually include ijarah, and that the whole is not necessarily consistent with its parts. He then presents a better explanation from Sahib al-Kafi: that the mudarabah is attached to the price (thaman) of the goods, not to the goods themselves, and since the price is valid capital, there is no issue. Additionally, attachment to the future is allowed because mudarabah can be considered wakalah, wadi'ah, or ijarah, all of which accept attachment. Thus, the hila is valid and practical.

Key Terms
حیلہ (ḥīlah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible result while complying with legal restrictions.
اضافت الی استقبل (iḍāfat ilā mustaqbal): Attaching a contract to a future time, so it takes effect later.
ثمن (thaman): The price or sale proceeds obtained from selling goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Avoid mudarabah altogether

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a hila for mudarabah with commodities by first selling them and then using the proceeds as capital.
