Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
6 min
The Musha' Requirement: Profit Must Be a Common Share
Explains the mushā' requirement and the ruling on fixing a profit share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the stipulation of a fixed profit amount invalidates a mudarabah and determine the resulting distribution of profit and wage.

Core Idea
Profit in mudarabah must be a common share (musha'); a fixed sum cuts the partnership and voids the contract.

In mudarabah (silent partnership), profit allocation is foundational. The Hanafi school insists that profit must be an undivided proportion, not a fixed number of dirhams. This lesson unpacks why this condition is essential and what happens if it is violated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states that profit must be shared as a common share (musha'an) between the rabb al-mal and mudarib.
Musha' means undivided and proportional.
2
Understand the rationale
A fixed sum cuts the partnership because it limits the mudarib's share to that amount, breaking the proportional sharing essential to the contract.
Partnership (shirkah) is necessary even in mudarabah.
3
Recognize the consequence
If a fixed profit is stipulated, the mudarabah becomes fasid (void).
Fasid means the contract is defective but can be corrected in some cases.
4
Determine profit distribution
All profit goes to the rabb al-mal because it is the growth of his property.
The mudarib does not share the profit; he is compensated separately.
5
Determine mudarib compensation
The mudarib is entitled to the wages of his like (ajr al-mithl) for his work.
This is market wages for similar work, not the stipulated amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ شَرَطَهَا أَنْ يَكُونَ الرِّبْحُ بَيْنَهُمَا مُشَاعَاً لَا يَسْتَحِقُ أَحَدَهُمَا دَرَاهِمُ مُسَمَاةِ مِنَ الرِّبْحِ لَانَّ شَرْطَ ذلِكَ يَقْطَعُ الشَّرْكَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا وَلَابُدَّ مِنْهَا كَمَا فِى عَقْدِ الشَّرُكَةِ قَالَ فَإِنْ شَرَطَ زِيَادَةَ عَشَرَةَ فَلَهُ أَجْرُ مِثْلِهِ لفَسَادِهِ فَلَعَلَّهُ لَا يَرْبَحْ إِلَّا هَذَا الْقَدْرَ فَيَقْطَعُ الشَّرْكَةُ فِي الرِّبْحِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ ابْتَغَى عَنْ مُنَافِعِهِ عِوَضًا وَلَمْ يَنَلْ لفَسَادِهِ وَالرِّبْحُ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّهُ نماءُ مِلْكِهِ وَهَذَا هُوَ الْحُكْمُ فِى كُلَّ مَوْضِعِ لَمْ يَصِحُ الْمُضَارَبَةُ وَلَا تُجَاوَزُ بِالْآخِرِ الْقَدْرِ الْمَشْرُوطِ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ خِلَافًا لِمُحَمَّدٌ كَمَا بَيَّنَا فِي الشَّرَكَةِ وَيَجِبُ الْأَجْرُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَرْبَحَ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ لِأَنَّ أَجْرَ الْأَخِيرِ يَجِبُ بِتَسْلِيمِ الْمَنَافِعِ أَوِ الْعَمَلِ وَقَدْ وَجَدَ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْمُضَارَبَةِ الصَّحِيحَةِ مَعَ أَنَّهَا فَوْقَهَا وَالْمَالُ فِى الْمُصَارَبَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونِ بِالْهَلَاكِ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالصَّحِيحَةِ وَلِأَنَّهُ عَيْنٌ مُسْتَاجَرَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ وَكُلُّ شَرْطٍ يُوجِبُ جِهَالَةً فِي الرِّبْحِ يُفْسِدُهُ لِاخْتِلَالِ مَقْصُودِهِ وَغَيْرَ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الشَّرُوطِ الْفَاسِدَةِ لَا يُفْسِدُهَا وَيَبْطُلُ الشَّرْطُ كَاشْتِرَاطِ الْوَضِيْعَةِ عَلَى الْمُصَارِبِ

ترجمہ شروط مضاربت میں ہے یہ ہے کہ نفع ان دونوں میں مشترک ہو کہ ان میں سے کوئی نفع سے معین در اہم کا مستحق نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ اس کی شرط کرنا قاطع شرکت ہے۔ حالانکہ شرکت ضروری ہے جیسا کہ عقد شرکت میں ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر شرط کی دیں دور ہم زائد کی تو مضارب کے لئے اجر مثل ہوگا فساد مضاربت کی وجہ سے کیونکہ ممکن ہے نفع اس قدر ہو تو نفع میں شرکت منقطع ہو جائے گی اور یہ اس لئے کہ مضارب نے اپنے نفع کا عوض چاہا اور وہ فساد عقد کی وجہ سے نہیں پایا۔ اور پورا نفع رب المال کا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کی ملک کا پھل ہے اور یہی حکم ہے ہر اس جگہ میں جہاں مضاربت صحیح نہ ہوئی ہو۔ اور اجر مثل مقدار مشروط سے نہیں بڑھے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بر خلاف امام محمد کے جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا ہے کتاب الشرکة میں۔ اور اجرت واجب ہوگی۔ اگر چہ نفع نہ کمایا ہو۔ مبسوط کی روایت میں۔ کیونکہ اجیر کی اجرت واجب ہو جاتی ہے۔ منافع یا کام سپر د کر نے سے اور یہ پایا گیا اور امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی بقیاس مضاربت صحیحہ کے باوجود یکہ بیچ فاسدہ سے بڑھ کر ہے اور مضاربت فاسدہ میں مال مضمون نہیں ہوتا ہلاک ہونے سے بقیاس مضاربت صحیح کے اور اس لئے کہ مال تو اس کے قبضہ میں اجارہ پر لی ہوئی چیز ہے۔ اور ہر وہ
He said: One of its conditions is that profit be shared (musha'an) between them, and neither of them deserves specified dirhams from the profit, because stipulating that cuts the partnership between them, and partnership is necessary, as in the contract of shirkah. He said: So if he stipulates an extra ten [dirhams], then he [the mudarib] is entitled to the wages of his like (ajr al-mithl) due to the voidness [of the condition], for it may be that he only profits this amount, and thus partnership in profit is cut. This is because he sought compensation for his benefit but did not receive it due to the voidness, and the profit goes to the rabb al-mal because it is the growth of his property. And this is the ruling in every case where mudarabah is not valid. And the wage does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, as we explained in the chapter on shirkah. And the wage is obligatory even if he did not profit, in the narration of al-Asl, because the wage of the hireling becomes obligatory with the delivery of benefits or work, and it has occurred. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is not obligatory, by analogy with valid mudarabah, even though it is above it, and the property in void mudarabah is not guaranteed against destruction, by analogy with valid mudarabah, and because it is an object hired in his hand. And every condition that causes ignorance (jahl) in profit invalidates it because of disturbance of its purpose, but other void conditions do not invalidate it, and the condition is void, like stipulating loss upon the mudarib.

Translation: Among the conditions of mudarabah is that profit be shared between them, so that neither of them deserves specified dirhams from the profit. Because stipulating that cuts off partnership, while partnership is necessary, as in the contract of shirkah. So if he stipulates an extra ten dirhams, then the mudarib is entitled to the wages of his like due to the voidness of the mudarabah, because it is possible that profit is only that amount, so partnership in profit is cut. And this is because the mudarib sought compensation for his benefit, and he did not attain it due to the voidness of the contract. And all profit goes to the rabb al-mal because it is the growth of his property. And this is the ruling in every case where mudarabah is invalid. And the wage does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, as we mentioned in the book of shirkah. And the wage is obligatory even if no profit was earned, in the narration of al-Asl, because the wage of the hireling becomes obligatory upon delivery of benefits or work, and it has occurred. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is not obligatory, by analogy with valid mudarabah, even though it is superior; and the property in void mudarabah is not guaranteed against destruction, by analogy with valid mudarabah, and because it is an object hired in his hand. And every condition that causes ignorance (jahl) in the profit invalidates it due to disturbance of its purpose, but other void conditions do not invalidate it, and the condition is void, such as stipulating a loss upon the mudarib.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, outlining the conditions of profit sharing in mudarabah. It states that the profit must be a common share (musha'), meaning it is undivided and proportionally allocated, not a fixed sum like ten dirhams. If a fixed sum is stipulated, the mudarabah becomes fasid (void), and the mudarib is entitled to the wages of his like (ajr al-mithl) for his labor, up to the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, but without that limit according to Imam Muhammad. The profit goes entirely to the rabb al-mal. The passage also discusses whether the wage is due even if no profit is made: the narration of al-Asl (which is part of Zahir al-Riwayah) says it is due because the mudarib's work is compensated like a hireling; Abu Yusuf analogizes to valid mudarabah where no wage is due if no profit is earned, but the text notes that valid mudarabah is superior, so the analogy may not hold. Additionally, the property in fasid mudarabah is not guaranteed (i.e., the mudarib is not liable for loss), unlike a borrower. The passage ends by noting that any condition causing ignorance (jahl) about the profit invalidates the mudarabah due to uncertainty (gharar), but other void conditions do not invalidate the contract itself; only the condition is void, such as stipulating that the mudarib bears any loss.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushāʿ): A common, undivided share; profit must be shared proportionally, not as a fixed sum.
اجرة المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage equivalent to the mudarib's work.
مضاربت فاسدہ (muḍārabah fāsidah): A void mudarabah due to a defective condition, e.g., fixed profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if mudarabah parties stipulate a fixed sum profit for the mudarib?
A) The mudarabah is valid but the condition is void
B) The mudarabah becomes fasid and the mudarib gets the profit as stipulated
C) The mudarabah is fasid, the mudarib gets ajr al-mithl, and all profit goes to rabb al-mal
D) The mudarabah is void (batil) entirely

Key Takeaway
Profit in mudarabah must be a proportional common share; a fixed sum invalidates the contract.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
8 min
Compensation in Fasid Mudarabah: The Wage Dispute
Presents the intra-Hanafi debate on the mudarib's wage in fasid mudarabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the limit and obligation of the mudarib's wage in a fasid mudarabah.

Core Idea
In fasid mudarabah, the mudarib's wage (ajr al-mithl) is disputed: Abu Yusuf limits it to the stipulated amount; Muhammad allows exceeding it; and whether it is due without profit is also contested.

When a mudarabah becomes void due to a defective condition, compensation for the mudarib's labor is not straightforward. The Hanafi school has an internal debate, recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, about whether the wage is capped by the void stipulation and whether it is owed even if no profit is generated. This lesson examines the evidence and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the dispute
The passage presents two points of contention: (1) the maximum limit of ajr al-mithl, and (2) whether the wage is due without profit.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
2
State Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that ajr al-mithl cannot exceed the stipulated amount, and that it is not obligatory if no profit is earned.
He analogizes to valid mudarabah where no wage is due without profit.
3
State Muhammad's view
Muhammad holds that ajr al-mithl is not limited by the stipulation (it can be higher), and that it is obligatory even if no profit is made.
He relies on the narration of al-Asl (Zahir al-Riwayah) and general principles of hire.
4
Identify the dalil for each
Abu Yusuf uses qiyas with valid mudarabah. Muhammad uses the narration of al-Asl that the wage of a hireling is due upon delivery of work.
The narration of al-Asl is a strong textual proof within the school.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If market rate is higher than stipulated, Abu Yusuf caps at stipulated; Muhammad gives market rate. If no profit, Abu Yusuf says no wage; Muhammad says wage due.
The mufta bihi position seems to combine: wage is due even without profit (al-Asl) but capped at stipulated amount (Abu Yusuf).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, outlining the conditions of profit sharing in mudarabah. It states that the profit must be a common share (musha'), meaning it is undivided and proportionally allocated, not a fixed sum like ten dirhams. If a fixed sum is stipulated, the mudarabah becomes fasid (void), and the mudarib is entitled to the wages of his like (ajr al-mithl) for his labor, up to the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, but without that limit according to Imam Muhammad. The profit goes entirely to the rabb al-mal. The passage also discusses whether the wage is due even if no profit is made: the narration of al-Asl (which is part of Zahir al-Riwayah) says it is due because the mudarib's work is compensated like a hireling; Abu Yusuf analogizes to valid mudarabah where no wage is due if no profit is earned, but the text notes that valid mudarabah is superior, so the analogy may not hold. Additionally, the property in fasid mudarabah is not guaranteed (i.e., the mudarib is not liable for loss), unlike a borrower. The passage ends by noting that any condition causing ignorance (jahl) about the profit invalidates the mudarabah due to uncertainty (gharar), but other void conditions do not invalidate the contract itself; only the condition is void, such as stipulating that the mudarib bears any loss.

Key Terms
اجرة المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage equivalent to the mudarib's work.
رواية الأصل (riwayat al-asl): The narration from the original (al-Asl) text, a foundational book of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Yusuf's view regarding the mudarib's wage in a fasid mudarabah?
A) The wage is unlimited and obligatory even without profit
B) The wage is limited to the stipulated amount and obligatory even without profit
C) The wage is limited to the stipulated amount and not obligatory if no profit
D) The wage is not obligatory in any case

Key Takeaway
In fasid mudarabah, Abu Yusuf caps the wage at the stipulated amount and does not obligate it without profit; Muhammad allows market rate and obligates it even without profit.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
6 min
Conditions That Invalidate Mudarabah vs. Those That Are Merely Void
Differentiates conditions that invalidate mudarabah from those merely void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions that cause jahl (ignorance) in profit — which invalidate the entire mudarabah — and other void conditions that do not affect the contract's validity.

Core Idea
Jahl in profit destroys mudarabah; but void conditions like stipulating loss on the mudarib are merely void, leaving the contract intact.

Not all defective conditions destroy a mudarabah. The Hanafi school differentiates between conditions that create uncertainty about the profit (jahl) — which directly undermine the contract's purpose — and conditions that are simply invalid but do not affect the essential profit-sharing nature. This lesson clarifies the distinction and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage states that any condition that causes ignorance (jahl) in profit invalidates the mudarabah.
Jahl in profit means uncertainty about how much or what share the mudarib will receive.
2
Understand why jahl in profit is fatal
It disturbs the purpose of the contract, which is to share known profit proportionally.
This is based on the prohibition of gharar (excessive uncertainty).
3
Recognize examples of jahl conditions
Fixing a profit sum (e.g., 10 dirhams) creates jahl because the profit amount is unknown; the mudarib's share becomes uncertain.
Other examples: 'you get whatever is left' or 'a fair share' without specification.
4
Contrast with other void conditions
Conditions that do not cause jahl in profit, like 'mudarib bears all losses', are void but do not invalidate the contract.
Such conditions are simply dropped, and the mudarabah proceeds normally.
5
Determine the effect
If the condition is void but does not cause jahl, the contract remains valid and the condition is void. If it causes jahl, the contract is fasid.
The passage explicitly contrasts: 'every condition that causes jahl in profit invalidates it... other void conditions do not invalidate it'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ شَرَطَهَا أَنْ يَكُونَ الرِّبْحُ بَيْنَهُمَا مُشَاعَاً لَا يَسْتَحِقُ أَحَدَهُمَا دَرَاهِمُ مُسَمَاةِ مِنَ الرِّبْحِ لَانَّ شَرْطَ ذلِكَ يَقْطَعُ الشَّرْكَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا وَلَابُدَّ مِنْهَا كَمَا فِى عَقْدِ الشَّرُكَةِ قَالَ فَإِنْ شَرَطَ زِيَادَةَ عَشَرَةَ فَلَهُ أَجْرُ مِثْلِهِ لفَسَادِهِ فَلَعَلَّهُ لَا يَرْبَحْ إِلَّا هَذَا الْقَدْرَ فَيَقْطَعُ الشَّرْكَةُ فِي الرِّبْحِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ ابْتَغَى عَنْ مُنَافِعِهِ عِوَضًا وَلَمْ يَنَلْ لفَسَادِهِ وَالرِّبْحُ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّهُ نماءُ مِلْكِهِ وَهَذَا هُوَ الْحُكْمُ فِى كُلَّ مَوْضِعِ لَمْ يَصِحُ الْمُضَارَبَةُ وَلَا تُجَاوَزُ بِالْآخِرِ الْقَدْرِ الْمَشْرُوطِ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ خِلَافًا لِمُحَمَّدٌ كَمَا بَيَّنَا فِي الشَّرَكَةِ وَيَجِبُ الْأَجْرُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَرْبَحَ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ لِأَنَّ أَجْرَ الْأَخِيرِ يَجِبُ بِتَسْلِيمِ الْمَنَافِعِ أَوِ الْعَمَلِ وَقَدْ وَجَدَ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْمُضَارَبَةِ الصَّحِيحَةِ مَعَ أَنَّهَا فَوْقَهَا وَالْمَالُ فِى الْمُصَارَبَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونِ بِالْهَلَاكِ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالصَّحِيحَةِ وَلِأَنَّهُ عَيْنٌ مُسْتَاجَرَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ وَكُلُّ شَرْطٍ يُوجِبُ جِهَالَةً فِي الرِّبْحِ يُفْسِدُهُ لِاخْتِلَالِ مَقْصُودِهِ وَغَيْرَ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الشَّرُوطِ الْفَاسِدَةِ لَا يُفْسِدُهَا وَيَبْطُلُ الشَّرْطُ كَاشْتِرَاطِ الْوَضِيْعَةِ عَلَى الْمُصَارِبِ

ترجمہ شروط مضاربت میں ہے یہ ہے کہ نفع ان دونوں میں مشترک ہو کہ ان میں سے کوئی نفع سے معین در اہم کا مستحق نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ اس کی شرط کرنا قاطع شرکت ہے۔ حالانکہ شرکت ضروری ہے جیسا کہ عقد شرکت میں ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر شرط کی دیں دور ہم زائد کی تو مضارب کے لئے اجر مثل ہوگا فساد مضاربت کی وجہ سے کیونکہ ممکن ہے نفع اس قدر ہو تو نفع میں شرکت منقطع ہو جائے گی اور یہ اس لئے کہ مضارب نے اپنے نفع کا عوض چاہا اور وہ فساد عقد کی وجہ سے نہیں پایا۔ اور پورا نفع رب المال کا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کی ملک کا پھل ہے اور یہی حکم ہے ہر اس جگہ میں جہاں مضاربت صحیح نہ ہوئی ہو۔ اور اجر مثل مقدار مشروط سے نہیں بڑھے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بر خلاف امام محمد کے جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا ہے کتاب الشرکة میں۔ اور اجرت واجب ہوگی۔ اگر چہ نفع نہ کمایا ہو۔ مبسوط کی روایت میں۔ کیونکہ اجیر کی اجرت واجب ہو جاتی ہے۔ منافع یا کام سپر د کر نے سے اور یہ پایا گیا اور امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی بقیاس مضاربت صحیحہ کے باوجود یکہ بیچ فاسدہ سے بڑھ کر ہے اور مضاربت فاسدہ میں مال مضمون نہیں ہوتا ہلاک ہونے سے بقیاس مضاربت صحیح کے اور اس لئے کہ مال تو اس کے قبضہ میں اجارہ پر لی ہوئی چیز ہے۔ اور ہر وہ
He said: One of its conditions is that profit be shared (musha'an) between them, and neither of them deserves specified dirhams from the profit, because stipulating that cuts the partnership between them, and partnership is necessary, as in the contract of shirkah. He said: So if he stipulates an extra ten [dirhams], then he [the mudarib] is entitled to the wages of his like (ajr al-mithl) due to the voidness [of the condition], for it may be that he only profits this amount, and thus partnership in profit is cut. This is because he sought compensation for his benefit but did not receive it due to the voidness, and the profit goes to the rabb al-mal because it is the growth of his property. And this is the ruling in every case where mudarabah is not valid. And the wage does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, as we explained in the chapter on shirkah. And the wage is obligatory even if he did not profit, in the narration of al-Asl, because the wage of the hireling becomes obligatory with the delivery of benefits or work, and it has occurred. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is not obligatory, by analogy with valid mudarabah, even though it is above it, and the property in void mudarabah is not guaranteed against destruction, by analogy with valid mudarabah, and because it is an object hired in his hand. And every condition that causes ignorance (jahl) in profit invalidates it because of disturbance of its purpose, but other void conditions do not invalidate it, and the condition is void, like stipulating loss upon the mudarib.

Translation: Among the conditions of mudarabah is that profit be shared between them, so that neither of them deserves specified dirhams from the profit. Because stipulating that cuts off partnership, while partnership is necessary, as in the contract of shirkah. So if he stipulates an extra ten dirhams, then the mudarib is entitled to the wages of his like due to the voidness of the mudarabah, because it is possible that profit is only that amount, so partnership in profit is cut. And this is because the mudarib sought compensation for his benefit, and he did not attain it due to the voidness of the contract. And all profit goes to the rabb al-mal because it is the growth of his property. And this is the ruling in every case where mudarabah is invalid. And the wage does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, as we mentioned in the book of shirkah. And the wage is obligatory even if no profit was earned, in the narration of al-Asl, because the wage of the hireling becomes obligatory upon delivery of benefits or work, and it has occurred. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is not obligatory, by analogy with valid mudarabah, even though it is superior; and the property in void mudarabah is not guaranteed against destruction, by analogy with valid mudarabah, and because it is an object hired in his hand. And every condition that causes ignorance (jahl) in the profit invalidates it due to disturbance of its purpose, but other void conditions do not invalidate it, and the condition is void, such as stipulating a loss upon the mudarib.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, outlining the conditions of profit sharing in mudarabah. It states that the profit must be a common share (musha'), meaning it is undivided and proportionally allocated, not a fixed sum like ten dirhams. If a fixed sum is stipulated, the mudarabah becomes fasid (void), and the mudarib is entitled to the wages of his like (ajr al-mithl) for his labor, up to the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, but without that limit according to Imam Muhammad. The profit goes entirely to the rabb al-mal. The passage also discusses whether the wage is due even if no profit is made: the narration of al-Asl (which is part of Zahir al-Riwayah) says it is due because the mudarib's work is compensated like a hireling; Abu Yusuf analogizes to valid mudarabah where no wage is due if no profit is earned, but the text notes that valid mudarabah is superior, so the analogy may not hold. Additionally, the property in fasid mudarabah is not guaranteed (i.e., the mudarib is not liable for loss), unlike a borrower. The passage ends by noting that any condition causing ignorance (jahl) about the profit invalidates the mudarabah due to uncertainty (gharar), but other void conditions do not invalidate the contract itself; only the condition is void, such as stipulating that the mudarib bears any loss.

Key Terms
جهالت (jahālah): Ignorance or uncertainty that can invalidate a contract.
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fāsid): A condition that is void and does not invalidate the contract (if it does not cause jahl in profit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a condition invalidate a mudarabah?
A) Whenever the condition is void
B) Only if the condition involves a fixed sum of money
C) Only if the condition creates ignorance (jahl) in the profit
D) Never, because conditions can always be removed

Key Takeaway
Only conditions that cause uncertainty (jahl) in the profit share invalidate the mudarabah; other void conditions are simply dropped.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
12 min
Profit Must Be Shared: Conditions of Valid Mudarabah and Rulings on Defective Contracts
Shaping rules for mudarabah conditions and defective contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that profit in mudarabah must be musha' and explain the rulings when a fixed profit amount is stipulated, including ajr al-mithl and the intra-Hanafi disputes.

Core Idea
Stipulating a fixed profit severs partnership; the contract becomes fasid, and the mudarib gets ajr al-mithl.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a fundamental condition of mudarabah: profit must be shared proportionally (musha'), not fixed. If a fixed amount is stipulated, the contract becomes fasid (corrupt). The mudarib then deserves the prevailing market wage (ajr al-mithl), and all profit goes to the investor. The passage also presents disagreements between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding whether the wage exceeds the stipulated amount and whether it is obligatory without profit. Understanding these details helps you apply Hanafi rules in partnership investments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential condition for valid mudarabah
The passage states that profit must be musha' (shared proportionally, e.g., half or one-third). A fixed amount severs partnership. This is the key validity condition.
Also compare with partnership (shirkah) where profit must be shared.
2
Analyze the ruling when a fixed amount is stipulated
If any party stipulates a fixed dirham amount from profit, the contract becomes fasid. The mudarib is not entitled to that fixed amount but instead gets ajr al-mithl (market wage) for his labor. All profit goes to the investor.
The fasid contract still has some effects — wage is due, capital is not guaranteed.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi disputes on wage
Two disputes: (1) Whether ajr al-mithl can exceed the stipulated amount? Abu Yusuf says no (limited by stipulation); Muhammad says yes (full market wage). (2) Whether wage is obligatory if no profit? In al-Asl narration, yes; from Abu Yusuf, no (qiyas to valid mudarabah).
The text references the Book of Partnership for more detail.
4
Apply the general rule on conditions causing ignorance
Any condition that creates uncertainty (jahalah) in profit corrupts the mudarabah. Other corrupt conditions (like stipulating loss on mudarib) are void but do not invalidate the contract.
This distinguishes between conditions affecting profit and other invalid conditions.

ہوئی چیز ہے۔ اور ہر وہ چیز جو نفع میں جہالت پیدا کرے وہ مفید مضاربت ہے مقصود میں خلل پڑنے کی وجہ سے اس کے علاوہ چوری کی نہیں کرتیں بلکہ خود شرط باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے مضارب پر چھٹی کی شرط لگانا۔ تشریح چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ ایسی شرط سے تو ان کے درمیان شرکت ہی جاتی رہے گی حالانکہ شرکت کا ہونا ضروری ہے ۔ قوله فان شرط زيادة ... الخ - پس اگر مضارب یا رب المال نے اپنے لئے معین مقدار کی یادس درہم زائد کی شرط کر لی تو عقد فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے اس مقدار سے زائد نفع حاصل نہ ہو پس نفع میں شرکت منقطع ہو جائے گی۔ اور جب عقد فاسد ہو گیا تو اب مضارب کو اس کی محنت کی مزدوری ملے گی۔ اس لئے کہ اس نے اپنے منافع کا عوض چاہا تھا جو فساد عقد کی وجہ سے نہیں پایا گیا لہذا اس کو مزدوری دی جائے گی اور پورا نفع رب المثال کا ہوگا کیونکہ وہ اس کی ملکیت کا ثمرہ ہے۔ تنبیه .... عام شراح ہدایہ نے بعد والے مسئلے یعنی "فان شرط زيادة اہ" کو پہلے مسئلے "ومن شرطها ان يكون الربح اهـ" کی تفسیر قرار دیا ہے۔ مگر یہ اس لئے صحیح نہیں کہ پہلا مسئلہ جو مختصر القدوری کا ہے وہ دوسرے مسئلہ سے ( جو جامع صغیر کا ہے ) عام ہے۔ کیونکہ کسی ایک کے لئے معین در اہم کا مشروط ہونا متعددصورتوں میں جاری ہو سکتا ہے جو فتاویٰ کی کتب معتبرہ بدائع وذخیرہ وغیرہ میں مذکور ہیں مثلاً۔ یہ شرط کرنا کہ نفع سے ایک سو درہم یا اس سے کم و بیش ایک کے لئے ہوں گے اور باقی دوسرے کے۔ ۲۔ ایک کے لئے نفع کا نصف یا ثلث ہو گا مگر دس درہم کم ۔ ۳۔ ایک کے لئے نفع کا نصف یا ثلث ہوگا۔ مگر دس درہم زائد۔ ان سب صورتوں میں مضاربت فاسد ہو گی۔ کیونکہ اس طرح کی شرطیں قاطع شرکت ہیں۔ بخلاف دسن درہم زائد کی شرط کے جو جامع صغیر میں مذکور ہے کہ یہ مذکورہ صورتوں میں سے صرف تیسری صورت میں چل سکتی ہے۔ پس جامع صغیر کا مسئلہ اخص ہو جوام کی تفسیر نہیں ہوسکتا۔ علاوہ مسئلہ کا مقصد فساد عقد مضاربت کا بیان ہے اور دوسرے مسئلہ کا مقصد وجوب اجر مثل کو بیان کرتا ہے۔ فكانه قال اذا عرفت فساد عقد الْمُضَارَبَةِ بالشرط المذكور فاعلم ان حكم وجوب اجر المثل اهـ - (نتائج) قـولـه ولا يجاوز بالاجر..... الخ - فساد عقد کی صورت میں اجرت مثل تو ملے گی۔ لیکن جو مقدار مشروط تھی ۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس مقدار سے زائد مزدوری نہیں دی جائے گی۔ اجارہ فاسدہ کا یہی حکم ہے کہ اس کی اجرت مقدار مشروط سے زیادہ نہیں ہوتی ۔ امام محمد اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک پوری مزدوری دی جائے گی ۔ گومشروط سے زائد ہو۔ قوله و لا يجب الاجر .... الخ - پھر اصل یعنی مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق مضاربت فاسدہ میں اجرت واجب ہوگی۔ اگر چہ مضارب نے نفع نہ کمایا ہو۔ امام شافعی اور ایک قول میں امام احمد بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ جب اجر خاص اپنے منافع اور اجیر مشترک اپنا کام سپر د کر دے تو اس کی اجرت واجب ہو جاتی ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ بقیاس مضاربت صحیحہ یہاں بھی اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ حالانکہ مضاربت صحیحہ تو مضاربت فاسدہ سے بڑھ کر ہے۔ پس جب نفع نہ ہونے کی صورت میں مضاربت صحیحہ میں کچھ نہیں ملتا تو مضاربت فاسدہ میں بطریق اولی نہیں ملے گا۔ قوله مضاربت شرط .... الخ شرور مضاربت کا قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ گر عقد مضاربت میں کوئی موجب جہالت نفع شرط لگائی گئی۔ مثلاً
Book of Mudarabah. Conditions of Mudarabah: He said: Among its conditions is that the profit between them be shared (musha'), that neither of them deserves fixed dirhams from the profit, because stipulating that severs the partnership between them, and partnership is necessary as in the contract of partnership. He said: If he stipulates an increase of ten, then he gets the equivalent wage (ajr mithl) due to its corruptness, because perhaps he may not earn except this amount, so it severs partnership in profit. This is because he sought compensation for his benefits but did not attain it due to the corruptness, and the profit belongs to the owner of capital because it is the growth of his property. And this is the ruling in every instance where the mudarabah is not valid. And the wage does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, as we explained in the Book of Partnership. And the wage is obligatory even if he did not profit in the narration of the original (al-Asl), because the wage of the hiree becomes due by handing over benefits or work, and that has occurred. And from Abu Yusuf that it is not obligatory by analogy to valid mudarabah, even though it is above it (the defective one). And in defective mudarabah, the capital is not guaranteed for destruction by analogy to valid mudarabah, and because it is a leased commodity in his possession. And every condition that causes ignorance in the profit corrupts it due to disturbance of its purpose. Other than that from corrupt conditions do not corrupt it, and the condition becomes void, like stipulating loss upon the mudarib. Translation: In the conditions of mudarabah, it is that the profit is shared between them, that none of them deserves fixed dirhams from the profit. Because stipulating that severs the partnership, while partnership is necessary as in the contract of company. So if he stipulates an increase of ten dirhams, then the mudarib gets the equivalent wage due to the corruptness of the mudarabah, because it is possible that the profit is that much, so partnership in profit would be severed. And this is because the mudarib sought compensation for his profit, and he did not attain it due to corruptness. And all profit belongs to the owner of capital because it is the fruit of his ownership. And this is the ruling in every place where the mudarabah is not valid. And the equivalent wage does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Imam Abu Yusuf, contrary to Imam Muhammad, as we explained in the Book of Partnership. And the wage is obligatory even if he did not earn profit, in the narration of al-Mabsut, because the wage of the hiree becomes obligatory by handing over benefits or work, and that has occurred. And from Abu Yusuf that the wage is not obligatory by analogy to valid mudarabah, even though it is above the defective one. And in defective mudarabah, the capital is not guaranteed for destruction by analogy to valid mudarabah, and because the capital is a leased thing in his possession. And every condition that creates ignorance in the profit invalidates the mudarabah due to disturbance of its purpose. Apart from that, corrupt conditions do not invalidate it, but the condition itself becomes void, like stipulating loss upon the mudarib. Elaboration: His statement: 'Among its conditions...' For the validity of mudarabah, it is a condition that the profit is common and general between them, e.g., half half or one third each. The meaning is that none of them should deserve fixed dirhams from the profit. Because such a condition will sever the partnership between them, while partnership is necessary. His statement: 'If he stipulates an increase...' So if the mudarib or the owner of capital stipulates for himself a fixed amount, like ten dirhams increase, then the contract becomes corrupt. Because it is possible that profit beyond that amount is not achieved, so partnership in profit would be severed. And when the contract is corrupt, then the mudarib gets the wage for his labor. This is because he sought compensation for his profit, which was not attained due to the corruptness of the contract, so he is given a wage, and all profit belongs to the owner of capital because it is the fruit of his ownership. Note: Most commentators of Hidayah have interpreted the later mas'alah 'If he stipulates an increase...' as an explanation of the first mas'alah 'Among its conditions that profit be shared...'. But this is not correct because the first mas'alah (from Mukhtasar al-Quduri) is general compared to the second (from Jami' al-Saghir). Because stipulating fixed dirhams for one can occur in multiple scenarios mentioned in reliable fatwa books like Bada'i' and Dhakhirah, for example: stipulating that one gets one hundred dirhams and the rest for the other; or stipulating half or third minus ten dirhams; or half or third plus ten dirhams. In all these cases mudarabah is corrupt because such conditions sever partnership. Unlike the condition of ten dirhams increase mentioned in Jami' al-Saghir, which only applies to the third scenario. So the mas'alah of Jami' al-Saghir is specific and cannot be an interpretation of the general. Moreover, the ruling of the first mas'alah is corruptness of the contract, while the ruling of the second is obligation of equivalent wage. So how can one be an explanation of the other? Therefore it is better to consider the letter 'fa' as for detailing, saying that the purpose of the first mas'alah is to state the corruptness of the mudarabah contract, and the purpose of the second is to state the obligation of equivalent wage. As if he said: When you know the corruptness of the mudarabah contract due to the mentioned condition, know that the ruling is the obligation of equivalent wage. (Results) His statement: 'And the wage does not exceed...' In case of corrupt contract, equivalent wage is given, but not exceeding the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf. This is the ruling in corrupt ijarah: its wage does not exceed the stipulated amount. According to Imam Muhammad and the three Imams, the full wage is given, even if it exceeds the stipulated amount. His statement: 'And the wage is not obligatory...' Then according to the original (al-Mabsut) narration, in defective mudarabah the wage is obligatory even if the mudarib did not earn profit. Imam Shafi'i and in one saying Imam Ahmad also hold this. Because when a specific hiree hands over his benefits or a common hiree performs the work, his wage becomes obligatory. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that by analogy to valid mudarabah, the wage is not obligatory here. Even though valid mudarabah is superior to defective mudarabah. So when in valid mudarabah nothing is given in case of no profit, then in defective mudarabah a fortiori nothing is given. His statement: 'Condition of mudarabah...' The general rule of conditions in mudarabah is that if a condition that causes ignorance in profit is stipulated in the mudarabah contract, for example...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the conditions of a valid mudarabah contract and the rulings when a corrupt condition is stipulated. The passage is a commentary (sharh) on the original matn from al-Hidayah, which itself builds on earlier texts (Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir). The author begins by stating the essential condition: profit must be shared proportionally between the investor (rabb al-mal) and the worker (mudarib) on a common ratio (musha'), i.e., a fraction like half or one-third. Stipulating a fixed amount (e.g., 10 dirhams) for either party invalidates the contract because it severs the partnership in profit, which is the essence of mudarabah. If such a fixed condition is made, the contract becomes fasid (corrupt). In that case, the mudarib is entitled to ajr al-mithl (the prevailing market wage) for his labor, and all profit belongs to the investor as it is the growth of his capital. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Abu Yusuf, the wage cannot exceed the stipulated amount; this is based on the analogy with a corrupt ijarah contract, where the wage is limited by the agreed amount. Imam Muhammad (and the three other schools) hold that the full market wage is due, even if it exceeds the stipulated amount. Another dispute concerns whether the wage is obligatory if no profit is earned. In the narration of al-Asl (al-Mabsut), the wage is obligatory even without profit, because the mudarib has performed work. But Abu Yusuf analogizes to a valid mudarabah: if no profit, the mudarib gets nothing; hence in a defective mudarabah, a fortiori he should get nothing. The passage also clarifies a common misunderstanding: the two mas'alah (conditions and increase) are not in the relation of general to specific; rather they address separate issues—the first states that fixing profit invalidates the contract, the second states the consequence (wage). The general rule is that any condition causing gharar (uncertainty) in profit corrupts the contract, but other corrupt conditions (like imposing loss on the mudarib) are void while the contract remains valid.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushā‘): Shared proportionally between the parties, e.g., half or one-third, not fixed in amount.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The prevailing market wage for similar work, given to the mudarib when the contract is defective.
مضاربة فاسدة (muḍārabah fāsidah): A mudarabah contract lacking a condition of validity (e.g., profit fixed), still produces some effects but not full partnership effects.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The investor who provides the capital in a mudarabah.
مضارب (muḍārib): The worker/manager who invests labor in the mudarabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid mudarabah, what is the mudarib's entitlement if the contract stipulated a fixed profit share?
A) The fixed amount stipulated.
B) Ajr al-mithl (market wage) for his labor.
C) Nothing, because the contract is void.
D) Half of the profit by default.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a mudarabah contract is valid only if profit is shared proportionally; stipulating a fixed amount makes it fasid, entitling the mudarib to market wage but not the fixed sum.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
10 min
Fixed Profit Stipulation Invalidates Mudaraba
Ruling with proof on fixed profit condition invalidating mudaraba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mudaraba contract becomes fasid if a fixed profit is stipulated, explain the reason (severance of partnership), and determine the consequence: the mudarib receives wages and all profit goes to the capital owner.

Core Idea
A fixed profit stipulation severs the partnership; the contract becomes fasid and the mudarib only gets wages.

In a mudaraba (sleeping partnership), profit must be shared in a known proportion. Any condition that creates jahalah (uncertainty) in the profit share disrupts the essence of the contract. This lesson examines the effect of stipulating a fixed amount of profit for one party, a practice that renders the contract defective (fasid) and changes the financial rights of the parties.

Guided Path
1
Understand the essential condition of mudaraba
Profit must be shared between the capital owner (rabb al-mal) and the worker (mudarib) in a known proportion (e.g., half, one-third). This partnership is the foundation of the contract.
2
Identify the invalidating condition
If either party stipulates a fixed amount of profit (e.g., 100 dirhams) the contract becomes fasid. This is because the fixed amount severs the profit-sharing partnership—the profit may not reach that amount, making the share uncertain.
3
Determine the ruling: fasid (defective)
The contract is not void (batil) but fasid. This means it is invalid from its inception, but if work has been done, the mudarib is entitled to wages (ujrat al-mithl) for his labor, and all profit belongs to the capital owner.
4
Contrast with a condition that does not invalidate
Not every condition invalidates. For example, stipulating that the mudarib does not work on holidays does not create jahalah in profit; only the condition is void, and the contract remains valid.

(نتائج)
Those are. They make mudaraba fasid. A thing that creates ignorance in profit is harmful to mudaraba because it disrupts the objective. Apart from that, they do not steal [؟], but rather the condition itself becomes void, like stipulating a holiday for the mudarib. Explanation: The saying 'and from its conditions...' etc.: For the validity of mudaraba, it is necessary for the profit to be common and shared between the two, e.g. half-half or one-third each is a condition. Meaning that none of them should have the right to a fixed known amount from the profit, because such a condition would cut the partnership between them, whereas partnership is necessary. The saying: 'For if he stipulates an increase...' etc.: So if the mudarib or the owner of capital stipulates for himself a fixed amount of dirhams as additional, the contract becomes fasid. Because it is possible that no profit beyond that amount is obtained, so partnership in profit is severed. And when the contract becomes fasid, the mudarib will receive wages for his labor, because he sought compensation for his profit which was not attained due to the invalidity of the contract. Therefore, he will be paid wages, and all profit will belong to the owner of capital because it is the fruit of his ownership. Warning: Most commentators of Al-Hidayah have interpreted the later issue, i.e. 'for if he stipulates an increase', as an interpretation of the earlier issue 'and from its conditions is that the profit be...' But this is incorrect because the first issue, which is from Mukhtasar al-Quduri, is more general than the second issue, which is from Jami' al-Saghir. Because stipulating a fixed amount for one party can apply to multiple forms, which are mentioned in reliable books of fatwa like Bada'i' and Dhakhira etc., for example: 1. Stipulating that one hundred dirhams, or more or less than that, from the profit will be for one and the rest for the other. 2. For one, half or one-third of the profit, but ten dirhams less. 3. For one, half or one-third of the profit, but ten dirhams more. In all these forms the mudaraba is fasid, because such conditions cut partnership. Unlike the condition of ten extra dirhams mentioned in Jami' al-Saghir, which applies only to the third of these forms. So the issue of Jami' al-Saghir is more specific and cannot be an interpretation of the more general. Moreover, the ruling of the first issue is invalidity of the contract, and the ruling of the second issue is obligation of compensation (ujrat al-mithl). So how can one be the interpretation of the other? Therefore, it is better to take the 'fa' as for explanation, saying that the purpose of the first issue is to state the invalidity of the mudaraba contract, and the purpose of the second issue is to state the obligation of compensation. As if he said: When you know the invalidity of the mudaraba contract due to the mentioned condition, then know that the ruling is the obligation of compensation... (Results).
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation. It addresses the effect of stipulating a fixed amount of profit in a mudaraba contract. The author begins by stating the general principle: any condition that creates ignorance (jahalah) in the profit share invalidates the mudaraba (makes it fasid). Conversely, a condition that does not cause jahalah does not invalidate the contract; only the condition itself becomes void. An example is requiring the mudarib to work on holidays. The commentary then explains the condition from the matn: for a valid mudaraba, the profit must be shared between the two parties in a known proportion (e.g., half-half, one-third). No party can claim a fixed amount from the profit, as this negates the partnership. The author then quotes the ruling from Al-Hidayah: if the mudarib or the capital owner stipulates a fixed additional amount for himself, the contract becomes fasid. The reason is that the stipulated amount may not be realized from the profit, thereby severing the profit-sharing partnership. The consequence is that the mudarib receives wages (ujrat al-mithl) for his labor, and all profit goes to the capital owner. The passage includes a warning (tanbih) clarifying that the later statement in Jami' al-Saghir about stipulating ten extra dirhams is not a mere interpretation of the earlier general statement in Mukhtasar al-Quduri; rather, they address distinct issues. The general statement covers multiple scenarios of fixed stipulations (e.g., a fixed sum, half minus a fixed sum, half plus a fixed sum), all of which invalidate the contract. The specific statement applies only to the case of an additional fixed amount beyond a profit share. The author prefers to view the two statements as separate: one explains invalidity, the other explains the ruling of compensation.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudāraba): A partnership contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared according to a stipulated ratio.
فساد العقد (fasād al-ʿaqd): The contract is legally defective (fasid) meaning it is not valid but may have some effects, such as entitlement to wages for work done.
جهالة الربح (jahālat al-ribḥ): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the amount of profit, which is a cause of invalidity in mudaraba because the subject matter must be known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of stipulating that the capital owner receives a fixed 1,000 dirhams from the profit in a mudaraba contract?
A) The condition is void, but the contract remains valid.
B) The entire contract becomes fasid, and the mudarib receives wages.
C) The contract is valid and the condition is enforceable.
D) The contract becomes batil and no compensation is due.

Key Takeaway
A condition that creates jahalah (uncertainty) in the profit share of a mudaraba, such as a fixed amount, invalidates the contract (fasid) and triggers the rule of compensation (ujrat al-mithl) for the worker’s labor.

Compensation in Fasid Mudaraba: Limit and Condition
Rulings on compensation in invalid mudaraba with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-school dispute on whether ujrat al-mithl in a fasid mudaraba is capped by the stipulated amount and whether it is due without profit, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ujrat al-mithl is due in fasid mudaraba, but Abu Yusuf caps it at the stipulated amount; Muhammad and others give full market rate.

This lesson unpacks two intertwined disputes within the Hanafi school regarding compensation for the mudarib when the mudaraba is fasid. The first concerns the ceiling of compensation, the second its conditionality on profit. You will see how the school's reasoning (ta'lil) leads to different conclusions and which view becomes operative for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sub-issues
The text treats two separate questions: (a) whether ujrat al-mithl can exceed the stipulated wage, and (b) whether ujrat al-mithl is due even without profit.
2
State each imam's position on the limit
Abu Yusuf: no exceeding the stipulated amount (analogy to fasid ijara). Muhammad: full ujrat al-mithl even if more.
The 'three imams' (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) agree with Muhammad.
3
State each imam's position on obligation without profit
According to al-Mabsut (Zahir al-Riwayah), wages are obligatory even without profit. Abu Yusuf dissents via qiyas with valid mudaraba.
Imam al-Shafi'i and a report from Imam Ahmad agree with the Mabsut view.
4
Analyze the dalil and analogies used
On obligation: the mudarib is like an ajir khas (specific hired worker) who has surrendered his labor, so wages are due. On the cap: Abu Yusuf analogizes to fasid ijara where wages are limited to the agreed amount. Muhammad rejects this analogy because the mudarib's compensation is not a wage but a share of profit; when the contract is fasid, the share is void and ujrat al-mithl replaces it without artificial ceiling.
The strength of each analogy determines the preferred view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text presents the Mabsut narration first, indicating it is the relied-upon view. Later fatwa works adopt Imam Muhammad's position: full ujrat al-mithl is due even without profit.
Abu Yusuf's view is marjuh (weak) for fatwa but remains a valid ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قـولـه ولا يجاوز بالاجر..... الخ - فساد عقد کی صورت میں اجرت مثل تو ملے گی۔ لیکن جو مقدار مشروط تھی ۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس مقدار سے زائد مزدوری نہیں دی جائے گی۔ اجارہ فاسدہ کا یہی حکم ہے کہ اس کی اجرت مقدار مشروط سے زیادہ نہیں ہوتی ۔ امام محمد اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک پوری مزدوری دی جائے گی ۔ گومشروط سے زائد ہو۔ قوله و لا يجب الاجر .... الخ - پھر اصل یعنی مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق مضاربت فاسدہ میں اجرت واجب ہوگی۔ اگر چہ مضارب نے نفع نہ کمایا ہو۔ امام شافعی اور ایک قول میں امام احمد بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ جب اجر خاص اپنے منافع اور اجیر مشترک اپنا کام سپر د کر دے تو اس کی اجرت واجب ہو جاتی ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ بقیاس مضاربت صحیحہ یہاں بھی اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ حالانکہ مضاربت صحیحہ تو مضاربت فاسدہ سے بڑھ کر ہے۔ پس جب نفع نہ ہونے کی صورت میں مضاربت صحیحہ میں کچھ نہیں ملتا تو مضاربت فاسدہ میں بطریق اولی نہیں ملے گا۔
His saying: 'and does not exceed the wage...' etc. - In the case of a fasid contract, compensation (ujrat al-mithl) will be given, but it will not exceed the amount that was stipulated. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, wages will not be given more than the stipulated amount. This is the same ruling for a fasid ijara: its wages do not exceed the stipulated amount. According to Imam Muhammad and the three imams, full wages will be given, even if more than stipulated. His saying: 'and the wage is not obligatory...' etc. - Then, according to the original narration from al-Mabsut, in a fasid mudaraba, wages are obligatory even if the mudarib earned no profit. Imam al-Shafi'i and in one report Imam Ahmad also hold this view. Because when a specific worker (ajir khas) surrenders his labor for his profit share, and a common worker (ajir mushtarak) surrenders his work, his wage becomes obligatory. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that by analogy (qiyas) with a valid mudaraba, here too wages would not be obligatory, although a valid mudaraba is stronger than a fasid one. So if in a valid mudaraba nothing is given when there is no profit, then in a fasid mudaraba a fortiori nothing should be given.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage presents disputes within the Hanafi school and between schools regarding the compensation (ujrat al-mithl) due to the mudarib in a fasid mudaraba. It consists of two sub-rulings. First, the limit of compensation: In a fasid mudaraba, the mudarib is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (market rate for similar work). The question is whether this can exceed the amount stipulated in the invalid condition. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that it cannot exceed the stipulated amount, drawing an analogy to a fasid ijara (hire contract) where wages are capped by the agreed amount. Imam Muhammad and the three other school imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that full ujrat al-mithl is due even if it exceeds the stipulated amount. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is actually the view of Imam Muhammad, as the text mentions. Second, the obligation of wages when no profit is earned: According to the narration from al-Mabsut (a Zahir al-Riwayah text), wages are obligatory in a fasid mudaraba even if the mudarib earned no profit. This is because the mudarib is like an ajir khas (specific hired worker) who has surrendered his labor, making wages due. Imam al-Shafi'i and a report from Imam Ahmad agree. However, Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to hold that wages are not obligatory if no profit is earned, by qiyas with a valid mudaraba where no profit means no share. The text notes that the valid mudaraba is stronger, so a fasid one should a fortiori yield nothing. The commentary does not specify which view is mufta bihi for this second issue, but the first mention of the Mabsut narration suggests it is the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
أجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for work of a similar nature, determined by the prevailing rate for the same kind of labor.
أجير خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): A specific hired worker who works exclusively for one employer during the contract period; wages are due once he makes himself available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid mudaraba where the mudarib worked but earned no profit, which view is considered mufta bihi regarding compensation?
A) No compensation is due because no profit was earned.
B) The mudarib gets ujrat al-mithl even without profit.
C) The mudarib gets only the stipulated amount.
D) The mudarib gets nothing because the contract is batil.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid mudaraba, the mufta bihi Hanafi view awards the mudarib full ujrat al-mithl for his work, even if it exceeds the stipulated share and even if no profit is earned.

General Rule for Conditions in Mudaraba
Establishes a general rule for conditions in mudaraba and responds to an exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi general rule for conditions in mudaraba, identify which conditions invalidate the contract and which do not, and apply the exception for conditions that oppose the contract's essence.

Core Idea
Conditions causing ignorance of profit or cutting partnership invalidate mudaraba; other invalid conditions only become void.

This passage presents a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh for mudaraba contracts: not every invalid condition voids the contract. Only conditions that cause jahalah (ignorance) in the profit share or break the partnership between capital owner and worker make the contract fasid. However, an exception arises when a condition contradicts the very essence of mudaraba. Understanding this rule helps distinguish between void conditions and void contracts, a critical skill for Islamic finance professionals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
What two types of conditions invalidate a mudaraba according to the text? Look for the phrase 'موجب جہالت نفع' (causes ignorance of profit) and 'قاطع شرکت' (cuts partnership).
The rule is a qawida kulliyya (general principle).
2
Find examples of invalid conditions
The text gives explicit examples: an ambiguous profit share stated disjunctively (half or one-third) and a fixed amount for one party. Note how each falls under the two categories.
3
Identify valid conditions that do not invalidate
The text gives the example of stipulating loss liability on the mudarib. Such conditions do not cause jahalah or cut partnership, so the contract remains valid; only the condition is void.
Analogous to wakala and mahr contracts.
4
Analyze the exception
The later statement 'stipulating work on the owner of capital invalidates the contract' seems to contradict the general rule because it does not involve jahalah. Understand why it still invalidates—because it opposes the essence (muqtada al-aqd) of mudaraba.
Two responses are given: from Sahib al-Nihaya and Sahib al-Inaya.
5
Compare the two responses
Sahib al-Nihaya interprets the general rule's phrase 'other invalid conditions' as conditions that do not oppose the essence. Sahib al-Inaya argues that when such a condition is made, the contract ceases to be a mudaraba entirely, so the rule does not apply. Evaluate which reasoning you find more convincing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله مضاربت شرط .... الخ شرور مضاربت کا قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ گر عقد مضاربت میں کوئی موجب جہالت نفع شرط لگائی گئی۔ مثلاً رب المال نے مضارب سے بطریق تردید کہا کہ تیرے لئے نصف نفع ہے یا ثلث یا کوئی ایسی شرط لگائی گئی جو قاطع شرکت ہو۔ مثلا کسی ایک کے لئے معین در اہم کی شرط کر لینا تو ایسی شرطوں سے عقد مضاربت فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ مضاربت میں نفع معقود علیہ ہوتا ہے اور جہالت معقود علیہ مفسد عقد ہوتی ہے۔ اور اگر کوئی ایسی شرط لگائی گئی جو موجب جہالت نفع یا موجب قطع شرکت نہ ہو۔ جیسے مضارب پر ٹوٹے اور نقصان کی شرط کرنا تو ایسی شرط سے عقد فاسد نہیں ہوتا بلکہ خود وہ شرط باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے وکالت اور عقد مہ کہ شرط فاسد سے فاسد نہیں ہوتے۔ اس کلیہ پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ یہ آئندہ قول و شرط العمل على رب المال مفسد للعقد سے ٹوٹ جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ شرط بھی اس کلیہ کے تحت میں داخل ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ موجب جہالت ریح نہیں ہے اس کے باوجود مفسد عقد ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ہاں بات تو یہی ہے لیکن " وغير ذلك من الشروط الفاسدة " سے مراد وہ شرط ہے جو موجب عقد سے مانع نہ ہو۔ اور اگر شرط ایسی ہو جو موجب عقد سے مانع ہو تو وہ بھی مفسد عقد ہوگی۔ کیونکہ عقد کی مشروعیت تو موجب عقد کے اثبات ہی کے لئے ہے۔ یہ جواب صاحب نہایہ کا ہے۔ صاحب عنا یہ نے اس کا جواب یوں دیا ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے یہ کہا ہے " وغير ذلك من الشروط الفاسدة لا يفسدهااور جب رب المال پر عمل کی شرط ہو گئی تب تو وہ مضاربت ہی نہ رہی اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ معدوم سے شئی کا سلب جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ یہ کہنا صحیح ہے۔ زیـ المعدوم ليس ببصير، وقوله بعد هذا وشرط العمل على رب المال مفسد المعقد، معناه مانع عن تحققه
His saying: 'condition of mudaraba...' etc. The general rule of mudaraba conditions is that if a condition causing ignorance of profit is stipulated, for example the capital owner says to the mudarib in a hesitant manner 'you have half the profit or one-third', or a condition that cuts partnership, such as stipulating a fixed amount for one party, then such conditions make the mudaraba contract fasid. Because in mudaraba, profit is the subject matter, and ignorance of the subject matter invalidates the contract. And if a condition is stipulated that does not cause ignorance of profit or cut partnership, such as stipulating loss liability on the mudarib, then such a condition does not make the contract fasid; rather, the condition itself becomes void, like in wakala and mahr contracts where an invalid condition does not invalidate the contract. This general rule is objected to: it is contradicted by the upcoming statement 'and stipulating work on the owner of capital invalidates the contract', because this condition also falls under the general rule, yet it is not a cause of ignorance of profit, but it still invalidates the contract. The answer: yes, this is the case, but 'and other invalid conditions' refers to a condition that does not contradict the essence of the contract. If the condition contradicts the essence, then it also invalidates the contract, because the legality of the contract is only to establish its essence. This is the answer of Sahib al-Nihaya. Sahib al-Inaya answered: Sahib al-Hidayah said 'and other invalid conditions do not invalidate it', and when the condition of work on the owner of capital is made, then it is no longer a mudaraba, and it is established that negation of a thing from a non-existent is permissible. Thus this statement is correct. 'The non-existent is not sighted [؟]', and his saying after this: 'and stipulating work on the owner of capital invalidates the contract' means it prevents its realization.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage presents a general rule (qawida kulliyya) for mudaraba contracts: Conditions that cause ignorance (jahalah) in the profit share or cut the partnership between the parties invalidate the entire mudaraba contract (make it fasid). Examples include an ambiguous profit share stated disjunctively (half or one-third) or a fixed amount for one party (which cuts the partnership). Conversely, conditions that do not cause jahalah or cut partnership, such as stipulating that the mudarib bears losses, do not invalidate the contract; only the condition itself becomes void, analogous to wakala and mahr. However, an exception arises: the later ruling in Al-Hidayah states that 'stipulating work on the owner of capital invalidates the contract.' This condition does not involve jahalah in profit, yet it invalidates. The text provides two responses. First, from Sahib al-Nihaya: The general rule's phrase 'other invalid conditions' refers to conditions that do not oppose the essence of the contract (muqtada al-aqd). The condition of work on the owner opposes the essence of mudaraba (which is that capital is from one side and work from the other), so it invalidates. Second, from Sahib al-Inaya: The statement 'other invalid conditions do not invalidate it' applies only when the mudaraba remains intact; but when the condition of work on the owner is made, the contract ceases to be a mudaraba, so it is not a case of invalid condition but of non-existence of the contract. Thus, negating a ruling from a non-existent contract is valid (i.e., the statement does not apply). The passage ends with Arabic: 'The non-existent is not blind' – a saying to illustrate that negation from non-existence is permissible.

Key Terms
قاعدة كلية (qāʿida kulliyya): A comprehensive legal principle that applies to a set of similar cases; here it governs which conditions invalidate a mudaraba.
موجب العقد (mūjib al-ʿaqd): The essential legal effect of a contract; for mudaraba, it is partnership in profit. Conditions that contradict this invalidate the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following conditions would invalidate a mudaraba contract according to the general rule?
A) Stipulating that the mudarib bears losses.
B) Stipulating a fixed profit amount for the capital owner.
C) Stipulating that the mudarib must work during business hours.
D) Stipulating that the mudarib may invest in any asset class.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi general rule for mudaraba conditions: only conditions causing jahalah in profit or cutting partnership invalidate the contract; other invalid conditions merely become void, except when they oppose the contract's essence.

Liability for Loss in Fasid Mudaraba: The Mudarib as Amin
Dispute on mudarib's liability in fasid mudaraba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the mudarib's liability in a fasid mudaraba and identify the condition under which liability arises according to the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In a fasid mudaraba, the mudarib remains an amin – not liable for loss unless negligent.

This passage examines the mudarib's liability (daman) for the capital in a fasid (defective) mudaraba. While the default rule is trusteeship (amanah), there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds the mudarib is not liable, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold him liable if the loss results from an avoidable cause. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the school balances contractual validity with practical fairness.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify the default ruling stated at the beginning of the passage: the mudarib is not liable (ghayr madmun) for destruction of the capital. Note that this is also the view of the 'three imams' (the other founders).
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage then presents conflicting views: from Imam Muhammad via Ibn Sama'a that he is liable in all cases, and from the Sahibayn that he is liable only if the loss is due to an avoidable cause. Attribute each view correctly.
The Sahibayn's position is often considered a compromise.
3
Analyze the basis for trusteeship
Why is the mudarib considered an amin? The passage gives two reasons: (1) the same ruling applies in a valid mudaraba, and (2) the capital is in his possession as a hired thing (ajr), making him a trustee. Understand the qiyas to valid mudaraba.
This is a qiyas jaliy: asl is valid mudaraba, far' is fasid mudaraba, illa is the mudarib being an amin.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage attributes the view of non-liability unless negligence to al-Tahawi, which harmonizes the positions. This is the operative ruling for fatwa. Know the authority weight: zahir riwayah with nawadir.
Al-Tahawi's view is a tarjih that aligns with the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله غير مضمون بالهلاك ... مضاربت فاسدہ مین جو مال مضارب کے قبضہ میں ہے اگر وہ تلف ہو جائے تو اس کا ضامن نہ ہو گا ۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔ کیونکہ مضاربت صحیح میں یہی حکم ہے۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ وہ مال تو اس کے قبضہ میں اجارہ پر لی ہوئی چیز ہے یعنی وہ امین ہے۔ لیکن مبسوط میں امام محمد سے ابن سماعہ کی روایت ہے کہ وہ ضامن ہوگا۔ اور بعض نے یہ بھی کہا ہے کہ جو ہم منمان مذکور ہے۔ وہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ضامن ہوگا۔ جب کہ وہ ایسے سبب سے تلف ہو۔ جس سے احتراز ممکن ہے ۔ وهذا قول الطحاوی
His saying: 'not guaranteed by destruction...' - In a fasid mudaraba, the capital that is in the possession of the mudarib, if it is destroyed, he will not be guarantor (damin). The three imams also hold this view, because this is the same ruling in a valid mudaraba. Also because the capital is in his possession as a hired thing, meaning he is an amin (trustee). But in al-Mabsut, from Imam Muhammad via Ibn Sama'a, it is narrated that he will be damin. And some have said that what is mentioned [؟] is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he will be damin if it is destroyed due to a cause from which avoidance was possible. And this is the saying of al-Tahawi.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage discusses the mudarib's liability (daman) for the capital in a fasid mudaraba. The main ruling stated is that the mudarib is not liable (damin) for loss or destruction of the capital, similar to a valid mudaraba where he is an amin (trustee). The three other school imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) agree. However, there are conflicting narrations. According to al-Mabsut, from Imam Muhammad via Ibn Sama'a, the mudarib is liable. Some hold that this (non-liability) is Imam Abu Hanifa's view, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he is liable if the loss occurs due to a cause that could have been avoided (tafrit or negligence). This last view is also attributed to al-Tahawi. The passage thus presents multiple positions: the preferred view (mufta bihi) is likely the non-liability unless negligence, as that harmonizes the narrations. The practical effect: the mudarib in a fasid mudaraba is not automatically liable for loss, but if he fails to exercise care, he becomes liable.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage to property held in trust; here it means the mudarib is not automatically liable.
أمين (amīn): A person trusted with property, not liable for accidental loss or destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid mudaraba, under which circumstance does the mudarib become liable for the capital according to the Sahibayn?
A) If he earns no profit.
B) If he commits a violation or negligence (tafrit).
C) If the capital is destroyed by an earthquake.
D) He is never liable.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib in a fasid mudaraba is not automatically liable for loss; liability arises only from negligence or an avoidable cause.

Exclusive Possession: The Fundamental Condition for Mudaraba Validity
Condition for mudaraba validity: exclusive possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of exclusive possession (khulūṣ al-yad) required for a valid mudaraba and explain the rationale distinguishing it from shirkah.

Core Idea
Exclusive possession of capital by mudarib is essential; owner's retention of control invalidates the contract.

In mudaraba, the capital owner provides funds while the mudarib provides labour. For the mudarib to effectively trade, he must have sole authority over the capital. This lesson unpacks that condition, its justification, and how it contrasts with partnership (shirkah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the passage: it states that for mudaraba validity, capital must be handed over exclusively to the mudarib, leaving the capital owner with no possession (yad) in the capital.
2
Understand the rationale
The capital is a trust (amānah) in the mudarib's hand, so it must be fully entrusted. In mudaraba, capital is from one side and work from the other, so the worker must have exclusive control to transact.
This is a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī).
3
Distinguish from shirkah
In shirkah, both sides contribute capital and work, so exclusive control for one is not required; stipulating it invalidates the partnership.
Contrast the two contract types.
4
Apply to special cases
The ruling applies whether the owner is a party (adult) or not (minor). If a guardian retains control, mudaraba is invalid. Also, if partners in mufāwaḍa or ʿinān give mudaraba to each other and stipulate work on the partner-owner, it is invalid due to retained ownership.
Ownership blocks exclusive possession.
5
Note the exception
A father or guardian of a minor can validly be stipulated to work because they are qualified to take the property as mudaraba themselves (i.e., they can act as mudarib).
Exception to the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صحت مضاربت کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ مضارب کو راس المال پورے طور پر سپر د کر دیا گیا اور رب المال کا کسی قسم کا قبضہ تصرف نہ ہو قَالَ وَلَابُدَّ أنْ يَكُونَ الْمَالُ مُسْلَمًا إِلَى الْمُضَارِبِ وَلَايَدَ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ فِيهِ لِأَنَّ الْمَالَ أَمَانَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ فَلَابُدَّ مِنَ التَسْلِيمِ إِلَيْهِ وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ الشِّرْكَة لِاَنَّ الْمَالَ فِى الْمُضَارَبَةِ مِنْ اَحَدِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ وَالْعَمَلُ مِنَ الْجَانِبِ الْآخَرِ فَلَابُدَّ مِنْ اَنْ يَخْلُصَ الْمَالُ لِلْعَامِلِ لِيَتَمَكَّنَ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ فِيْهِ أَمَّا الْعَمَلُ فِي الشَّرْكَةِ مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ فَلَوْ شَرَطَ خُلُوصَ الْيَدِ لِاحْدِهِمَا لَمْ تَنْعَقِدِ الشَّرُكَةُ وَشَرْطُ الْعَمَلِ عَلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ مُفْسِدٌ لِلْعَقْدِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمْنَعُ خُلُوصَ يَدِ الْمُصَارِبِ فَلَا يَتَمَكَّنَ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ الْمَقْصُودُ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ الْمَالِكُ عَاقِدًا اَوْ غَيْرَ عَاقِدٍ كَالصَّغِير لاَ يَدَ الْمَالِكِ ثَابِتٌ لَهُ وَبَقَاءُ يَدِهِ يَمْنَعُ التَّسْلِيمَ إِلَى الْمُصَارِبِ وَكَذَا أَحَدُ الْمُتَفَاوَضَيْن وَاَحَدُ شَريكى الْعِنَانِ إِذَا دَفَعَ الْمَالَ مُضَارَبَةً وَشَرَطَ عَمَلَ صَاحِبِهِ لِقِيَامِ الْمِلْكِ لَهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عَاقِدًا وَإِشْتِرَاطُ الْعَمَلِ عَلَى الْعَاقِدِ مَعَ الْمُصَارِبِ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَالِكِ يُفْسِدُه إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ أَهْل الْمُضَارَبَةِ فِيهِ كَالْمَادُون  ِبخِلَافِ الآب وَالْوَصِى لأنَّهُمَا مِنْ أَهْل أنْ يَأخُذَا مَالَ الصَّغِير مُضَارَبَةً بِأَنْفُسِهِمَا فَكَذَا اشْتِرَاطُهُ عَلَيْهِمَا بِجُزْءٍ مِنَ الْمَالِ
For the validity of mudaraba, it is necessary that the capital is fully handed over to the mudarib and that the capital owner has no form of possession or control over it. He said: It is necessary that the capital is handed over to the mudarib and the capital owner has no hand in it, because the capital is a trust in his hand, so it must be handed over to him. This is unlike partnership (shirkah), because in mudaraba the capital is from one side and the work from the other, so it is necessary for the capital to be exclusively for the worker so that he can dispose of it. As for work in shirkah, it is from both sides, so if exclusive control were stipulated for one of them, the partnership would not be formed. And stipulating work on the capital owner invalidates the contract because it prevents the exclusive control of the mudarib, so he cannot dispose, and thus the objective is not achieved, whether the owner is a party to the contract or not, like a minor, who has no hand; the owner's hand remains and prevents handing over to the mudarib. Similarly, one of the partners in mufawada or inan, if he gives capital as mudaraba and stipulates the work of his partner (the capital owner), because ownership remains with him, even if he is not a party to the contract. And stipulating work on a party who is not the owner, along with the mudarib, invalidates it if he is not qualified for mudaraba therein, like a minor. Unlike the father and trustee, because they are qualified to take the property of a minor as mudaraba themselves, so stipulating it on them with a share of the capital is valid.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is an Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah (with Urdu heading) asserting a fundamental condition for mudaraba validity: the mudarib must have exclusive possession (yad khulis) over the capital. The capital owner cannot retain any control. This distinguishes mudaraba from shirkah (partnership), where both parties contribute capital and work. In mudaraba, because capital comes from one side and work from the other, the worker must have sole power to transact. Stipulating work on the capital owner invalidates the contract because it prevents exclusive mudarib control. The ruling applies whether the owner is a direct party (e.g., an adult) or not (e.g., a minor's property held by guardian). For a minor, the guardian's hand remains, so handing over to the mudarib is not possible. Similarly, if one partner in a mufawada or inan partnership gives partnership capital as mudaraba to the other partner and stipulates work on him, it is invalid because the giver retains ownership. However, if the stipulation is on a non-owner (e.g., the mudarib's agent) who is not qualified for mudaraba, it also invalidates. The exception is for a father or trustee who, being qualified to take the minor's property as mudaraba themselves, validly can be stipulated to work along with the mudarib (i.e., they can act as mudarib themselves with a share).

Key Terms
خلوص اليد (khulūṣ al-yad): Exclusive control and possession over the capital, meaning no other party (especially the capital owner) retains any right to dispose of it.
مفوضة (mufāwaḍa): A type of partnership where partners are equal in capital, work, and liability, and can act on behalf of each other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does stipulating work on the capital owner invalidate a mudaraba contract?
A) Because it creates jahalah in profit.
B) Because it prevents the mudarib from having exclusive control over the capital.
C) Because it increases the work load.
D) Because it reduces the profit share.

Key Takeaway
For a mudaraba to be valid, the mudarib must have exclusive possession of the capital; any retention of control by the capital owner invalidates the contract.

Conditions for a Valid Mudarabah: Exclusive Possession and the Prohibition of Stipulating Work on the Owner
States conditions for valid mudarabah, contrasts with shirkah, and governs stipulations on owner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential conditions for a valid mudarabah and identify which stipulations invalidate the contract according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A mudarabah is valid only when the mudarib has exclusive possession of the capital and the owner does not stipulate his own work.

This passage from al-Hidayah explains the foundational conditions for a valid mudarabah contract. It contrasts mudarabah with shirkah and addresses common stipulations that could break the contract. By understanding these rules, you will see why the Hanafi school places such emphasis on the mudarib's exclusive control over the capital.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage and extract the two key conditions for mudarabah validity: exclusive possession by the mudarib and no stipulation of work on the owner (rabb al-mal).
2
Understand why exclusive possession is necessary
Note the contrast with shirkah: in mudarabah, work comes only from the mudarib, so he must have full control of the capital to trade effectively.
In shirkah, both parties work, so exclusive possession would prevent the other from contributing.
3
Recognize why stipulating work on the owner invalidates the contract
If the owner retains any right to work or control, the mudarib's possession is not exclusive, undermining the contract's purpose.
This applies whether the owner is the contractor or not (e.g., a child whose guardian contracts).
4
Note the exceptions and extensions
The passage discusses cases where the person stipulating work is a father or executor (valid) vs. an authorized slave (invalid), and also a benefit where partial owner work does not invalidate if not exclusive.
Also covers when a partner in shirkah gives mudarabah to a third party and stipulates his partner's work.
