شرط عمل کا مفسد عقد ہونا تو اس وقت ہے جب پورا عمل اسی کے لئے مشروط ہو کہ اس صورت میں مال مضارب کے سپرد نہ ہوگا ( ذخیرہ)۔ قوله واشتراط العمل على العاقد.... الخ - ایک شخص جو عاقد ہے اور مال کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ اس نے مضارب کے ساتھ اپنے کام کرنے کی شرط کی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ عاقد مذکور اس مال میں اہل مضاربت سے ہوگا یا نہیں۔ اگر وہ اہل مضاربت سے ہو جیسے باپ نے یا وصی نے صغیر کا مال مضار بت پر دیا اور مضارب کے ساتھ اپنے کام کرنے کی شرط لگائی تو جائز ہے اور اگر وہ اہل مضاربت سے نہ ہو جیسے عبد مازون
Mudarabah: And this is contrary to shirkah. Because in mudarabah, wealth comes from one side and work from the other. So it is necessary for the worker that the wealth be exclusively his, so that he can dispose of it. As for the work in shirkah, it comes from both sides. So if exclusive possession of one is stipulated, shirkah will not be contracted. And stipulating work on the owner of capital is invalidative of the contract, because this prevents the mudarib's exclusive possession, so he will not control disposal and the objective will not be achieved, whether the owner is the contractor or not, like a child. Because the owner's possession over the wealth remains established, and the continuation of his possession prevents handing over to the mudarib. Similarly, if in shirkah mufawadah or shirkah 'inan, one partner gave wealth on mudarabah and stipulated the work of his partner, due to his ownership remaining, even if he is not the contractor, stipulating work on the contractor along with the mudarib while he is not the owner is invalidative of the contract, provided he is not among those eligible for mudarabah in this wealth, like an authorized slave, contrary to a father and executor, because they themselves can take the wealth of a minor on mudarabah, so likewise stipulating work on them in exchange for a portion of profit is valid. Translation: And it is necessary that the wealth be handed over to the mudarib without any possession of the owner, because the wealth is a trust in his possession [?]. Explanation: ... His saying: 'And it is necessary that...' For the validity of mudarabah, it is also necessary that the capital be fully handed over to the mudarib and that the owner have no kind of possession or disposal in it. Because the wealth is a trust in the mudarib's possession, so just as it is necessary to hand over a deposit to the depositary, similarly it is necessary to hand over the capital to the mudarib. His saying: 'And this is contrary to shirkah...' The mentioned ruling is contrary to shirkah, i.e., in the case of shirkah, it is not a condition that wealth be given only to one partner. The reason is that in mudarabah, wealth comes from the owner and work from the mudarib, and the mudarib can only work when the wealth is in his possession without interference from another. As for shirkah, work comes from both sides. So if in shirkah exclusive possession of one is stipulated, the shirkah will not be contracted, i.e., work from the non-possessing party will not be possible. His saying: 'And stipulating work on the owner...' If in mudarabah work is stipulated on the owner, the contract becomes invalid. Because this condition prevents the mudarib's exclusive possession, so he cannot control disposal, and thus the objective of mudarabah is not achieved, whether the owner is the contractor or not, like when a child's wealth is given on mudarabah, his possession must also be removed, otherwise the objective will not be achieved, because the owner's possession remains established, and the continuation of his possession prevents handing over to the mudarib. So the mudarabah becomes invalid. Similarly, if in shirkah mu'awadah or shirkah 'inan, one partner gave wealth [to someone] on mudarabah, it becomes invalid. Similarly, if in shirkah mufawadah or shirkah 'inan, one partner gave wealth to someone on mudarabah and stipulated with the mudarib the work of his partner, then also the mudarabah becomes invalid, because the partner's possession over the wealth remains, even if he did not contract the mudarabah. Benefit... Qadi 'Asim al-'Amiri narrated from Faqih Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Darir that if the owner made the condition for himself that 'whenever I wish I will dispose of the wealth alone, and when the mudarib gets an opportunity he will dispose alone', then this condition does not invalidate the mudarabah; it remains valid. The invalidity of stipulating work on the owner is only when the entire work is conditioned on him, because in that case the wealth will not be handed over to the mudarib (from al-Dhakhirah). His saying: 'And stipulating work on the contractor...' A person who is the contractor and not the owner of the wealth stipulated his own work with the mudarib. This has two cases: whether that contractor is eligible for mudarabah in this wealth or not. If he is eligible, like when a father or executor gave the wealth of a minor on mudarabah and stipulated his own work with the mudarib, it is valid. And if he is not eligible, like an authorized slave.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the conditions for a valid mudarabah contract as per the Hanafi school. It opens by contrasting mudarabah with shirkah (partnership): in mudarabah, capital comes from one party (rabb al-mal) and labor from the other (mudarib), so exclusive possession of capital by the mudarib is necessary for him to trade effectively. In shirkah, both parties contribute work, so exclusive possession by one is not required; indeed, stipulating it would prevent the other from working. The core ruling: stipulating work on the rabb al-mal invalidates the mudarabah because it compromises the mudarib's exclusive control over the capital, thwarting the contract's purpose of profit through trade. This applies whether the owner is the actual contractor or not (e.g., a child whose guardian contracts). The text then extends this to cases where a partner in a shirkah gives capital to a third party on mudarabah and stipulates his partner's work; the mudarib's exclusive possession is also compromised, invalidating the contract. An exception is noted: if the one stipulating work is the father or executor of a minor, it is valid because they are eligible to take the minor's capital themselves for mudarabah; their stipulation is akin to their own participation. The passage also cites a benefit from al-Dhakhirah: a condition allowing the owner to also trade alone does not invalidate the contract, as long as the condition does not reserve all work for the owner. Finally, it distinguishes between an authorized slave (who cannot validly stipulate his own work because his possession is like the owner's) and a father/executor (who can).

Key Terms
مضاربت (mudarabah): A contract where one party provides capital (rabb al-mal) and the other provides labor (mudarib) for trade, with profit shared as agreed.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of capital who provides funds for mudarabah and is not to work in the business.
عبد ماذون (abd ma'dhun): A slave who is granted permission by his master to engage in trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mudarabah contract, why does stipulating work on the rabb al-mal invalidate the contract according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the rabb al-mal is not allowed to do any work.
B) Because it prevents the mudarib from having exclusive possession of the capital.
C) Because the rabb al-mal must be the only one working.
D) Because it changes the contract into a partnership.

Key Takeaway
A valid mudarabah requires that the mudarib have exclusive possession of the capital and that no work be stipulated on the owner, with exceptions for those who are themselves eligible to act as mudarib.

Permissible Actions for Mudarib in Absolute Mudarabah
Lists actions permissible for mudarib and discusses travel dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six permissible actions for a mudarib in an absolute mudarabah and explain the conditions under which travel is permitted or prohibited.

Core Idea
An absolute mudarabah grants the mudarib all customary trade actions, but travel may be restricted if capital is given in the mudarib's own town.

In an absolute mudarabah (unrestricted partnership), the mudarib is empowered to engage in all activities customary among merchants to generate profit. This lesson enumerates those actions—selling, buying, agency, deposit, bida'a, and travel—and examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the mudarib's right to travel with the capital. You will learn the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) and the reasoning behind the qualifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
2
List the six permissible actions
The commentary adds other customary actions like pledges and leasing.
3
Understand the justifications
An analogy with the depositor's right to travel also supports.
4
Examine the travel dispute
The relied-upon view (al-zahir) in al-Hidayah generally permits travel with this qualification.
5
Determine the mufta bihi

وہ امور جو مضارب کے لئے جائز یا نا جائز ہیں
قَالَ وَإِذَا صَحْتِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ مُطْلَقَةً جَازَ لِلْمُضَارِبِ أَنْ يَبِيعَ وَيَشْتَرِى وَيُوَ كِلُ وَيُسَا فِرُوَ يُبْضِعُ وَيُوَدِعُ لاطلاقِ الْعَقْدِ وَالْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهُ الْاِسْتَرْ بَاحُ وَلَا يَتَحَصَّلُ إِلَّا بِا َلتِجَارَةِ فَيَنْتَظِمُ الْعَقْدُ صُنُوقَ التِّجَارَةِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنْ صَنِيعِ التِّجَارِوَ التَّوْكِيلُ مِنْ صَنِيْعِهِمْ وَكَذَا الْإِبْدَاعُ وَالْإِبْصَاعُ وَالْمُسَافَرَةُ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْمُوْدَع لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ فَالْمُضَارِبُ أَوْلَى كَيْفَ وَإِنَّ اللَّفْظَ دَلِيْلٌ عَلَيْهِ لَا نَّهَا مُسْتَقَةٌ مِنَ الضَّرْبِ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَهُوَ السَّيْرُ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ وَعَنْهُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ أَنَّهُ إِنْ دَفَعَ فِي بَلَدِهِ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ بِهِ لَا نَّهُ تَعْرِيض عَلَى الْهَلَاكِ مِنْ غَيْرِ ضَرُورَةٍ فَإِنْ دَفَعَ فِي غَيْرِ بَلَدِهِ لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ إِلَى بَلَدِهِ لَا نَّهُ هُوَ الْمُرَادُ فِي الْغَالِبِ وَالظَّاهِرُ مَا ذُكِرَ فِي الْكِتَابِ
ترجمہ جب مضاربت مطلق ٹھہر جائے تو جائز ہے مضارب کے لئے خرید و فروخت اور وکیل کرنا، سفر کرنا، بضاعت پر دینا، ودیعت رکھنا، اطلاق عقد کی وجہ سے اور مقصود اس سے نفع حاصل کرنا ہے جو نہیں ملتا مگر تجارت سے پس یہ عقد تمام اقسام تجارت کو شامل ہوگا۔ اور ان کو بھی جو مصنیع تجار سے ہیں اور وکیل کرنا صنیع تجار میں سے ہے۔ اسی طرح ودیعت رکھنا، بضاعت پر دینا اور سفر کرنا کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ مودع کو سفر میں لے جانے کا اختیار ہے تو مضارب کو بطریق اولی یہ اختیار ہوگا اور کیسے نہ ہو۔ حالانکہ لفظ خود اس کی دلیل ہے۔ کیونکہ مضاربت ضرب فی الارض سے مشتق ہے اور وہ سیر وسفر کرنا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی کہ اگر مالک نے مضارب کے شہر میں مال دیا ہو تو اس کو لے کر سفر نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو بلاضرورت تلف پر پیش کرنا ہے۔ اور اگر اس کے شہر کے علاوہ میں دیا ہو تو اس کو اپنے شہر کی طرف سفر کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ غالب مراد یہی ہوتی ہے اور ظاہر وہی ہے جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔
تشریح قوله واذا صبحت یہاں سے ان امور کا بیان ہے جو مضارب کے لئے جائز یا نا جائز ہیں۔ سواگر عقد مضاربت کسی مکان و زمان اور تصرف خاص کے ساتھ مفید نہ ہو بلکہ مطلق ہو تو مضارب کے لئے وہ تمام امور جائز ہیں جو تجار کے یہاں معتاد ہوں۔ جیسے ہاتھ درہاتھ یا ادھار خرید و فروخت کرنا ( ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک بلا اجازت ادھار نہیں بچ سکتا) وکیل بنانا، سفر کرنا بطریق بضاعت مال دینا کسی کے پاس مال ودیعت رکھنا، گروی لینا، گروی رکھنا، کرایہ پر لینا، کرایہ پر دینا وغیرہ۔ کیونکہ یہ سب امور سوداگروں کے یہاں معتاد ہیں اور تجارت کے سلسلہ میں ان کی ضرورت واقع ہوتی ہے۔ نیز مضاربت کا مقصد یہی ہیکہ نفع حاصل ہو اور یہ تجارت کے بغیر نہیں ہوسکتا لہذا عقد مذکور تجارت کے جملہ اقسام کو شامل ہوگا۔
Matters that are permissible or impermissible for the mudarib: He said: And when the mudarabah is valid as absolute, it is permissible for the mudarib to sell, buy, appoint an agent, travel, give as bida'a, and deposit, due to the absoluteness of the contract. And the objective from it is profit, which is only obtained through trade. So the contract encompasses the various types of trade and what is customary for merchants. Appointment of an agent is among their customs, likewise deposit, bida'a, and travel. Do you not see that the depositor has the right to travel? So the mudarib has even more right. Moreover, the word itself indicates it, because mudarabah is derived from 'darb fi al-ard', which is travel. And from Abu Yusuf that he has no right to travel. And from him from Abu Hanifa that if [the owner] gave [the capital] in his own town, he may not travel with it, because it is exposing [the capital] to destruction without necessity. But if he gave in a town other than his own, he may travel to his own town, because that is what is usually intended. And the apparent [position] is what is mentioned in the book. Translation: When the mudarabah is absolute, it is permissible for the mudarib to buy, sell, appoint an agent, travel, give as bida'a, deposit, due to the absoluteness of the contract, and the objective is profit, which is only obtained through trade. So this contract includes all types of trade and what is customary for merchants. Appointment of an agent is among their customs, likewise deposit, bida'a, and travel. Do you not see that the depositor has the right to travel? So the mudarib has even more right. And how could it not be, while the word itself is evidence for it, because mudarabah is derived from 'darb fi al-ard', which is travel. Imam Abu Yusuf narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that if the owner gave the capital in the mudarib's town, he may not travel with it, because it is exposing to destruction without necessity. But if he gave in a town other than his own, he may travel to his own town, because that is usually the intended meaning. And the apparent [position] is what is mentioned in the book. Explanation: His saying 'and when the mudarabah is valid' – from here begins the explanation of matters permissible or impermissible for the mudarib. So if the mudarabah contract is not restricted to a specific place, time, or specific transaction, but is absolute, then all matters that are customary among merchants are permissible for the mudarib, such as spot or credit sales (according to the three imams, credit without permission is not permissible), appointing an agent, traveling, giving as bida'a, depositing, taking and giving as pledge, leasing, etc. Because all these matters are customary among merchants and necessary in the course of trade. Also, the objective of mudarabah is profit, and this cannot be achieved without trade, so the said contract includes all types of trade.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the actions permissible for a mudarib under an absolute (unrestricted) mudarabah contract. It begins with the Arabic matn from al-Hidayah: when the mudarabah is valid as absolute (not restricted by time, place, or specific transactions), the mudarib may sell, buy, appoint agents, travel, give goods as bida'a (a type of consignment), and deposit goods for safekeeping. The justification is that the contract's purpose—profit—is achieved only through trade, and these actions are customary among merchants. The text emphasizes that the very word 'mudarabah' derives from 'darb fi al-ard' (striking the earth), implying travel for trade. The commentary adds that all customary merchant activities like credit sales, pledges, and leases are included, provided the owner does not restrict the contract. The passage then records an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding travel: Imam Abu Yusuf reports that Abu Hanifa held that if the capital is given in the mudarib's own town, he may not travel with it because it unnecessarily risks destruction. However, if the capital is given in a different town, he may travel back to his own town as that is usually the intended purpose. The relied-upon position (al-zahir) is the one mentioned in the book (al-Hidayah), which permits travel in absolute terms, but with the qualification for the case of the mudarib's town.

Key Terms
مضاربت مطلقہ (mudarabah mutlaqah): An absolute mudarabah contract without restrictions on time, place, or type of trade.
بضاعت (bida'a): A consignment or goods given to someone to sell without a specific commission arrangement.
ضرب فی الارض (darb fi al-ard): Literally 'striking the earth', meaning traveling for trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He may travel freely.

C) He may travel only if the owner agrees in advance.

Key Takeaway
In absolute mudarabah, the mudarib may perform all customary trade actions, but travel is prohibited if the capital was given in his own town.

Permissible Actions for the Mudarib in a General Mudarabah
Explains which actions are permitted for the mudarib in an unrestricted mudarabah contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default permissibility of actions for the mudarib in a general mudarabah and identify the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding travel.

Core Idea
In a general mudarabah, the mudarib may do all customary trade actions, including travel, because the contract's purpose is profit.

This passage from Al-Hidayah sets out the scope of the mudarib's authority when the contract is unrestricted. It explains why certain actions are permissible by default and addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement about travel. By understanding this, you will appreciate how the Hanafi school uses customary practice and linguistic derivation to define contractual terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The text lists actions explicitly permitted for the mudarib in a general mudarabah: selling, buying, appointing an agent, traveling, giving as bida', and depositing.
These are the core permissible actions.
2
Understand the rationale
The contract is absolute (mutlaq) and its purpose is profit, which is only achieved through trade. Therefore, the contract includes all types of trade and customary practices of traders.
The rationale ties permissibility to the contract's purpose.
3
Locate the proofs
The proofs are: (1) linguistic derivation of 'mudarabah' from 'darb fi al-ard' (traveling), (2) analogy with the depositary who may travel with a deposit, and (3) customary practice of traders.
These proofs support the permissibility of travel and other actions.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and a narration from Abu Hanifa restrict travel, arguing it risks destruction without necessity. The opposed view is that travel is permitted absolutely because it is customary and implied by the word mudarabah.
This dispute shows the internal scholarly debate within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the tarjih
The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is absolute permission for travel, as stated in the matn. This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih is based on the authority of the matn and consistency with the contract's purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وہ امور جو مضارب کے لئے جائز یا نا جائز ہیں
قَالَ وَإِذَا صَحْتِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ مُطْلَقَةً جَازَ لِلْمُضَارِبِ أَنْ يَبِيعَ وَيَشْتَرِى وَيُوَ كِلُ وَيُسَا فِرُوَ يُبْضِعُ وَيُوَدِعُ لِاطلاقِ الْعَقْدِ وَالْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهُ الْاِسْتَرْ بَاحُ وَلَا يَتَحَصَّلُ إِلَّا بِا َلتِجَارَةِ فَيَنْتَظِمُ الْعَقْدُ صُنُوفَ التِّجَارَةِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنْ صَنِيعِ التِّجَارِ وَالتَّوْكِيلُ مِنْ صَنِيْعِهِمْ وَكَذَا الْإِبْدَاعُ وَالْإِبْصَاعُ وَالْمُسَافَرَةُ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْمُوْدَعَ لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ فَالْمُضَارِبُ أَوْلَى كَيْفَ وَإِنَّ اللَّفْظَ دَلِيْلٌ عَلَيْهِ لَا نَّهَا مُشْتَقَّةٌ مِنَ الضَّرْبِ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَهُوَ السَّيْرُ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ وَعَنْهُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ أَنَّهُ إِنْ دَفَعَ فِي بَلَدِهِ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ بِهِ لَا نَّهُ تَعْرِيضٌ عَلَى الْهَلَاكِ مِنْ غَيْرِ ضَرُورَةٍ فَإِنْ دَفَعَ فِي غَيْرِ بَلَدِهِ لَهُ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ إِلَى بَلَدِهِ لَا نَّهُ هُوَ الْمُرَادُ فِي الْغَالِبِ وَالظَّاهِرُ مَا ذُكِرَ فِي الْكِتَابِ
ترجمہ: جب مضاربت مطلق ٹھہر جائے تو جائز ہے مضارب کے لئے خرید و فروخت اور وکیل کرنا، سفر کرنا، بضاعت پر دینا، ودیعت رکھنا، اطلاق عقد کی وجہ سے اور مقصود اس سے نفع حاصل کرنا ہے جو نہیں ملتا مگر تجارت سے پس یہ عقد تمام اقسام تجارت کو شامل ہوگا۔ اور ان کو بھی جو مصنیع تجار سے ہیں اور وکیل کرنا صنیع تجار میں سے ہے۔ اسی طرح ودیعت رکھنا، بضاعت پر دینا اور سفر کرنا کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ مودع کو سفر میں لے جانے کا اختیار ہے تو مضارب کو بطریق اولی یہ اختیار ہوگا اور کیسے نہ ہو۔ حالانکہ لفظ خود اس کی دلیل ہے۔ کیونکہ مضاربت ضرب فی الارض سے مشتق ہے اور وہ سیر وسفر کرنا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی کہ اگر مالک نے مضارب کے شہر میں مال دیا ہو تو اس کو لے کر سفر نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو بلا ضرورت تلف پر پیش کرنا ہے۔ اور اگر اس کے شہر کے علاوہ میں دیا ہو تو اس کو اپنے شہر کی طرف سفر کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ غالب مراد یہی ہوتی ہے اور ظاہر وہی ہے جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔
تشریح: قوله واذا صحت: یہاں سے ان امور کا بیان ہے جو مضارب کے لئے جائز یا نا جائز ہیں۔ سواگر عقد مضاربت کسی مکان و زمان اور تصرف خاص کے ساتھ مفید نہ ہو بلکہ مطلق ہو تو مضارب کے لئے وہ تمام امور جائز ہیں جو تجار کے یہاں معتاد ہوں۔ جیسے ہاتھ درہاتھ یا ادھار خرید و فروخت کرنا (ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک بلا اجازت ادھار نہیں بچ سکتا) وکیل بنانا، سفر کرنا بطریق بضاعت مال دینا کسی کے پاس مال ودیعت رکھنا، گروی لینا، گروی رکھنا، کرایہ پر لینا، کرایہ پر دینا وغیرہ۔ کیونکہ یہ سب امور سوداگروں کے یہاں معتاد ہیں اور تجارت کے سلسلہ میں ان کی ضرورت واقع ہوتی ہے۔ نیز مضاربت کا مقصد یہی ہے کہ نفع حاصل ہو اور یہ تجارت کے بغیر نہیں ہوسکتا لہذا عقد مذکور تجارت کے جملہ اقسام کو شامل ہوگا۔
(اشرف الہدایہ جلد - یازدهم .. ۱۴۸)
قوله وعن ابی یوسف .... الخ - امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ مضارب کو مال لے کر سفر کرنا جائز نہیں۔ یعنی وہ مال جس میں دیا ہو تو اس کو لے کر سفر کا اختیار نہیں اھ۔ لیکن ظاہر الروایہ وہی ہے جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے کہ علی الاطلاق سفر کی اجازت ہے۔ بار برداری اور خرچہ پڑتا ہو۔ بناءً على قوله في الوديعة ( مبسوط اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ اگر مالک نے مضارب کو مال اس کے شہر یا [؟]
The matters that are permissible or impermissible for the mudarib: He said: When a general mudarabah is valid, it is permissible for the mudarib to sell, buy, appoint an agent, travel, give as bida', and deposit, due to the absolute nature of the contract. The purpose is profit, which is only attained through trade, so the contract includes all types of trade and what is of the practice of traders. Appointing an agent is from their practice, similarly deposit, bida', and travel. Do you not see that the depositor can travel, so the mudarib is even more entitled. How so? Because the word itself indicates it, as it is derived from 'striking in the land' which is travel. From Abu Yusuf: He may not travel. From him from Abu Hanifa: If capital is given in his city, he may not travel with it because it exposes it to destruction without necessity. If given outside his city, he may travel to his city because that is usually intended. The apparent position is what is mentioned in the book. Translation: When the mudarabah is settled as absolute, it is permissible for the mudarib to buy, sell, appoint an agent, travel, give as bida', deposit, due to the absolute nature of the contract... Commentary: From here begins the explanation of matters permissible or impermissible for the mudarib...
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof clarifying the scope of the mudarib's authority in a general (mutlaq) mudarabah contract. The author first states the default rule: when the mudarabah is unrestricted, the mudarib may engage in all actions customary among traders. These include selling, buying, appointing agents, traveling, giving capital as bida' (entrusting for trade), and depositing. The rationale is that the contract's purpose is profit, which requires trade, and the contract is therefore inclusive of all trade-related acts. The proof is two-fold: (1) the practice of traders, and (2) the linguistic derivation of the word 'mudarabah' from ضرب في الأرض (striking/traveling in the land), which implies travel. The author then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf narrates from Abu Hanifa that travel is not permitted if capital was given in the mudarib's own city, due to risk of loss without necessity. However, if given outside his city, he may travel back to it. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is the absolute permissibility of travel, as stated in the matn. The commentary elaborates that 'mutlaq' means no restriction of time, place, or specific transaction, and that all customary trade practices are included.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership contract where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital and the other (mudarib) provides labor, with profits shared according to agreement.
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner who manages the capital. In this passage, his permitted actions are discussed.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The capital provider, the silent partner in the mudarabah.
ضرب في الأرض (darb fi al-ard): Literally 'striking in the land'; a term used in the Quran (e.g., 73:20) to mean traveling for trade, from which 'mudarabah' is derived.
إبضاع (ibda'): Entrusting capital or goods to someone for trade without a formal mudarabah contract; often a form of agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah), which of the following actions is NOT listed as permissible for the mudarib in a general mudarabah?
A) Selling and buying goods.
B) Traveling with the capital to another city for trade.
C) Giving the capital as a loan (qard) to a third party.
D) Appointing an agent to assist in trade.

Key Takeaway
In a general mudarabah, the mudarib may engage in all customary trade practices, including travel, and this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
When Can a Mudarib Delegate Mudarabah to Another?
States the rule against sub-mudarabah delegation with qiyas evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib delegating a sub-mudarabah and identify when permission or absolute discretion makes it permissible.

Core Idea
A mudarib cannot delegate mudarabah unless the owner explicitly permits or gives absolute discretion.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah establishes a key limitation on the mudarib's authority: he may not sub-contract the capital as a second mudarabah. The ruling is derived via analogy (qiyas) with agency (wakalah) and the principle that a contract cannot contain its like in strength. Understanding this limitation is crucial for proper mudarabah transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling and Exceptions
Read the opening statement: the mudarib may not give the capital as mudarabah unless the owner permits or says 'act according to your opinion.' These are the two exceptions.
2
Understand the Qiyas with Wakalah
The author likens the mudarib to an agent (wakil). An agent cannot appoint another agent for the same task without permission. Similarly, the mudarib cannot sub-contract mudarabah because both contracts are equal in strength.
The maxim 'a thing does not contain its like' is applied.
3
Distinguish Lesser Actions (Ibda', Ida')
The text notes that deposit (ida') and bida' (entrusting goods) are lesser in strength than mudarabah, so they are automatically included within the mudarib's authority. This contrasts with the equal-strength sub-mudarabah.
Lesser actions are contained because they are weaker.
4
Exclude Loans Even with Absolute Discretion
Even if the owner says 'act according to your opinion,' the mudarib cannot give loans. Reason: loans are charity, not trade practice, and do not yield profit. The absolute discretion only covers customary trading acts.
This is a specific exception to the generalization.
5
Apply Restrictions on Location/Commodity
If the owner limits the mudarabah to a specific city or commodity, the mudarib cannot exceed that limit, nor can he delegate to someone who would.
The restriction binds the mudarib's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضارب آگے مضاربت پر مال دے سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟
قَالَ وَلَا يُضَارِبُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَأْذَنَ لَهُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ أَوْ يَقُولُ لَهُ اِعْمَلْ بِرَأيِكَ لِأَنَّ الشَّيْءَ لَا يَتَضَمَّنُ مِثْلَهُ لِتَسَاوِيْهِمَا فِي الْقُوَّةِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّنْصِيصِ عَلَيْهِ أَوِ التَّفْوِيْضِ الْمُطْلَقِ إِلَيْهِ وَكَانَ كَالتَّوْكِيْلِ فَإِنَّ الْوَكِيْلَ لَا يَمْلِكُ أَنْ يُوَكَّلَ غَيْرَهُ فِيْمَا وَكَّلَهُ بِهِ إِلَّا إِذَا قِيلَ لَهُ اعْمَلْ بِرَأيِكَ بِخِلَافِ الْإِبْدَاعِ وَالْإِبْضَاعِ لِأَنَّهُ دُونَهُ فَيَتَضَمَّنَهُ وَبِخِلَافِ الْإِقْرَاضِ حَيْثُ لَا يَمْلِكُهُ وَإِنْ قِيلَ لَهُ اِعْمَلَ بِرَأْيِكَ لِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْهُ التَّعْمِيمُ فِيمَا هُوَ مِنْ صَنِيعِ التَّجَارِ وَلَيْسَ الْإِقْرَاضُ مِنْهُ وَهُوَ تَبَرُّعٌ كَالْهِبَةِ وَالصَّدَقَةِ فَلَا يَحْصُلُ بِهِ الْعَرْضُ وَهُوَ الرِّبْحُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ الزِّيَادَةُ عَلَيْهِ أَمَّا الدَّفْعُ مُضَارَبَةً فَمِنْ صَنِيْعِهِمْ وَكَذَا الشَّرْكَةُ وَالْخَلْطُ بِمَالِ نَفْسِهِ فَيَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ هَذَا الْقَوْلِ
قَالَ. وَإِنْ خَصَّ لَهُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ التَّصَرُّفَ فِى بَلَدِ بَعَيْنِهِ أَوْ فِي سِلْعَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا لَمْ يَجُزُ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَجَاوُزَهَا لِأَنَّهُ تَوْكِيلٌ وَفِي التَّخْصِيصِ فَائِدَةً فَيَتَخَصَّصَ وَكَذَا لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَهُ بِضَاعَةً إِلَى مَنْ يُخْرِجَهَا مِنْ تِلْكَ الْبَلْدَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمْلِكُ الْإِخْرَاجَ بِنَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَمْلِكُ تَفْوِيْضُهُ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ
ترجمہ: اور مضاربت پر نہ دے مگر یہ کہ اجازت دے دے اس کو مالک یا کہہ دے کہ اپنی رائے کے مطابق کام کر، کیونکہ شئی اپنے مثل کو تضمن نہیں ہوتی قوت میں ان دونوں کے برابر ہونے کی وجہ سے پس تصریح یا مطلق تفویض ضروری ہے۔ اور یہ توکیل کی طرح ہو گیا کہ وکیل اس کام میں سرے کو وکیل نہیں کر سکتا جس کے لئے اس کو وکیل کیا گیا ہے۔ مگر جب ہی کہ اس سے پہلے کہا گیا ہو کہ اپنی رائے سے کام کر بخلاف ودیعت رکھنے اور بضاعت دینے کے کیونکہ یہ مضاربت سے کم ہیں تو وہ ان کو شامل ہوگی اور بخلاف قرض دینے کے کہ اس کا بھی اختیار نہیں۔ اگر چہ اس سے کہا گیا ہو کہ اپنی رائے سے کام کر کیونکہ اس سے انہیں امور میں تعمیم مراد ہوتی ہے جو صنع تجار سے ہوں اور قرض دینا ان میں سے نہیں ہے وہ تو ہبہ اور صدقہ کی طرح احسان ہے تو اس سے غرض حاصل نہ ہوگی اور وہ نفع ہے۔ کیونکہ قرض پر کچھ بڑھانا جائز نہیں۔ رہا مضاربت پر دینا سو یہ صنیع تجار میں سے ہے۔ ایسے ہی شرکت اور اپنے مال میں خلط کرنا ہے کہ یہ بھی اس قول کے تحت میں داخل ہوگا۔ اگر تخصیص کر دی مالک نے تصرف کی کسی خاص شہر یا معین اسباب میں تو مضارب کو اس سے تجاوز کرنا جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے کہ یہ توکیل ہے۔ اور تخصیص میں فائدہ بھی ہے تو تخصیص ہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح وہ ایسے شخص کو بضاعت نہیں دے سکتا جو اس کو اس شہر سے باہر لے جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ خود مضارب کو باہر لے جانے کا اختیار نہیں تو دوسرے کو بھی اس کی تفویض نہیں کر سکتا۔
تشریح: قوله ولا يضارب: مضارب کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ دوسرے کو مضاربت پر مال دے دے۔ مگر یہ کہ رب المال سے اس کی تصریح اجازت ہو۔ یا اس نے اپنی راۓ پر کام کا محتا کیا ہو۔ وہ یہ کہ دونوں مضاربتیں قوت میں برابر ہیں اور شئی اپنے مثل و تضمن نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا پہلی مضاربت کے ضمن میں دوسری مضاربت نہیں آئے گی۔
Can the mudarib give capital as mudarabah to someone else? He said: He may not give it as mudarabah unless the owner gives him permission or says 'Act according to your opinion,' because a thing does not contain its like due to their equality in strength. So there must be explicit authorization or absolute delegation. This is like wakalah: an agent cannot appoint another agent for that task unless told 'Act according to your opinion.' Unlike deposit and bida' because they are lesser than mudarabah, so it includes them. And unlike giving a loan, which he may not do even if told 'Act according to your opinion,' because the intended generalization is for what is of the practice of traders, and loan is not from it; it is charity like gift and sadaqah, so the purpose (profit) is not achieved, since increasing it is not permissible. As for giving as mudarabah, it is from their practice. Similarly, partnership and mixing with his own wealth are included under this statement. He said: If the owner specified the transaction to a particular city or a specific commodity, he may not exceed it, because it is an agency and the specification has benefit, so it is restricted. Similarly, he may not give it as bida' to someone who would take it out of that city, because he himself does not have the right to take it out, so he cannot delegate it to another. Translation: And he may not give as mudarabah unless the owner permits him or says 'Act according to your opinion,' because a thing does not contain its like... Commentary: The mudarib does not have authority to give the capital as mudarabah to another unless the owner explicitly permits or gives him absolute discretion. Both mudarabahs are equal in strength, so one cannot be contained within the other.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining that a mudarib cannot sub-contract the capital as a second mudarabah without explicit permission from the capital owner (rabb al-mal) or an absolute delegation ('act according to your opinion'). The reason given is that a thing cannot contain its like—i.e., the first mudarabah contract is of the same kind as a second mudarabah contract, so it is not automatically included. The analogy (qiyas) is with wakalah (agency): an agent cannot appoint another agent for the same task unless told 'act according to your opinion.' However, lesser actions like ibda' (entrusting) and ida' (deposit) are automatically included because they are lower in strength. Loans (iqrad) are not included even with absolute discretion because loans are acts of charity, not commercial practices, and do not yield profit. The passage then addresses a restricted mudarabah (e.g., limited to a specific city or commodity): in that case, the mudarib cannot go beyond the restriction, nor can he delegate to someone who would do so. The commentary emphasizes the key qiyas: 'a thing does not contain its like' is the principle barring delegation of the same level of contract.

Key Terms
تضمن (tadammana): To contain or include something within itself. Here, the principle that a contract cannot contain its like in terms of legal strength.
توکیل (tawkīl): Appointing an agent. The mudarib's position is analogous to that of an agent.
تفویض (tafwīḍ): Delegation of authority. Here, the owner's absolute delegation to the mudarib (e.g., 'act according to your opinion') permits sub-delegation.
بضاعت (biḍā'ah): Goods or capital given to someone to trade with, often without a formal mudarabah contract. It is a lesser form of delegation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the mudarib is given absolute discretion ('act according to your opinion'), which of the following is he still NOT permitted to do?
A) Give the capital as mudarabah to someone else.
B) Entrust the capital as a deposit (ida').
C) Lend the capital to a friend as a loan (qard).
D) Mix the capital with his own funds to form a partnership.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's authority to sub-contract mudarabah requires explicit permission or absolute discretion; otherwise, it is prohibited due to the principle that a contract cannot contain its like.

Mudarib Cannot Delegate Mudarabah or Give Loans
Ruling with proof on mudarib’s restrictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and explain the two restrictions on a mudarib’s authority delegation and lending.

Core Idea
A mudarib acts as an agent, so he cannot delegate his role or lend capital.

In a mudarabah, the mudarib is entrusted with capital for trade. However, his authority is limited to trade-related acts. This lesson explains two key restrictions he cannot appoint another mudarib (delegation) and he cannot lend the capital. The reasoning is rooted in the nature of mudarabah as agency and the definition of trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mudarib’s legal capacity
He is an agent (wakil), not owner. This is the foundation for the restrictions.
Mudarabah includes elements of wikalah.
2
Analyze delegation
By analogy to wikalah, an agent cannot appoint another agent without permission. The mudarib cannot appoint a sub-mudarib.
3
Contrast with lesser inclusions
He can appoint a custodian (wadi’ah) or give goods on commission (bida’ah) because these are lesser acts included in trade.
These are lesser than mudarabah and thus fall within his authority.
4
Analyze lending
Lending (qard) is not trade; it is charity. The mudarib has no authority to lend, even if the owner gives full discretion.
Lending is a contract of benevolence, not commerce.
5
Conclusion
These restrictions protect the capital and the owner’s rights. The mudarib’s liability remains if he violates them.

Source Text

جواب یہاں گفتگو اس تصرف میں ہے جو از راہ نیابت ہو اور مذکورین کا تصرف بحکیم مالکیت ہے نہ کہ بحکم نیابت، اس لئے کی مستعغیر منفعت کا مالک اور مکاتب قبضہ کے لحاظ سے آزاد ہو چکا۔ بخلاف مضارب کے کہ وہ عمل بطریق نیابت کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ مضاربت میں وکالت کے معنی ہوتے ہیں۔ اور وکیل جس کام کے لئے ہوتا ہے اس میں دوسرے کو وکیل نہیں کر سکتا ایسے ہی مضارب دوسرے کو مضارب نہیں کر سکتا۔ بخلاف ودیعت رکھنے یا بضاعت دینے کے کہ یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مضاربت سے کم ہے تو وہ ان کو شامل ہوگی۔

A master can permit his slave even though they are equal in power. The answer: here the discussion is about disposal by way of agency, and the disposal of the mentioned persons is by virtue of ownership, not by way of agency, because the lessor is owner of the benefit and the mukatab has become free in terms of possession. Unlike the mudarib, who acts by way of agency, because mudarabah has the meaning of agency. And an agent cannot appoint another agent for the task for which he is appointed. Similarly, a mudarib cannot appoint another mudarib. Contrary to placing a deposit (wadi'ah) or giving goods on commission (bida'ah), that is permissible because each of these is lesser than mudarabah, so it is included in it. His saying: 'And contrary to lending...' - contrary to giving a loan, the mudarib does not have authority for that, even if the owner said, 'Act on your opinion.' Because by that only those matters are intended which are of the type of trade, and lending is not of the type of trade; rather it is a favor like charity and almsgiving, and taking excess in loan is not permissible.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. It discusses two restrictions on the mudarib's authority. First, the mudarib cannot appoint another mudarib because mudarabah is a form of agency (wikalah), and an agent cannot delegate his agency to another unless permitted by the principal. However, the mudarib may appoint a custodian (wadi') or give goods on commission (bida'ah) because these are lesser acts and are included within the scope of trade. Second, the mudarib cannot lend the capital (qard), even if the owner gave him full discretion, because lending is not a trade transaction; it is an act of charity. Taking interest on a loan is prohibited. The proof is based on the nature of mudarabah as agency and the definition of trade.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner in a mudarabah contract who manages the capital.
قرض (qard): A loan; giving capital to another without expecting profit, as an act of charity.
وکالت (wikalah): Agency; the mudarib acts as an agent for the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mudarib cannot delegate mudarabah or lend capital because his role is that of an agent for trade, not an owner.

Effect of Owner's Specification on Mudarib's Authority
Rules when owner specifies a city or commodity for mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mudarib violates the owner's specification of city or commodity, and explain the analogy with the depositary.

Core Idea
A mudarib who violates the owner's specific instructions becomes liable for the capital, but the contract remains intact — reversal restores the agreement.

In a mudarabah contract, the owner may specify where or what to trade. The mudarib is bound by these specifications. If he violates them, he does not void the contract but incurs personal liability. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof via analogy with the depositary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mudarib's act and ruling
The mudarib takes capital to a non-specified city and buys goods. The ruling: he is a guarantor of the capital, and the purchased goods with profit are his.
The owner's specification is binding.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas on the depositary (wadi'ah). A depositary who violates the deposit becomes liable unless he corrects the violation.
Analogy is based on the shared illa of violation of command.
3
Trace the illa
The illa is violation of the owner's command (mukhalafah) followed by correction. In both cases, liability arises from unauthorized disposal and is removed when the property is returned to its proper state.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that specification invalidates the mudarabah contract itself, not just creates liability.
Hanafi view is that the contract remains valid.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on the analogy and the principle that delegation can be qualified. The contract is not void because specification is a condition of the mudarib's authority, not a pillar of the contract.
Mufta bihi: if mudarib buys after violation, he owns goods and profit but must return capital.

قوله وان خص له الخ - اگر رب المال نے تجارت کے لئے کوئی خاص شہر یا کوئی خاص اسباب معین کر دیا ہو تو مضارب کے لئے اس کے خلاف کرنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ مضارب جو مال میں تصرف کرنے کا مالک ہوتا ہے وہ رب المال کی تفویض سے ہوتا ہے۔ اور رب المال نے تفویض کو امور مذکورہ کے ساتھ خاص کیا ہے جوفائدہ سے خالی نہیں۔ کیونکہ تجارت اختلاف امکنہ وامتعہ کے لحاظ سے مختلف ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے مضارب کو اس کی تفویض کے خلاف کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر رب المال نے ان چیزوں کی تعیین کردی تو مضاربت ہی صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ مضارب رأس المال کو رب المال کے متعین کردہ شہر سے دوسرے شہر لے جاسکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ قَالَ فَإِنْ خَرَجَ إِلى غَيْرِ تِلْكَ الْبَلْدَةِ فَاشْتَرَى ضَمِنَ وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ لَهُ وَلَهُ رِبْحُهُ لِأَنَّهُ تَصَرَّفَ بِغَيْرِ أَمْرِهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَشْتَرِ حَتَّى رَدَّهُ إِلَى الْكُوفَةِ وَهِيَ الَّتِي عَيْنَهَا بَرِيءَ مِنَ الضَّمَانِ كَالْمُودَعِ إِذَا خَالَفَ فِي الْوَدِيْعَةِ ثُمَّ تَرَكَ وَرَجَعَ الْمَالُ مُضَارَبَةٌ عَلَى حَالِهِ لِبَقَانِهِ فِي يَدِهِ بِالْعَقْدِ السَّابِقِ وَكَذَا إِذَا رَدَّ بَعْضَهُ وَاشْتَرَى بِبَعْضِهِ فِي الْمِصْرِ كَانَ الْمَرْدُودِ وَالْمُشْتَرَى فِي الْمِصْرَ عَلَى الْمُضَارَبَةِ لِمَا قُلْنَا
ترجمه پس اگر نکلا اس شہر کے علاوہ کی طرف اور کچھ خریدا تو ضامن ہوگا اور خرید اسی کے لئے ہوگی اور نفع بھی اسی کا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تصرف حکم مالک کے بغیر ہے۔ اور اگر کچھ نہیں خرید ایہان تک کہ مال کوفہ میں واپس لے آیا اور یہی وہ شہر ہے جو مالک نے معین کیا تھا تو ضمان سے بری ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے موقع ودیعت میں مخالفت کرے پھر خلاف کو چھوڑ دے اور مال پھر مضاربت پر ہو جائے گا۔ عقد سابق کے ذریعہ اس کے قبضہ میں باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے۔ ایسے ہی اگر وہ کچھ مال واپس لایا۔ اور باقی سے شہر میں خرید چکا تھا تو واپس لایا ہوا اور شہر میں خریدا ہوا دونوں مضاربت پر ہوں گے۔ تر قوله فان خرج رب المال نے مضارب کے لئے کسی خاص شہر مثلا کوفہ کی تخصیص کی تھی ۔ مضارب وہاں سے مال کسی اور شہر میں لے گیا اور اس کے ذریعہ کوئی چیز خرید چکا تو وہ راس المال کا ضامن ہوگا اور خریدی ہوئی چیز مع نفع اسی کی ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس کا یہ تصرف حکم مالک کے خلاف ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے ابھی کچھ خریدا نہیں تھا کہ مال اسی معین جگہ پر لے آیا تو تاوان سے بری ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے موزع اگر مودع کے خلاف کرے اور پھر مخالفت سے باز آجائے تو بوجہ مخالفت جو مہمان آ گیا تھا اس سے بری ہو جاتا ہے۔ نیز جو مال مضارب کے پاس ہے وہ بدستور سابق پھر مضاربت پر ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ عقد سابق کی وجہ سے وہ ہنوز اس کے قبضہ میں باقی ہے۔
His saying: 'And if he specified for him...' - If the owner of capital specifies a particular city or particular goods for trade, then the mudarib is not permitted to act contrary to that. Because the mudarib's authority to dispose of the capital is by the owner's delegation, and the owner has specified that delegation to the mentioned matters, which are not without benefit. Since trade differs according to different places and commodities, therefore the mudarib cannot act contrary to the delegation. Imam Shafi'i says that if the owner specifies these things, the mudarabah itself will not be valid. Can the mudarib take the capital to another city other than the specified one? He said: 'If he goes out to a city other than that and buys something, he becomes a guarantor, and that (purchase) is for him and the profit is his, because he acted without his command. And if he does not buy until he returns it to Kufa, which is the specified city, he is discharged from guarantee, like the depositary when he violates in the deposit then leaves (the violation) and returns, the property remains mudarabah as before because it remains in his hand by the previous contract. Similarly, if he returns part of it and buys with part in the city, the returned and the purchased in the city remain on mudarabah for what we said.' Translation: So if he went out to another city and bought something, he will be a guarantor, and the purchase will be for him and the profit also for him, because this disposal is without the owner's command. And if he did not buy anything until he brought the capital back to Kufa, which is the city specified by the owner, he will be discharged from guarantee. Just like when a depositary violates in the deposit then leaves the violation and returns, the property becomes mudarabah again due to its remaining in his hand by the previous contract. Similarly, if he brought back part and bought with part in the city, both the returned and the purchased in the city will be on mudarabah. His saying: 'Then if he goes out' - The owner of capital had specified a particular city, e.g., Kufa, for the mudarib. The mudarib took the capital to another city and bought something with it, then he will be a guarantor of the capital, and the purchased item with profit will be his, because his disposal is against the owner's command. And if he had not yet bought anything and brought the capital back to the specified place, he will be discharged from the penalty. Just as if a depositary violates the deposit and then desists from the violation, he is discharged from the liability that had come due. Also, the capital that is with the mudarib will again become mudarabah as before, because by the previous contract it remains in his possession.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when the owner (rabb al-mal) specifies a particular city or commodity for the mudarabah. The mudarib must adhere to that specification; if he violates by taking the capital to another city and purchases goods, he becomes personally liable for the capital (daman), but the purchased goods and any profit belong to him. If he returns the capital to the specified city without purchasing, he is released from liability and the mudarabah continues. This is analogous to a depositary (mudi') who violates the deposit but then corrects his violation. Imam Shafi'i's opinion that such specification invalidates the contract is noted, but the Hanafi position is that the contract remains valid with the restrictions. The proof is based on the analogy with wadiah and the principle that acting without permission incurs liability.

Key Terms
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification by the owner of a particular city or commodity for the mudarabah.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; here, the mudarib becomes liable for the capital if he violates the specification and purchases.
مستودع (mustawda'): Depositary; one who holds a deposit (wadi'ah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the owner specifies Kufa for trade and the mudarib takes the capital to Basra and buys goods, what is the ruling?
A) The mudarib is not liable, and the profit is shared.
B) The mudarib is liable for the capital, but the purchased goods and profit belong to him.
C) The mudarabah is invalidated immediately.
D) The mudarib must return the goods to the owner without profit.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a mudarib who violates the owner's specification becomes personally liable for the capital but does not invalidate the contract; the profit is his compensation for risk.

Mudarib's Guarantee and Valid Restrictions: Reconciling Two Hanafi Narrations
Resolving narrational conflict and restriction rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the obligation (wujub) and establishment (taqarrur) of a mudarib's guarantee, and apply the Hanafi rules for valid restrictions in mudarabah contracts based on wording and purpose.

Core Idea
The mudarib's guarantee obligation arises on exit, but is only established by purchase; valid restrictions depend on wording and purpose.

This passage from Al-Hidayah resolves an apparent conflict between two transmissions from Imam Muhammad regarding when a mudarib becomes liable for the capital. It also provides detailed guidance on what kinds of restrictions an owner can place on a mudarib's work. Understanding this reconciliation is key to correctly applying Hanafi mudarabah law in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Narrational Conflict
First, note the two conflicting narrations: Al-Jami' Al-Saghir requires actual purchase for the mudarib's guarantee, while Al-Mabsut holds that mere exit from the designated city triggers liability. Understand the tension between them.
Both narrations come from Imam Muhammad, so the conflict is within the Hanafi school (intra-Hanafi).
2
Analyze the Reconciliation: Wujub vs. Taqarrur
The author reconciles by distinguishing between the obligation (wujub) of the guarantee, which arises upon exit, and its establishment (taqarrur), which requires purchase to eliminate the possibility of return. Grasp this two-step process.
The distinction is similar to the obligation of mahr becoming established only after consummation, though the obligation begins at contract.
3
Apply the Distinction to Scenarios
Consider a mudarib who exits the city but does not purchase. He has an obligation to compensate, but it is not yet established; if he returns the capital intact, no liability. If he purchases, the guarantee becomes irrevocable. Practice with examples.
The critical factor is purchase, which removes the chance of return without loss.
4
Analyze the Validity of Restrictions
The passage then discusses when a restriction (taqyid) placed by the owner is binding. Study the different wordings: 'ala an (condition), fa (consequence), ba (adhesion), wa (conjunction). Each conveys different legal force.
A restriction to a specific market within a city is ineffective unless explicitly prohibitive, because the entire city is considered one legal unit.
5
Evaluate the Role of Custom ('Urf)
Note that certain restrictions, like 'buy from the people of Kufa' or 'deal with money changers', are understood customarily as type restrictions. Violating them does not invalidate the mudarabah because the benefit is not in the individuality but in the type.
Custom ('urf) plays a role in interpreting the owner's intent.

ثُمَّ شَرَطَ الشِرَاءَ بِهَا هُنَا وَهُوَ رِوَايَةُ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ وَفِي كِتَابِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ ضَمِنَهِ بِنَفْسِ الْإِخْرَاجِ وَالصَّحِيحُ اَن بِالشِرَاءَ يَتَقَرَّرُ الضَمَانُ لِزَوَالِ اِحْتِمَالِ الرَّةِ إِلَى الْمِصْرِ الَّذِي عَيَّنَه أَمَّا الضَمَانُ فَوُجُوْبُهُ بِنَفْسِ الْإِخْرَاجِ وَإِنَّمَا شَرَطَ الشِرَاءَ لِلتَّقَرُّرِ لِاَصْلِ الْوُجُوبِ وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ عَلَى أَنْ تَشْتَرِي فِي سُوقِ الْكُوفَةِ حَيْثُ لَا يَصِحُ التَّفْسِيدُ لأَنَّ الْمِصْرَ مَعَ تَبَايُنِ اَطْرَافِهِ كَبُقْعَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فَلَا يُفِيدُ التَّقْسِيدُ إِلَّا إِذَا صَرَّحَ بِالنَّهْيِ بِاَنْ قَالَ إِعْمَل فِى السُّوقِ وَلَا تَعْمَلْ فِى غَيْرِ السُّوقِ لِأَنَّهُ صَرَّحَ بِالْحَجْرِ وَالْوِلَايَةُ إِلَيْهِ وَمَعْنَى الشَّخْصِيصِ أَنْ يَقُولَ عَلَى اَنْ تَعْمَلَ كَذَا أَوْ فِي مَكَان كَذَا وَكَذَا إِذَا قَالَ خُذْ هَذَا الْمَالَ تَعْمَلْ بِهِ فِي الْكُوفَةِ لأَنَّهُ تَفْسِيرٌ لَهُ أَوْ قَالَ فَاعْمَل بِهِ فِي الْكُوفَةَ لِاَنَّ الْفَاءَ لِلْوَصْلِ اَوْ قَالَ خُذْهُ بِالنِّصْفِ بِالْكُوفَةِ لِأَنَّ الْبَاءَ لِلْإِلْصَاقِ أَمَّا إِذَا قَالَ خُذْ هَذَا الْمَالَ وَاعْمَل بِهِ بِالْكُوفَةِ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَعْمَلَ فِيهَا وَفِي غَيْرِهَا لِاَنَّ الْوَاوَ لِلْعَطْفِ فَيَصِيرُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمَشْوَرَةِ وَلَوْ قَالَ عَلَى أَنْ تَشْتَرِى مِنْ فَلَان وَتَبِيعَ مِنْهُ صَحَ التَّقْبِيدُ لِأَنَّهُ مُفِيدٌ لِزِيَادَةِ الْبَقَةِ بِهِ فِي الْمُعَامَلَةِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ عَلَى اَنْ تَشْتَرِى بِهَا مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكُوفَةِ اَوْ دَفَعَ مَالًا فِي الصَّرْفِ عَلَى أَنْ تَشْتَرِي به مِنَ الصَّيَارِفَةَ وَتَبِيْعِ مِنْهُمْ فَبَاعَ بِالْكُوفَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَهْلِهَا أَوْ مِنْ غَيْرِ الصَّيَارِفَةِ جَازَ لَانَّ فَائِدَةَ الْأَوَّلِ التَّقْسِيدُ بالْمَكَان وَفَائِدَةُ الثَّانِي التَّقْدِيدُ بالنَّوْعِ هَذَا هُوَ الْمُرَادُ عُرْفًا لَا فِيمَا وَرَاءَ ذَلِكَ.
Then he made purchase a condition here, and this is the narration of Al-Jami' Al-Saghir. And in the Book of Mudarabah, he made him liable with the mere exit. The correct view is that by purchase the guarantee is established due to the removal of the possibility of return to the city which he specified. As for the guarantee, its obligation is by the mere exit, but purchase is a condition for establishment for the origin of the obligation. And this is contrary to when he says: 'On condition that you purchase in the market of Kufa,' where the restriction is not valid because the city, despite the diversity of its parts, is like one district, so the restriction is not beneficial unless he explicitly prohibits by saying: 'Work in the market and do not work outside the market,' because he explicitly restricted and authority is to him. And the meaning of specification is that he says: 'On condition that you work with such-and-such or in such-and-such a place.' Similarly, if he says: 'Take this wealth, you work with it in Kufa,' because it is an interpretation for him, or he said: 'So work with it in Kufa,' because the fa is for joining, or he said: 'Take it for half in Kufa,' because the ba is for adhesion. As for when he says: 'Take this wealth and work with it in Kufa,' then he may work in it and in other than it, because the waw is for conjunction, so it becomes like advice. And if he said: 'On condition that you buy from so-and-so and sell to him,' the restriction is valid, because it is beneficial for increased trust in the transaction. Contrary to when he says: 'On condition that you buy thereby from the people of Kufa,' or he gave money in currency exchange on condition that you buy thereby from the money changers and sell to them, then he sold in Kufa from other than its people or from other than the money changers, it is permissible, because the benefit of the first is restriction by place, and the benefit of the second is restriction by type. This is what is intended customarily, not beyond that.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute resolution between two narrations from Imam Muhammad: one from Al-Jami' Al-Saghir requiring actual purchase for the mudarib's guarantee, and one from Al-Mabsut where mere exit from the designated city triggers liability. The author reconciles by distinguishing between the obligation (wujub) of guarantee, which arises upon exit, and its establishment (taqarrur), which requires purchase to eliminate the possibility of return. The passage then discusses valid restrictions in mudarabah. A restriction to a specific marketplace (suq) is ineffective unless the owner explicitly forbids other locations, because a city is considered one legal unit. However, specifying a particular person is beneficial for trust and thus valid. Restrictions based on type (e.g., dealing only with money changers) are customarily understood as type restrictions, so violating them does not invalidate the mudarabah. The author provides detailed guidance on the phrasing of conditions: using 'ala an, fa, or the particle ba indicates a binding condition, while using wa makes it advisory.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability of the mudarib to compensate for loss or misuse of capital.
تقرر (taqarrur): Establishment or certainty of a legal obligation; here, the point at which the guarantee becomes irrevocable.
تقيد (taqyid): Restriction placed by the owner on the mudarib's actions, e.g., to a specific place or person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciled view in this passage, when does the mudarib's guarantee (daman) become established (muttaqarrir)?
A) Upon the mere exit (ikhraj) of capital from the designated city.
B) Upon purchase (shira') in the unauthorized location.
C) Upon the owner's explicit prohibition.
D) Upon return of the capital to the owner.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's guarantee obligation arises upon exit but is only established by purchase; restrictions are binding only if worded as conditions ('ala an) or explicit prohibitions, not as advice (wa).

Liability of Mudarib with Capital in Another City
Ruling on mudarib's liability when taking capital to another city

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which the mudarib becomes liable when taking capital to a non-specified city and explain the qiyas used to derive this ruling.

Core Idea
Liability in mudaraba is not by movement alone; it is fixed only by purchase in the forbidden city.

This passage from the Hanafi school clarifies a critical point in mudaraba law: the mudarib's liability (ḍamān) when he takes the capital to a city other than the one specified by the rabb al-mal. The ruling is based on a clear analogy (qiyas) to the mahr in marriage, where obligation arises only upon consummation. Understanding this condition helps distinguish between mere violation of contract and actual liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mudarib taking capital to a city not specified by the rabb al-mal. The ruling is that liability (ḍamān) is not immediate but conditional upon making a purchase in that city.
2
Locate the authoritative source
The passage cites al-Jami' al-Saghir, one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, as the textual basis for this ruling.
3
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
The commentary draws an analogy to marriage: just as mahr becomes obligatory only upon consummation (dukhul), liability in mudaraba becomes established only upon purchase (shira').
The common illa (effective cause) is that obligation is tied to a specific completion action.
4
Note the condition and exception
If the mudarib returns without purchasing anything, he is absolved of liability. The condition for liability is the actual purchase.
5
Apply to similar cases
Consider other scenarios where the mudarib acts outside authority but does not complete a transaction: no liability attaches until a transaction is conducted.
This ruling reinforces the principle that liability in agency is linked to actual conduct, not mere movement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب المضاربت میں ہے۔ لیکن ضمان ابھی متقرر نہیں ہے۔ جب تک دوسرے شہر میں خرید نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ اگر کچھ خریدے بغیر واپس لے آیا تو ضمان سے بری ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر کچھ خرید لیا تو ضمان منتقرر ہو گیا جیسا کہ جامع صغیر میں ہے۔ اور یہ ایسا ہی ہے جیسے نکاح سے مہر کا وجوب کہ اگر قبل از ولی طلاق دے دی تو متعہ رہا اور اگر ولی ہو گئی تو مہر متقر ر ہو گیا۔
It is in the Book of Mudaraba: But the liability is not yet established. Until he purchases in the second city — if he returns without buying anything, he is absolved of liability. If he purchased something, the liability becomes established, as mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And this is similar to the obligation of mahr in marriage: if the husband divorces before consummation, there is only mut'ah; if consummation occurs, the mahr becomes established.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school concerning the liability (ḍamān) of the mudarib when the rabb al-mal has specified a particular city for trade. The ruling, as found in al-Jami' al-Saghir (one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah), states that if the mudarib takes the capital to another city, liability is not immediately certain. It remains contingent until he actually makes a purchase in that second city. If he returns without buying anything, he is free from liability. If he buys something, the liability is established. The passage draws an analogy (qiyas) to marriage: the mahr becomes obligatory only upon consummation; similarly, liability in mudaraba becomes fixed only upon purchase. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of linking liability to actual action rather than mere movement.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for loss or guarantee; here, the mudarib's personal liability if the capital is lost or misused after leaving the specified city.
مضارب (muḍārib): The agent in a mudaraba contract who manages the capital provided by the rabb al-mal.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The owner/investor of the capital in a mudaraba contract.
متعہ (mut‘ah): A gift or compensation given to the wife in case of divorce before consummation; here used as analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only after making a purchase in the second city
C) When the rabb al-mal objects
D) After returning to the first city

Key Takeaway
Liability of the mudarib for taking capital to another specified city is contingent upon actual purchase, analogous to mahr becoming due only upon consummation.

Three Categories of Qayd in Mudaraba Restrictions
Explains when specification of a market is binding in mudaraba and the rule of different types of qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of three categories of qayd (beneficial, harmful, mixed) to determine when a restriction in mudaraba is binding.

Core Idea
A restriction in mudaraba is binding only if beneficial in every respect; if mixed, it binds only when explicitly stated.

In mudaraba, the rabb al-mal may try to restrict the mudarib's actions, for example by specifying a particular market. But is such a restriction always binding? This lesson examines a nuanced rule from later Hanafi scholarship that classifies restrictions into three types and explains when each is enforceable. Understanding this rule helps resolve apparent contradictions in the sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The passage discusses a case where the rabb al-mal says 'trade in the market of Kufa' without adding an explicit prohibition. Note the initial ruling: it is not binding.
The mudarib may trade anywhere in the city because the city is considered a single unit.
2
Examine the Explicit Prohibition Exception
If the rabb al-mal explicitly says 'trade only in the market, nowhere else', then the restriction becomes binding because the owner exercises his authority to prohibit.
Explicit wording transforms a mere suggestion into a binding condition.
3
Analyze the Apparent Contradiction
The passage cites al-Dhakhira: if the rabb al-mal says 'sell on credit only' and the mudarib sells for cash, he is not considered violating. This seems to contradict the rule that explicit prohibitions are binding.
The resolution lies in the nature of the restriction.
4
Apply the Three Categories of Qayd
The rule: (1) Beneficial in every respect → always binding. (2) Useless/harmful in every respect → always disregarded. (3) Beneficial in one respect but not another → binding only when explicitly stated, otherwise considered advice.
Category (3) is the key to solving the contradiction.
5
Classify the Market Specification
Specifying a market is beneficial because prices differ by locality, but not beneficial because a city is legally a single unit. Thus it is category (3): binding only when explicitly stated as a prohibition.
Analogies from wadi'ah and salam corroborate this classification.

Source Text

قوله وهذا بخلاف ما معین شہر کی تخصیص کا جو حکم مذکور ہوا یہ اس کے خلاف ہے۔ جب رب المال مضارب کے تصرف کے لئے کوفہ وغیرہ کے بازار کی تخصیص کرے کہ یہ تخصیص صحیح نہیں کیونکہ شہر اپنی جوانب مختلفہ کے باوجود بقعہ واحدہ کے درجہ میں ہے تو قید مذکور غیر مفید ہے۔ پس یہ سمجھا جائے گا کہ مالک نے بطریق مشورہ یا اتفاقی بول چال کے طور پر بازار کا لفظ بول دیا۔ غیر بازار کے تصرف سے منع نہیں کیا۔ ہاں اگر وہ صراحتا یہ کہہ دے کہ تو صرف بازار ہی میں تجارت کر اس کے علاوہ میں مت کر تو یہ صریح تقید معتبر ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس نے اختیار سے ممانعت کی تصریح کر دی اور ولایت ممانعت کا حق اس کو ہے۔ اب یہاں یہ سوال ہوتا ہیکہ ذخیرہ میں یہ مسئلہ مذکور ہے کہ اگر مالک یہ کہتے۔ بع بالنسية ولا تبع بالنقد ( ادھار پیچ نقدمت بیچ) اور مضارب نقد بیچے تو وہ صریح ممانعت کے باوجود مخالف حکم قرار نہیں دیا جاتا ( جب کہ نقد اور ادھار کے بھاؤ میں کوئی تفاوت نہ ہو ) ۔ اس کا جواب ایک قاعدہ پر مبنی ہے اور وہ یہ جو قید ہر لحاظ سے مفید ہو۔ اس کا بالضرور اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ اور جوقید ہر لحاظ سے غیر مفید ہو وہ لغو ہو گی اور جو قید من وجہ مفید ہوا ر من وجہ غیر مفید تو وہ صریح نہی کے وقت تو معتبر ہوگی۔ اور جب اس سے سکوت ہو تو لغو ہوگی ۔ اول کی مثال تخصیص بلد وسعلہ ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں گزر چکا اور دوم کی مثال بیع بالنسیہ کہ ادھار کے بجائے نقد بیچنا مفید ہے تو ادھار کی قید مضر ہونے کی وجہ سے لغو ہوگی اور سوم کی مثال تقیید بالسوق ہے کہ یہ اس حیثیت سے مفید ہے کہ شہر اماکن مخلفہ پر مشتمل ہے۔ حقیقتا بھی اور حکما بھی۔ حقیقتہ تو ظاہر ہے اور حکم اس لئے کہ اگر مودع کسی ایک محلے میں حفاظت کی شرط لگائے تو اس کے علاوہ میں حفاظت کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ (اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ اختلاف امکنہ سے کبھی بھاؤ مختلف ہوتا ہے ) اور اس لحاظ سے غیر مفید ہے کہ شہر تباین اعتراف کے باوجود واحدہ کے درجہ میں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر سلم کے متعاقدین شہر میں ہونے کی شرط کریں اور محلہ بیان نہ کریں تو عقد صیح ہوتا ہے۔ پس نہی کی تصریح کے وقت اس کا اعتبار ہوگا اور سکوت کے وقت اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ (بنایہ)
His saying: 'And this is contrary to...' — This is contrary to the ruling mentioned for specification of a city. When the rabb al-mal specifies a particular market (e.g., the market of Kufa) for the mudarib's transactions, this specification is not valid because a city, despite containing various areas, is considered a single unit. So the mentioned restriction is useless. Therefore, it will be understood that the owner mentioned the market by way of advice or casual talk, and did not prohibit transactions outside the market. Yes, if he explicitly says, 'Trade only in the market and nowhere else,' then this explicit restriction is valid because he has clearly expressed prohibition with authority. Here a question arises: In al-Dhakhira, it is mentioned that if the owner says, 'Sell on credit and do not sell for cash,' and the mudarib sells for cash, he is not considered violating the prohibition even though explicit, (when there is no difference in price between cash and credit). The answer is based on a rule: any restriction that is beneficial in every respect is necessarily observed. A restriction that is useless in every respect is disregarded. A restriction that is beneficial in one respect but not in another is valid when explicitly stated, but disregarded when there is silence. The first example is specification of city and merchandise as previously mentioned. The second example is the sale on credit: since selling for cash is more beneficial, the credit restriction is harmful and thus disregarded. The third example is restriction to the market: it is beneficial because the city consists of different places, both literally and legally. Literally it is obvious; legally, if a depositor specifies one locality for safekeeping, the depositary has no right to keep it elsewhere (and it is obvious that prices differ by location). In another respect, it is not beneficial because the city, despite its diverse parts, is a single unit. Thus, if parties to a salam contract stipulate that delivery be in the city without specifying a locality, the contract is valid. So when the prohibition is explicit, this restriction is considered; when there is silence, it is not considered. (Binyah)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (Ashraf al-Hadaya) explains a key distinction in mudaraba: the ruling on specifying a market (sūq) within a city versus specifying a whole city. It begins by stating that if the rabb al-mal says 'trade in the market of Kufa' without explicit prohibition, this is not a binding restriction because a city, despite diverse areas, is legally a single unit. The mudarib may trade anywhere in the city. However, if the rabb al-mal explicitly says 'trade only in the market, not elsewhere,' then this explicit restriction is valid and binding because the owner has the authority to impose conditions. The author then addresses an apparent contradiction from al-Dhakhira: if the owner says 'sell on credit, not for cash,' and the mudarib sells for cash (when prices are equal), he is not considered to have violated the prohibition. To resolve this, the author introduces a fundamental rule of qayd (restriction) with three categories: (1) A restriction that is beneficial in every respect (e.g., specifying city or merchandise) is always binding. (2) A restriction that is harmful in every respect (e.g., selling on credit when cash is equally beneficial and quicker) is disregarded even if explicitly stated. (3) A restriction that is beneficial in one respect but not in another (e.g., specifying a market) is binding only when explicitly stated as a prohibition; if mentioned without emphasis, it is considered advice. This is supported by analogies from wadi'ah (deposit) and salam (advance sale) contracts. The rule is taken from Binyah (a commentary).

Key Terms
تخصیص (takhṣīṣ): Specification of a particular place, person, or type in a mudaraba contract by the rabb al-mal.
قید (qayd): A restriction or condition placed on the mudarib's actions.
مفید (mufīd): Beneficial or useful; used here to describe a restriction that serves a purpose.
غیر مفید (ghayr mufīd): Useless; a restriction that is not beneficial and thus disregarded.
بقعہ واحدہ (buq‘ah wāḥidah): A single unit; used to describe how a city is considered legally as one place despite multiple areas.
سلم (salam): A forward sale contract where payment is made in advance for future delivery of a specified commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the specification of a market (sūq) become binding on the mudarib?
A) Whenever the rabb al-mal mentions a market, even casually
B) Only when the rabb al-mal explicitly prohibits trading outside that market
C) Never, because the city is a single unit
D) Only if the mudarib agrees in writing

Key Takeaway
A restriction in mudaraba is only binding if it is beneficial in every respect, or if it is of mixed benefit and explicitly stated as a prohibition.

Beneficial vs Non-Beneficial Phrases for Specifying Place in Mudaraba
Classification of eight Arabic phrases for place specification in mudaraba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify six beneficial and two non-beneficial Arabic phrases for specifying place in a mudaraba contract by applying the Hanafi grammatical rule of independent utterance.

Core Idea
A condition binds only if it cannot start an independent sentence.

In a mudaraba contract, the rabb al-mal may specify a city for trade. But not every phrase mentioning a city creates a binding condition. The Hanafi jurists formulated a precise grammatical rule based on whether the phrase can stand alone as an independent sentence. This lesson examines the eight common phrases and the rule that distinguishes effective specifications from mere advice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight phrases
List the eight phrases given in the text. Note that the first six are said to be 'beneficial for specification' (mufīd li al-takhṣīṣ), and the last two are 'non-beneficial'.
The phrases are presented in pairs: three with the capital mentioned, three without, but all follow the same grammatical pattern.
2
Examine the grammatical structure of each phrase
For each phrase, determine if the part after 'mudaraba' can be spoken as the beginning of an independent sentence. For example, 'on condition that you trade' cannot start alone; 'so trade' can.
Focus on the verb form: subjunctive (dependent) vs. imperative or jussive (independent).
3
Apply the rule (ḍābiṭah)
The rule states: if the phrase after the contract cannot be uttered independently and is syntactically dependent on the preceding, it becomes part of the contract (binding). If it can start an independent sentence, it remains separate and non-binding.
The rule prevents speech from being pointless (laghw).
4
Classify each phrase accordingly
Match each of the eight phrases against the rule. Confirm that the six 'beneficial' ones are dependent (cannot start alone), and the two 'non-beneficial' ones are independent (can start alone).
The text mentions 'ibtidā’' (starting) as the key criterion.

Source Text

قوله ومعنى التخصيص .... اس قول کا مقصد مفید تخصیص وغیرہ مفید تخصیص الفاظ کے درمیان امتیاز بیان کرنا ہے سواس بارے میں فقہا نے آٹھ الفاظ معین کئے ہیں جن میں سے چھ مفید تخصیص ہیں۔ اور دو غیر مفید، مفید تخصیص یہ ہیں۔ دفعت اليك المال مُضَارَبَةً على ان تعمل به بالكوفة (۲ دفعت اليك المال مُضَارَبَةٌ تعمل بالكوفة (۳) دفعت اليك المال مُضَارَبَةٌ فاعمل به بالكوفة دفعت اليك مُضَارَبَة بالنصف عله ان تعمل به بالكوفة (۵) دفعت اليك مُضَارَبَةٌ بالنصف تعمل بالكوفة دفعت اليك مُضَارَبَة بالنصف فاعمل به بالكوفة اور غیر مفید تخصیص یہ ہیں: 1) دفعت اليك مُضَارَبَةُ بالنصف واعمل بالكوفة (۲) دفعت اليك مُضَارَبَةً بالنصف اعمل بالكوفة اس کا ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جب رب المال مضاربت کے بعد ایسا لفظ ذکر کرے جس کا تلفظ ابتداہم ناممکن ہو۔ اور اس کے ماقبل پر منی کرنا ممکن ہو تو اس کو ماقبل پر مبنی کیا جائے گا ( تا کہ کلام لغونہ ہو ) جیسا کہ الفاظ ستہ میں یہی بات ہے اور جب کوئی ایسا لفظ ذکر کرے جس سے ابتداء کرنا مستقیم ہو تو اس کو ماقبل پر بنی نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ بلکہ مستقل کلام کہا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ آخری دو لفظوں میں ہے۔ جب یہ ضابط مع تفصیل سامنے آ گیا تو اب عبارت سے تطبیق دینا بہت آسان ہے۔
His saying: 'And the meaning of specification...' The purpose of this statement is to distinguish between beneficial and non-beneficial words of specification. Regarding this, the jurists have designated eight words, six of which are beneficial for specification: 1) 'I gave you the capital as a mudaraba on the condition that you trade with it in Kufa.' 2) 'I gave you the capital as a mudaraba, you (will) trade in Kufa.' 3) 'I gave you the capital as a mudaraba, so trade with it in Kufa.' 4) 'I gave you a mudaraba for half, on the condition that you trade with it in Kufa.' 5) 'I gave you a mudaraba for half, you (will) trade in Kufa.' 6) 'I gave you a mudaraba for half, so trade with it in Kufa.' And the non-beneficial ones are: 1) 'I gave you a mudaraba for half, and trade in Kufa.' 2) 'I gave you a mudaraba for half, (I) trade in Kufa.' The rule is: when the rabb al-mal mentions after the mudaraba a word that cannot be uttered independently at the beginning, and can be syntactically dependent on what precedes, it is made dependent on the preceding (so that the speech is not pointless), as in the six phrases. If he mentions a word with which starting independently is proper, it is not made dependent; rather, it is considered an independent statement, as in the last two words. Once this rule and its details are understood, applying it to the text becomes easy.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (Ashraf al-Hadaya) presents a crucial linguistic rule for specifying location in a mudaraba contract. The jurists identified eight common phrases used by the rabb al-mal to indicate where the mudarib should trade. Six of these phrases are considered 'beneficial for specification' (mufīd li-al-takhṣīṣ), meaning they effectively bind the mudarib to trade only in the specified city. These six include phrases with 'alā an (on condition that) or sentences that are syntactically dependent on the preceding contract, such as 'I gave you a mudaraba that you trade in Kufa.' The two non-beneficial phrases are 'I gave you a mudaraba for half, and trade in Kufa' and 'I gave you a mudaraba for half, I trade in Kufa.' These are considered independent statements because the word 'and' or the imperative form allows a fresh start; thus they do not effectively restrict the mudarib. The underlying rule is based on Arabic syntax: if the word after the contract cannot be the beginning of an independent sentence (e.g., it is a verb in the jussive or a conditional clause), it is attached to the preceding and becomes part of the contract. If the word can stand alone as a complete sentence (like a command 'trade' or a nominal sentence), it is treated as a separate statement and not a condition of the mudaraba. This distinction helps in interpreting the intent of the rabb al-mal.

Key Terms
مفید تخصیص (mufīd li-al-takhṣīṣ): A phrasing that effectively specifies a condition in the mudaraba contract, making it binding.
غیر مفید تخصیص (ghayr mufīd li-al-takhṣīṣ): A phrasing that does not effectively impose a binding condition; it is considered independent speech.
ضابطہ (ḍābiṭah): A general rule or principle governing the classification of these phrases.
ابتداء (ibtidā’): The ability to begin a sentence independently; a criterion for determining if a phrase is independent or dependent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for beneficial place specification in mudaraba relies on whether the phrase can be independently uttered; only dependent phrases are binding.
