Why the Waw in 'Wa'imil' is Conjunctive, Not Circumstantial
Explains why the waw is conjunctive, not circumstantial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conjunctive and circumstantial waw in Arabic contractual phrases and explain why an imperative clause cannot be a circumstantial clause in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
An imperative (insha') cannot be a circumstance (hal) — so the waw in 'wa'imil' is conjunctive, making it an independent command.

In mudarabah contracts, precise grammatical analysis can determine the binding nature of conditions. This passage examines a subtle point: whether the waw in 'wa'imil' introduces a circumstantial clause or simply joins two commands. The answer hinges on a firm rule of Arabic grammar: performative sentences cannot serve as circumstantial modifiers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
The waw in 'wa'imil' could be conjunctive (waw al-'atf) or circumstantial (waw al-hal). The latter would make it part of the preceding condition, affecting the ruling.
In the source text, the author is responding to a hypothetical objection that the waw might be hal.
2
Recognize the proposed objection
Why not take it as waw al-hal? An example is given: 'dakhaltu al-dāra wa anta ḥurr' (I entered while you were free), where the waw introduces a circumstance.
The example is from standard Arabic grammar; the source cites a similar example.
3
Apply the grammatical rule
A circumstantial clause must be khabari (informative). Imperatives are insha'i (performative) and thus cannot be hal. This rule is established in Arabic grammar.
The text states that insha'i sentences lack the capacity to function as hal.
4
Conclude the function of the waw
Therefore, the waw is conjunctive, and 'wa'imil' stands as an independent command, not a condition. This affects whether the location specification is binding.
The passage ends with this conclusion, clarifying the classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله لان الوا و للعطف ..... الخ - اس پر سوال ہوتا ہے کہ اس واؤ کو حال کے لئے کیوں نہیں لیا گیا جیسے ادالتی الفا وانت حریر برائے حال ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ و اعمل یہ جملہ إنشائیہ ہے اور علوم عربیہ سے یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ جمل انشائیہ میں حال ہونے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہوتی۔ واؤ کے ساتھ ہوں یا بلا واؤ ہوں۔
His saying: 'Because the waw is for conjunction...' — A question arises: why is this waw not taken as for the circumstantial clause (hal), like 'adālatī alfa wa anta ḥarīr' where it is for hal? The answer is that 'wa'imil' is an insha'i sentence (performative utterance) and it is established in Arabic grammar that insha'i sentences do not have the capacity to function as hal, whether with waw or without.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This brief passage handles a grammatical objection against the classification of the phrase 'wa'imil' (and trade) as a conjunctive rather than a circumstantial clause. In the previous lesson, the sixth beneficial phrase ends with 'fā'mil bihī' (so trade with it), and the non-beneficial phrases use 'wa'imil' (and trade). The author of Ashraf al-Hadaya had classified 'wa'imil' as a separate statement. Here he answers a hypothetical objection: why not take the waw as a waw al-ḥāl (waw of circumstance), making it a circumstantial clause and thus part of the condition? The answer is that a circumstantial clause must be a nominal sentence or a verbal sentence describing a state. However, 'wa'imil' is an imperative, which is an insha'i sentence (performative, not informative). Arabic grammar rules state that insha'i sentences cannot function as ḥāl (circumstantial modifiers). Therefore, the waw must be treated as a simple conjunctive (wāw al-‘aṭf), making 'wa'imil' an independent command. This linguistic distinction is crucial for determining whether the location specification is binding or not.

Key Terms
واو حال (wāw al-ḥāl): The waw that introduces a circumstantial clause, describing the state of the subject.
جملہ انشائیہ (jumlah inshā’iyyah): A performative sentence that creates a new reality (e.g., commands, prohibitions, contracts) as opposed to informative sentences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because it is a command for the mudarib

Key Takeaway
In Arabic grammar, insha'i sentences (like commands) cannot function as circumstantial clauses, so the waw in 'wa'imil' is conjunctive, making it an independent command in mudarabah.

Binding Effect of Specifying a Person in Mudaraba
Ruling when the rabb al-mal names a specific person for trade or specifies a type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ta'yin ismi (binding person specification) and ta'yin naw'i (non-binding category specification) in mudaraba, and state the ruling when the mudarib violates a binding specification.

Core Idea
Naming a specific person is binding; specifying a type or place is not.

This lesson explores a key nuance in mudaraba contracts: when the rabb al-mal specifies a particular person for trade, that specification is binding because trust is person-specific. However, if the specification is by category (e.g., 'people of Kufa' or 'money changers'), it is merely an indication of place or trade type and does not restrict the mudarib to those individuals. Understanding this distinction prevents disputes and protects the interests of both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of specification
Read the passage and note the two scenarios: (1) the rabb al-mal names a specific person, e.g., 'Buy from Zaid'; (2) the rabb al-mal specifies a category, e.g., 'people of Kufa' or 'money changers'.
These are termed ta'yin ismi and ta'yin naw'i respectively.
2
Understand the rationale for binding effect
The text explains that specifying a person is beneficial because trade varies with individuals and the owner trusts that person. Thus, acting contrary is not permissible.
The basis is the owner's trust and the benefit of the contract.
3
Apply to the category specification
If the rabb al-mal says 'with the people of Kufa' or 'with money changers', the purpose is to specify location or trade type, not persons. Therefore, the mudarib may trade with others within that location or type.
The text gives the example of buying from a visitor in Kufa or from a non-money changer in currency exchange.
4
Distinguish the outcomes
When a binding person specification is violated, the purchase is for the mudarib's own account. When a category specification is violated (but within the implied location/type), it is valid for the mudaraba.
This distinction follows from the intention of the rabb al-mal.

Source Text

قـولـه عـلـى ان تشترى من فلان ... الخ - اگر رب المان نے تجارتی معاملہ کے لئے کسی شخص کی اسما تعیین کردی و ی تعیین سی ہوگی کہ فائدہ سے خالی نہیں۔ کیونکہ تجارت اختلاف اشخاص کے لحاظ سے مختلف ہوتی ہے اور مالک نے معاملات میں شخص معین پر زیادہ اعتماد کیا ہے تو اس کے خلاف کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر مالک نے اسمی تعیین کے بغیر یوں کہا کہ اہل کوفہ کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کر، یا بیع صرف میں کہا کہ صرافوں کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کر اور مضارب نے کوفہ میں اہل کوفہ یا صرافوں کے علاوہ کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کی تو یہ جائز ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اول کا مقصد صرف مکان اور جگہ کی تخصیص ہے کہ کوفہ میں ہونی چاہیے اور ثانی کا مقصد نوع تجارت کی تخصیص ہے کہ بیچ صرف ہونی چاہئے ۔ کہنے کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ اس سے اشخاص کی تخصیص مقصود نہیں ہوتی۔
His saying: 'On condition that you buy from so-and-so...' — If the rabb al-mal specifies a person by name for trade, this specification is not without benefit because trade varies according to individuals, and the owner has greater trust in that specific person for transactions. So acting contrary is not permissible. However, if the owner, without naming a person, says, 'Buy and sell with the people of Kufa,' or in currency exchange says, 'Buy and sell with the money changers,' and the mudarib in Kufa buys and sells with others besides the people of Kufa or the money changers, this is permissible. Because the purpose of the first (naming a person) is only to specify the location — that it should be in Kufa — and the second is to specify the type of trade — that it should be currency exchange. The point is that specification of individuals is not intended.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya addresses a situation where the rabb al-mal specifies a particular individual for trade, e.g., 'Buy from Zaid only.' The commentary rules that such a specification is binding and beneficial because trade relations depend on trust, and the owner's confidence in that person is a valid consideration. The mudarib cannot trade with others in that case. However, if the rabb al-mal specifies a general category like 'the people of Kufa' or 'the money changers,' this is not a binding restriction on persons; it is merely an indication of place or type of trade. The mudarib may trade with others as long as the trade is in Kufa (for place) or involves currency exchange (for type). The distinction lies in whether the specification is of a particular person (ismī) or of a category (naw‘ī). The former is a valid condition; the latter is not, because the owner's intention is not to restrict persons but to identify the scope of trade. This ruling protects the owner's legitimate interests while avoiding unnecessary restrictions on the mudarib's flexibility.

Key Terms
تعیین اسمی (ta‘yīn ismī): Specification by name of a particular person.
تعیین نوعی (ta‘yīn naw‘ī): Specification by type or category (e.g., people of a city, profession).
بیع صرف (bay‘ ṣarf): Currency exchange transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The purchase is valid for the mudaraba
D) The mudaraba is terminated

Key Takeaway
A named person specification (ta'yin ismi) is binding; a category or place specification (ta'yin naw'i) is not, reflecting the owner's intended level of restriction.

Effect of Specifying a Time Limit in Mudaraba
Ruling that a mudaraba contract ends when the specified time expires, with qiyas reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a time-specified mudaraba contract and explain the qiyas reasoning (analogy to wakalah).

Core Idea
A mudaraba with a fixed time expires automatically — it is like an agency that ends when its term ends.

This lesson examines a key ruling from al-Hidayah: when a mudaraba contract is limited to a specific time period, it becomes invalid upon expiry. The reasoning uses a clear qiyas (analogy) to wakalah and to restrictions of type and place. Understanding this ruling clarifies the binding nature of time conditions in partnership contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify the act: mudaraba with a specified time limit. Ruling: the contract becomes batil (invalid) when the time expires.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to wakalah: mudaraba is a form of agency, so it ends when the term ends. Also analogy to restriction by type or place.
The text states: faṣāra ka-al-taqyīd bi al-naw‘ wa al-makān.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The illa (effective cause) is the binding restriction (taqyid) by time, which is similar to restriction by type or place. Both are specific conditions that limit the mudarib's authority.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may allow the contract to continue if both parties consent, but the Hanafi school holds it invalid automatically.
The text is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
This ruling is the relied-upon position. The Hanafi view is based on the clear analogy to wakalah and the principle that binding conditions must be honored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضاربت کے لئے معین وقت گزرنے کے بعد مضاربت باطل ہوگی قَالَ. وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ وَقَتَ لِلْمُضَارَبَةِ وَقْتًا بِعَيْنِهِ يَبْطُلُ الْعَقْدُ بِمُضِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ تَوْكِيْلٌ فَيَتَوَفَّتُ بِمَا وَفَّتَه وَالتَّوْقِيتُ مُفِيدٌ فَإِنَّهُ تَقْسِيدٌ بِالزَّمَانِ فَصَارَ كَالتَّقْلِيدِ بِالنَّوْعِ وَالْمَكَانِ ترجمہ ایسے ہی اگر مضاربت کے لئے معین وقت محدود کیا ہو تو اس کے گزرنے سے عقد باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو کیل ہے تو جس کے ساتھ موقت کیا ہے اسی تک رہے گی اور توقیت مفید بھی ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک زمانہ کی قید ہے تو نوع و مقام کی قید کی طرح ہو گئی۔
After the specified time for mudaraba passes, the mudaraba becomes invalid. He (the author) said: Similarly, if he specifies a fixed time for the mudaraba, the contract becomes invalid upon its expiry, because it is a wakalah, so it ends with what it was limited to. And specification of time is beneficial because it is a restriction by time, so it becomes like restriction by type and place. Translation: Similarly, if a fixed time is limited for mudaraba, after its expiry the contract becomes invalid because this is a wakalah, so it will remain only until the time specified. And specification of time is beneficial because it is a restriction by time, so it becomes like restriction by type and place.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling from the matn (likely al-Hidayah) and its commentary. It states that if the rabb al-mal specifies a particular time period for the mudaraba (e.g., one year), the contract automatically becomes invalid (bāṭil) when that time expires. The reasoning is that mudaraba is a form of agency (wakālah), and an agency contract ends when its term ends. The specification of time is considered beneficial and binding, analogous to specifying the type of trade or the location. Thus, after the time expires, the mudarib no longer has authority to trade with the capital; any transactions thereafter would be for his own account. This ruling emphasizes the importance of time as a valid condition in mudaraba, and it is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that conditions which serve a benefit are binding.

Key Terms
توقیت (tawqīt): Specification of a particular time period for the mudaraba contract.
موکل (mūkil): Principal; here used in the sense that mudaraba is like wakalah.
تقلید (taqlīd): Here used as 'restriction' or 'limitation' (taqyīd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a fixed time limit in mudaraba is binding: the contract becomes batil upon expiry, and the mudarib must cease operations immediately.

Mudarib Cannot Buy a Relative Who Would Be Freed
Ruling that mudarib cannot buy a slave who would become free upon ownership by rabb al-mal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mudarib buys a slave who would be emancipated upon ownership by the rabb al-mal, and explain the reason based on the purpose of mudaraba.

Core Idea
A mudarib cannot buy a slave who becomes free upon ownership — profit through resale is impossible.

In a mudaraba contract, the mudarib's role is to trade for profit. If he buys a slave who will be freed as soon as the rabb al-mal owns him, there is no chance to resell. This lesson explains why such a purchase is prohibited and what happens if the mudarib does it anyway.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited purchase
Note that the mudarib is not allowed to buy any slave that would be automatically emancipated upon ownership by the rabb al-mal, whether due to kinship (like a son or father) or a prior oath.
2
Understand the rationale: purpose of mudaraba
The mudaraba contract is designed to generate profit through repeated buying and selling. If the slave becomes free immediately, he cannot be resold, so profit is impossible.
3
Compare with invalid subjects
The text likens this to buying items that cannot be owned by possession, such as wine or buying with carrion — these are not valid subjects for mudaraba trade.
4
Distinguish from a fasid sale
A fasid (defective) sale is different because the buyer can still sell the item after possession, so profit is still achievable.
5
Apply the consequence: mudarib buys for himself
If the mudarib violates this prohibition, the purchase is binding on him personally, not on the mudaraba — analogous to a purchasing agent who acts contrary to instructions.

مضارب کو رب المال کے قریبی رشتہ دار خریدنے کی اجازت نہیں قَالَ وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُصَارِبِ أَنْ يَشْتَرِى مَنْ يَعْتِقُ عَلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ لِقَرَابَةٍ أَوْ غَيْرِهَا لِأَنَّ الْعَقْدَ وُضِعَ لِتَحْصِيلِ الربح وذلِكَ بالتَّصَرُّفِ مَرَّةً بَعْدَ أُخْرَى وَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ فِيهِ لِعِلْقِهِ وَهَذَا لَا يَدْخُلُ فِى الْمُضَارَبَةِ شِرَاءَ مَا لَا يُمْلَكُ بِالْقَبْضِ كَشِرَاءِ الْخَمْرِ وَالشَّرَاءِ بِالْمَيْتَةِ بِخِلَافِ الْبَيْعِ الْفَاسِد لأَنَّهُ يُمْكِنُهُ بَيْعُهُ بَعْدَ قَبْضِهِ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ الْمَقْصُودُ. قَالَ وَلَوْ فَعَلَ صَارَ مُشْتَرِبًا لِنَفْسِهِ دُونَ الْمُضَارَبَةِ أَنَّ الشَّرَاءَ مَتَى وَجَدَ نِفَاذَا عَلَى الْمُشْتَرِى نَفَذَ عَلَيْهِ كَالْوَكِيْلِ بِالشِّرَى إِذَا خَالَفَ ترجمہ اور اختیار نہیں مضارب کو یہ کہ خریدے اس کو جو آزاد ہو جائے مالک پر قرابت وغیرہ کی وجہ سے۔ کیونکہ عقد موضوع ہے تحصیل نفع کے لئے اور یہ بار بار تصرف کرنے سے ہوگا اور یہ بات اس میں متحقق نہیں ہو سکتی اس کے آزاد ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اسی لئے مضاربت میں ایسی چیز کی خرید داخل نہیں ہوتی جو قبضہ سے ملک میں نہ آئے جیسے شراب کی خرید اور مردار کے عوض کسی چیز کی خرید بخلاف بیع فاسد کے۔ کیونکہ اس کو قبضہ کے بعد فروخت کر سکتا ہے۔ پس مقصود تحقیق ہو جائے گا۔ اگر اس نے ایسا کیا تو اپنے لئے خریدنے والا ہوگا نہ کہ مضاربت پر ۔ اس لئے کہ خرید جب مشتری پر نفاذ پائے تااس پر نافذ ہو جاتی ہے جیسے خرید کا وکیل جب مخالفت کرے۔ تشریح... قوله وليس لِلْمُضَارِب "اگر کوئی غلام رب المال کا ذی رحم محرم ہو یا اس نے قسم کھالی ہو کہ اگر میں فلاں غلام خریدوں تو وہ آزاد ہے تو
The mudarib is not permitted to buy one who would become free upon the rabb al-mal due to kinship or other reason. Because the contract (mudaraba) is established for profit, and that (profit) occurs through repeated transactions, and it cannot be realized in this (purchase) due to its (the slave's) manumission. And this purchase does not enter into mudaraba, like buying items that are not owned by possession, such as buying wine or buying with carrion, unlike a fasid sale because one can sell after possession, so the purpose can be achieved. He said: If he does so, he becomes a buyer for himself, not for the mudaraba, because when a purchase is effective for the buyer, it applies to him, just as a purchasing agent when he acts contrary. Translation: And the mudarib is not allowed to buy one who becomes free upon the owner due to kinship or otherwise. Because the contract is for profit, and that (profit) occurs through repeated transactions, and this cannot be realized due to his becoming free. For this reason, buying something that cannot be owned by possession is not included in mudaraba, like buying wine or buying with carrion, unlike a fasid sale because one can sell after possession, so the purpose will be achieved. If he did so, he becomes a buyer for himself, not for the mudaraba, because when purchase is effective on the buyer, it applies to him, like a purchasing agent when he acts contrary. Commentary: ... His saying: 'And not for the mudarib' — if a slave is a mahram relative of the rabb al-mal, or if the owner had taken an oath that if he buys such-and-such slave, he will be free, then...
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya discusses a prohibition on the mudarib buying a slave who would be automatically emancipated upon ownership by the rabb al-mal, either due to a close blood relationship (like a son or father) or due to a prior oath or other cause. The ruling is that the mudarib is not permitted to make such a purchase within the mudaraba because the very purpose of mudaraba is profit through repeated trade. If the bought slave becomes free immediately upon entering the ownership of the rabb al-mal, there is no possibility of selling him again for profit. Therefore, the purpose of mudaraba is defeated. The text draws an analogy with buying items that cannot be owned legally, like wine or buying with carrion — these are not valid subjects of trade in mudaraba. However, a fasid (defective) sale is distinguished because the buyer can still sell the item after possession, so profit is possible. If the mudarib violates this prohibition and buys such a slave, the purchase is not for the mudaraba but for the mudarib personally. The reasoning is analogous to a purchasing agent (wakīl) who acts contrary to his instructions — the transaction is valid but it binds the agent himself, not the principal. The commentary begins to elaborate that if the slave is a mahram relative or if the owner had sworn to free the slave upon purchase, the same ruling applies. (The text cuts off, but the principle is clear.)

Key Terms
یعتق (ya‘tiq): He becomes free/emancipated; the legal category of manumission.
قرابت (qarābah): Kinship; close blood relationship that results in automatic emancipation.
بیع فاسد (bay‘ fāsid): A defective sale that can be corrected or whose subject can be sold after possession.
وکیل بالشراء (wakīl bi al-shirā’): An agent authorized to buy; if he acts contrary, the purchase binds him personally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the mudarib buys a slave who is the father of the rabb al-mal?
A) The purchase is valid for the mudaraba
B) The purchase is for the mudarib personally
C) The mudaraba becomes invalid
D) The slave is freed and the capital is lost

Key Takeaway
A mudarib cannot buy a slave who would be freed automatically; if he does, the purchase is his personal liability.

The Binding Effect of the Owner's Personal Specification in Mudarabah
Ruling with proof (talil) on ta'yin in mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mudarib's obligation to follow the owner's personal naming of a trading partner and distinguish it from categorical or locational specifications.

Core Idea
A mudarib must trade only with the person named by the owner; naming a class does not restrict individuals.

Mudarabah gives the mudarib agency to trade, but the owner may restrict that agency by specifying a trading partner. The Hanafi school draws a critical line between naming a particular person and naming a category or place. This lesson unpacks that distinction and the rationale behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the owner's specification
Determine whether the owner has named a specific individual (e.g., 'Buy from Zaid') or a general category (e.g., 'Buy from the people of Kufah'). This is the key factual question.
The wording 'from so-and-so' (min fulan) indicates a named person; 'from the people of Kufah' indicates a category.
2
Classify the type of ta'yin
Distinguish between ta'yin shakhsi (personal specification) and ta'yin naw'i (categorical specification). The former is binding, the latter is not binding on individuals.
The source text uses 'ismi ta'yin' (naming by name) vs. specifying a place or type.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
If the owner named a person, the mudarib must trade with that person only. If the owner named a category, the mudarib may trade with anyone falling within that category.
The ruling is based on the owner's trust being person-specific; outcomes of trade vary with persons.
4
Understand the rationale (talil)
The owner's personal trust in a specific individual is a legitimate restriction of the mudarib's agency. Trade results differ by person, so the owner's confidence is a valid consideration.
This is a maslahah-based reasoning: protecting the owner's interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله لان الواو و للعطف ..... الخ - اس پر سوال ہوتا ہے کہ اس واؤ کو حال کے لئے کیوں نہیں لیا گیا جیسے ادالتی الفا وانت حریر برائے حال ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ و اعمل یہ جملہ انشائیہ ہے اور علوم عربیہ سے یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ جمل انشائیہ میں حال ہونے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہوتی۔ واؤ کے ساتھ ہوں یا بلا واؤ ہوں۔
قـولـه عـلـى ان تشترى من فلان ... الخ - اگر رب المان نے تجارتی معاملہ کے لئے کسی شخص کی اسما تعیین کردی و ی تعیین سی ہوگی کہ فائدہ سے خالی نہیں۔ کیونکہ تجارت اختلاف اشخاص کے لحاظ سے مختلف ہوتی ہے اور مالک نے معاملات میں شخص معین پر زیادہ اعتماد کیا ہے تو اس کے خلاف کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر مالک نے اسمی تعیین کے بغیر یوں کہا کہ اہل کوفہ کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کر، یا بیع صرف میں کہا کہ صرافوں کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کر اور مضارب نے کوفہ میں اہل کوفہ یا صرافوں کے علاوہ کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کی تو یہ جائز ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اول کا مقصد صرف مکان اور جگہ کی تخصیص ہے کہ کوفہ میں ہونی چاہیے اور ثانی کا مقصد نوع تجارت کی تخصیص ہے کہ بیچ صرف ہونی چاہئے ۔ کہنے کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ اس سے اشخاص کی تخصیص مقصود نہیں ہوتی۔
His statement: 'Because the waw is for conjunction...' - There is a question: Why was this waw not taken as for hal, like 'adkhalta al-alfa wa anta harir' is for hal? The answer is that this sentence is inshaiyyah, and from Arabic sciences it is established that an inshaiyyah sentence does not have the capacity to be hal, whether with waw or without waw.  His statement: 'On the condition that you buy from so-and-so...' - If the owner of the capital designated a specific person by name for the commercial transaction, this designation is effective and not free from benefit. Because trade varies depending on differences of persons, and the owner has placed more trust in that specific person in transactions, so going against it is not permissible. Yes, if the owner without naming a person said: 'Buy and sell with the people of Kufah', or in sarf exchange said: 'Buy and sell with the money-changers', and the mudarib in Kufah bought and sold with other than the people of Kufah or the money-changers, then this is permissible. Because the first aims only at specifying the location that it should be in Kufah, and the second aims at specifying the type of trade that it should be sarf. The intent of saying is that specification of persons is not intended.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on two related points. First, the grammatical objection that the waw in the owner's statement might be interpreted as hal (circumstantial) rather than conjunction is refuted: the sentence is inshai' (performative) and thus cannot serve as hal. Second, the substantive ruling: when the owner explicitly names a person for the mudarib to trade with, that designation is binding because trade outcomes differ with persons and the owner's confidence is specific. However, if the owner specifies a class (e.g., people of Kufah) or a type (e.g., money-changers), the mudarib may trade with others within that locality or type, as the intent is spatial or categorical, not personal.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification by name or class by the owner in a mudarabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the owner says to the mudarib: 'Buy from Zaid,' may the mudarib buy from 'Amr instead?
A) Yes, because mudarib has authority to trade freely.
B) No, because the owner's specification of a person is binding.
C) Yes, if the mudarib expects better profit from 'Amr.
D) No, unless the owner also says 'or others'.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an owner's personal naming of a trading partner in mudarabah is binding because trade outcomes differ with persons; categorical specifications do not restrict the mudarib to specific individuals.

Time Limit in Mudarabah Renders Contract Void After Expiry
Ruling that a time-limited mudarabah terminates automatically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a time-limited mudarabah and apply the qiyas reasoning from wakalah to determine the contract's status after expiry.

Core Idea
A mudarabah with a fixed term ends automatically when the time expires – like a time-bound agency.

Mudarabah is a partnership in profit where the investor (rabb al-mal) entrusts capital to a manager (mudarib). Can this relationship be limited by a specific time? The Hanafi school says yes, and this lesson unpacks the proof: mudarabah is a form of agency (wakalah), and agency can be time-bound. Once the fixed period ends, the contract automatically terminates. Understanding this helps avoid disputes over post-expiry profits and losses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses a mudarabah contract with a fixed time limit. What is the ruling when that time passes? The text says يبطُلُ العقدُ بمضيه – the contract becomes void with its passing. Note: it is not void from the beginning, only after expiry.
The contract is valid until the end of the term.
2
Trace the proof – qiyas to wakalah
The author gives the proof: لأنَّه توكيل فيتوفَّت بما وفَّته – because mudarabah is an agency, so it ends with what it was timed. This is qiyas jaliy: the effective cause (illah) is that mudarabah fundamentally involves agency (wakalah). Since wakalah can be time-limited, mudarabah can too.
The analogy extends to restriction by type and place, mentioned in the text.
3
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
The Hanafi position is that tawqit (fixing a time) is effective. However, this is mukhtalaf fih – some other schools may not allow time-limiting a mudarabah, considering it either void ab initio or continuing indefinitely. The practical difference is who bears post‑expiry profit or loss.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is clear: the contract terminates automatically.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Consider: investor A gives mudarib B 10,000 for one year. After one year, B continues trading without A's permission. According to this ruling, the contract ended; B is now a trespasser. Any profit belongs to A (owner) and B gets no share unless they agree to a new contract.
This prevents confusion over authority after the fixed term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ. وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ وَقَتَ لِلْمُضَارَبَةِ وَقْتًا بِعَيْنِهِ يَبْطُلُ الْعَقْدُ بِمُضِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ تَوْكِيْلٌ فَيَتَوَفَّتُ بِمَا وَفَّتَه وَالتَّوْقِيتُ مُفِيدٌ فَإِنَّهُ تَقْسِيدٌ بِالزَّمَانِ فَصَارَ كَالتَّقْلِيدِ بِالنَّوْعِ وَالْمَكَانِ
ترجمہ ایسے ہی اگر مضاربت کے لئے معین وقت محدود کیا ہو تو اس کے گزرنے سے عقد باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو کیل ہے تو جس کے ساتھ موقت کیا ہے اسی تک رہے گی اور توقیت مفید بھی ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک زمانہ کی قید ہے تو نوع و مقام کی قید کی طرح ہو گئی۔
He said: Similarly, if he specified for the mudarabah a specific time, the contract becomes void with its passing, because it is a wakalah (agency), so it ends with what it was timed with, and timing is effective because it is a restriction by time, so it becomes like restriction by type and place. Translation: Likewise, if a specific limited time was fixed for the mudarabah, then upon its passing the contract becomes void. Because this is a wakalah, so it will last only as long as it was timed, and timing is beneficial because it is a restriction of time, so it becomes like the restriction of type and place.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof: the mudarabah contract, being a form of agency (wakalah), can be limited by time. Once the specified time passes, the contract automatically terminates. The proof is analogy (qiyas jaliy): just as restriction by type or place is effective, restriction by time is equally effective. The Urdu clarifies: the contract is void (batil) after the time elapses, not void ab initio. The mudarib's authority ends at the expiry.

Key Terms
توقيت (tawqit): Fixing a time limit for the duration of the mudarabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a mudarabah contract that was set for one year after one year passes?
A) The contract continues until both parties agree to end it.
B) The contract becomes void automatically.
C) The mudarib retains authority until the owner revokes.
D) The contract is void from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
A mudarabah with a fixed time term is valid but automatically terminates upon the expiry of that term, as it is analogous to a time-limited agency.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Mudarib Cannot Buy a Relative Freed on the Owner
Ruling with proof via qiyas and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib purchasing a slave who would become free on the capital owner, explain the ʿilla (cause) using qiyas, and identify the consequence if the mudarib proceeds.

Core Idea
A mudarib cannot buy a slave who would be freed on the owner—profit is impossible, so the purchase is for the mudarib personally.

In mudarabah, the mudarib trades with the owner's capital to generate profit. But what if the mudarib buys a slave who, due to kinship or an oath, would become free immediately upon purchase? This lesson explores why such a purchase defeats the purpose of mudarabah and how the Hanafi school treats it as a prohibited transaction that, if done, binds the mudarib personally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mudarib purchasing a slave who would become free on the capital owner due to qarabah (close kinship) or other causes (e.g., an oath). The ruling is that this is not permissible (makruh tahrimi) and not considered part of the mudarabah.
The ruling is near haram because it frustrates the objective of profit.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author uses qiyas (analogy) to show that this purchase is outside the scope of mudarabah. The text compares it to buying wine (which cannot be owned) or bartering with carrion (a batil sale).
The proof is based on the ʿilla that the purchased item cannot be further traded for profit.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The ʿilla is that the purchase immediately frees the slave, making further transactions impossible. Thus, profit cannot be realized, contradicting the contract's purpose.
This is a clear case of tahqiq al-manat: the ʿilla is directly present in the farʿ.
4
Distinguish from similar cases
A fasid (defective) sale is allowed because the item becomes owned and can be resold. An absolute agent (wakil mutlaq) is also allowed because his mandate is unrestricted, unlike mudarib whose mandate is implicitly restricted to profit-generating purchases.
The distinction hinges on whether profit is possible after possession.
5
Apply the consequence
If the mudarib buys such a slave, the purchase is valid but for himself, not the mudarabah. He must return the capital to the owner and keep the slave (who becomes free on the owner, so effectively the mudarib loses the capital value).
The mudarib becomes liable for the capital as if he misappropriated it.

Source Text

قَالَ وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُصَارِبِ أَنْ يَشْتَرِى مَنْ يَعْتِقُ عَلَى رَبِّ الْمَالِ لِقَرَابَةٍ أَوْ غَيْرِهَا لِأَنَّ الْعَقْدَ وُضِعَ لِتَحْصِيلِ الربح وذلِكَ بالتَّصَرُّفِ مَرَّةً بَعْدَ أُخْرَى وَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ فِيهِ لِعِلْقِهِ وَهَذَا لَا يَدْخُلُ فِى الْمُضَارَبَةِ شِرَاءَ مَا لَا يُمْلَكُ بِالْقَبْضِ كَشِرَاءِ الْخَمْرِ وَالشَّرَاءِ بِالْمَيْتَةِ بِخِلَافِ الْبَيْعِ الْفَاسِد لأَنَّهُ يُمْكِنُهُ بَيْعُهُ بَعْدَ قَبْضِهِ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ الْمَقْصُودُ. قَالَ وَلَوْ فَعَلَ صَارَ مُشْتَرِبًا لِنَفْسِهِ دُونَ الْمُضَارَبَةِ أَنَّ الشَّرَاءَ مَتَى وَجَدَ نِفَاذَا عَلَى الْمُشْتَرِى نَفَذَ عَلَيْهِ كَالْوَكِيْلِ بِالشِّرَى إِذَا خَالَفَ
تشریح... قوله وليس لِلْمُضَارِب "اگر کوئی غلام رب المال کا ذی رحم محرم ہو یا اس نے قسم کھالی ہو کہ اگر میں فلاں غلام خریدوں تو وہ آزاد ہے تو مضارب کے لئے ایسے غلام کو خریدنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ عقد مضاربت تحصیل منفعت کے لئے ہے اور تحصیل منفعت اس besturdubooks.wordpress سکتی ۔ تصرف ہو۔ اور غلام مذکور کی خرید میں یہ چیز متصور نہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ رب المال پر آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ قـولــه ولهذا لا يدخل ... الخ یعنی اسی وجہ سے کہ خرید مذکور کی صورت میں تصرف ناممکن ہے مضاربت میں ایسی چیز کی خرید داخل نہیں ہوتی جو قبضہ سے ملک میں نہ آئے جیسے شراب کی خرید کہ مسلمان کی ملک میں نہیں آسکتی۔ اسی طرح مردار کے عوض کسی چیز کی خرید کہ یہ بیع باطل ہے یہاں تک کہ جو چیز مردار کے عوض خریدی ہے وہ قبضہ سے بھی ملک میں نہیں آئے گی۔ بخلاف بیع فاسد کے کہ وہ مضاربت کے تحت میں داخل ہے اس لئے کہ جو چیز بیع فاسد کے طور پر خریدی ہے اس کو قبضہ کے بعد فروخت کر سکتا ہے پس تحصیل نفع جو اصل مقصد ہے وہ حاصل ہو جائے گا۔ سوال اگر کوئی شخص علی الاطلاق ایک ہزار کے عوض غلام خریدنے کا وکیل ہوا اوروہ ایسا نظام خرید لے جو موکل پر آزاد ہو جائے گا تو یہ جائز ہے اور اس کو مخالف حکم قرار نہیں دیا جاتا اس کی کیا وجہ ہے؟ جواب . وجہ یہ ہے کہ وکالت مطلق ہے اور مضاربت ایسی ہی خرید کے ساتھ مقید ہے جو نافع ہو۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر مؤکل نے یہ کہا۔ اشتر لی عبداً بالف ابيعه تو آزاد ہو جانے والا غلام خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
قوله ولو فعل .... اگر مضارب نے ایساہی غلام خرید لیا جورب المال پر آزاد ہو جائے گا تو یہ خرید مضاربت پر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ وہ اپنے لئے خریدنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جو خرید ایسی ہو کہ مشتری پر اس کا نافذ ہونا ممکن ہو تو مشتری پر نافذ ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے وکیل بالشراء اگر حکم موکل کے خلاف کرے تو خرید اسی پر نافذ ہوگی۔
He said: The mudarib may not buy one who would become free on the owner of the capital due to kinship or otherwise, because the contract was established for obtaining profit, and that is through repeated transactions, and it cannot be realized in this [purchase] due to its being a cause of freedom. And this [type of purchase] does not enter into mudarabah: buying what cannot be owned by possession, like buying wine or buying with carrion, unlike a fasid (defective) sale because it is possible for him to sell it after possession, so the objective is realized. He said: If he does so, he becomes a buyer for himself, not for the mudarabah, because the purchase, whenever it is effective upon the buyer, takes effect on him, like the agent for purchase when he violates [instructions].
Explanation: His statement: 'And the mudarib may not...' If a slave is a close relative (dhi rahm mahram) of the owner of the capital, or the owner has taken an oath that if I buy such-and-such slave he is free, then it is not permissible for the mudarib to buy such a slave. Because the mudarabah contract is for obtaining profit, and obtaining profit is [through] transactions. And in the purchase of the mentioned slave, this thing is not conceivable because he will become free on the owner of the capital. His statement: 'And for this reason, does not enter...' That is, for the same reason that in the mentioned purchase transaction is impossible, mudarabah does not include the purchase of something that does not become owned by possession, like buying wine because a Muslim cannot own it, similarly buying something in exchange for carrion because this is a batil sale, so that what is bought in exchange for carrion does not become owned by possession either. Unlike a fasid sale, for it is included under mudarabah because the item bought in a fasid sale can be sold after possession, so obtaining profit, which is the primary objective, is achieved. 
Question: If a person is absolutely appointed as an agent to buy a slave for one thousand, and he buys a slave who would become free on the principal, this is permissible and is not considered a violation; what is the reason? Answer: The reason is that wakalah is absolute, while mudarabah is restricted to a purchase that is beneficial. So much so that if the principal said, 'Buy for me a slave for one thousand to sell,' then buying a slave who would become free would not be permissible.
His statement: 'And if he does...' If the mudarib bought a slave who would become free on the owner of the capital, then this purchase is not for the mudarabah; rather, he becomes a buyer for himself. Because any purchase that can be effective upon the buyer is effective upon him, like the agent for purchase if he violates the principal's instruction.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling with proof on the prohibition of the mudarib purchasing anyone who would become free upon the owner of the capital due to kinship (e.g., a father, son) or other cause (e.g., a vow or oath of emancipation). The reason: the objective of mudarabah is profit through successive transactions, but here the slave would be freed immediately upon purchase, preventing any further trade and profit. Therefore, such a purchase is not included in the mudarabah contract. The text analogizes this to buying wine (cannot be owned) or bartering with carrion (batil sale, no ownership). In contrast, a fasid (defective) sale is allowed because the item becomes owned by possession and can be resold. If the mudarib proceeds to buy such a slave, the purchase is valid but for himself, not the mudarabah, because the purchase is enforceable on him as buyer, similar to a violating agent. A question arises: why is an absolute agent (wakil mutlaq) allowed to buy such a slave? Because the agency is unrestricted, whereas mudarabah is inherently conditioned on profitability. Even in agency, if the principal says 'buy to sell,' the restriction applies.

Key Terms
من يعتق على رب المال (man ya'tiqu 'ala rabb al-mal): A person who would become free on the capital owner due to kinship (e.g., father, son, or mahram) or other cause (e.g., an oath taken by the owner).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, why is a mudarib prohibited from buying a slave who would become free on the capital owner?
A) Because the purchase is void (batil) and cannot be completed.
B) Because the purchase prevents the possibility of profit through subsequent transactions.
C) Because the mudarib does not have the right to buy any property without owner's permission.
D) Because the slave is a relative of the mudarib, causing a conflict of interest.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib cannot buy a slave who would become free on the capital owner; if he does, the purchase is for himself and he must replace the capital.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate

Profit and No-Profit Scenarios in Buying Relatives in Mudarabah
Ruling with legal reasoning (talil) on mudarabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mudarib buying a relative when the mudarabah capital has profit versus when it has no profit, and explain the underlying legal reasoning.

Core Idea
A mudarib may only buy a relative who would become free on him when there is no profit in the capital, because profit creates a partnership that prevents the valid transaction.

In mudarabah, the mudarib is entrusted with capital to trade, and any profit is shared. When the capital itself has profit (i.e., the mudarib already has a share in the capital due to accrued profit), buying a relative who would become free on him creates a conflict. This lesson unpacks the ruling and reasoning from Al-Hidayah, clarifying when such a purchase is permissible and the consequences if done otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contrasts two situations: when the mudarabah capital has profit (ribh) and when it does not. Identify the ruling for each.
2
Understand the reasoning for impermissibility with profit
When profit exists, the mudarib has a share in the capital. Buying a relative would cause partial freedom on his share and spoil the owner's share, preventing the objective of mudarabah (profit generation).
The 'well-known difference' refers to whether the free portion is determined by value or number of shares.
3
Understand the reasoning for permissibility without profit
When there is no profit, the mudarib has no ownership in the capital, so no partnership. The purchase is valid; if the slave's value later increases, the mudarib's share (from profit) becomes free, but he is not liable for the increase.
4
Apply the ruling to a new case
Given a mudarib who wants to buy his father from the mudarabah capital, determine the ruling based on whether profit has been earned.
Consider the practical implication for the mudarib's liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ لَمْ يَجُزُ لَهُ أَنْ يَشْتِرَى مَنْ يَعْتِقَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ يَعْتِقُ عَلَيْهِ نَصِيبُهُ وَيُفْسِدُ نَصِيبَ رَبِّ الْمَالِ أَوْ يَعْتِقَ عَلَى الْاِخْتِلَافِ الْمَعْرُوفِ فَيَمْتَنِعُ التَّصَرُّفَ فَلَا يَحْصُلُ الْمَقْصُودُ وَإِن اشْتَرَاهُمْ ضَمِنَ مَالَ الْمُضَارَبَةِ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ مُشْتَرِيَا لِلْعَبْدِ فَيَضْمَنُ بِالنَّقْدِ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ جَازَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِيَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَانِعَ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ إِذْ لَا شِرْكَةَ لَهُ فِيهِ لِيَعْتَقَ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ زَادَتْ قِيْمَتُهُمْ بَعْدَ الشَّرَى عَتَقَ نَصِيبُهُ مِنْهُمْ لِمِلْكِهِ بَعْضَ قَرِيبِهِ وَلَمْ يَضْمَن لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ شَيْئًا لِأَنَّهُ لَا صَنَعَ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فِي زِيَادَةِ الْقِيِّمَةِ وَلَا فِي مِلْكِهِ الزِيَادَة لِاَنَّ هَذَا شَيْءٌ يَثْبُتُ مِنْ طَرِيْقِ الْحُكْمِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا وَرَثَهُ مَعَ غَيْرِهِ وَيَسْعَى الْعَبْدُ فِي قِيْمَةِ نَصِيبِهِ مِنْهُ لأَنَّهُ احْتُبِسَتْ مَالِيَتُه عِنْدَهُ فَيَسْعَى فِيْهِ كَمَا فِي الْوِرَاثَةِ
ترجمہ اگر مال میں نفع ہو تو مضارب کے لئے ایسا شخص خرید نا جائز نہیں جو اس پر آزاد ہو جائے کیونکہ اس کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور بالمال کا حصہ فاسد یا آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ بنا پر اس اختلاف کے جو معروف ہے پس تصرف ممتنع ہوگا۔ تو مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے ایسے لوگوں کو خریدا تو مال مضاربت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ غلام کو اپنے لئے خریدنے والا ہو گیا تو مضاربت کا مال دینے سے ضامن ہوگا۔ اور اگر مال میں نفع نہ ہو تو ان کو خریدنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ تصرف سے کوئی مانع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مال میں اس کی کوئی شرکت نہیں یہاں تک کہ وہ اس پر آزاد ہوں۔ پھر اگران کی قیمت بڑھ جائے خریدنے کے بعد تو اُن میں سے مضارب کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اپنے رشتہ دار کے بعض کا مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور وہ رب المال کے لئے کسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی حرکت نہیں قیمت بڑھ جانے میں اور نہ بڑھتی کے مالک ہونے میں اس
He said: If there is profit in the capital, it is not permissible for him to buy one who would become free on him, because his share becomes free and corrupts the share of the owner of the capital, or becomes free according to the well-known difference, so transaction is prevented and the objective is not achieved. And if he buys them, he becomes liable for the mudarabah capital because he becomes a buyer of the slave, so he becomes liable by paying from the mudarabah capital. And if there is no profit in the capital, it is permissible for him to buy them, because there is no preventing factor from transaction since there is no partnership for him in it such that they would become free on him. Then if their value increases after the purchase, his share from them becomes free due to his owning part of his relative, and he is not liable to the owner of the capital for anything, because there is no action from his side in the increase in value, nor in his ownership of the increase, because this is something established by way of legal ruling, so it is like when he inherits it with others. And the slave must work to earn the value of his share from him, because his monetary value is detained with him, so he works for it as in inheritance.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling when the mudarabah capital already has profit (i.e., the mudarib has a share in the capital due to profit) versus when there is no profit. When profit exists, the mudarib has a partial ownership in the capital, so buying a relative would cause part of the slave to become free and spoil the owner's share, preventing further profit. Hence it is impermissible, and if done, the mudarib is liable for the capital (he must pay back). When there is no profit, the mudarib has no ownership in the capital, so buying the relative is permissible; the slave would become free on the mudarib only if the value increases after purchase (since then the mudarib's share from profit would be a part). But the mudarib is not liable for the increase because it is a legal consequence, not his action. The slave must then work to pay off the value of the mudarib's share, similar to co-inheritance situations.

Key Terms
ربح (ribh): Profit in the mudarabah capital; the mudarib's share in the capital once accrued.
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership in profit where one party provides capital (rabb al-mal) and the other works (mudarib).
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner in a mudarabah contract.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The capital provider in a mudarabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when may a mudarib permissibly buy a slave relative from the mudarabah capital?
A) Only when the owner gives express permission.
B) Only when there is no profit in the capital at the time of purchase.
C) Only when the slave is not a relative closer than a cousin.
D) Never, because it is always a conflict of interest.

Key Takeaway
In mudarabah, the mudarib may only buy a relative who would become free on him if the capital has no profit; otherwise, the purchase is void and he becomes liable.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
12 min
Mudarib Purchasing a Relative Slave: Profit vs No Profit
Core matn and commentary on mudarib purchasing a relative slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib purchasing a relative who would become free, distinguishing between profit and no-profit scenarios, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on divisibility of emancipation.

Core Idea
Emancipation of a relative slave upon purchase defeats mudarabah's purpose; the ruling depends on profit existence and the school's view on whether 'itq is divisible.

In a mudarabah contract, the mudarib is authorized to trade for profit. But what if he buys a close relative who would instantly become free upon ownership? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, which flips depending on whether the mudarabah capital has generated profit. The dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn over whether emancipation can be partial adds another layer that affects the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that the mudarib is using mudarabah capital to purchase a slave who is his mahram relative (e.g., father, son). The purchase triggers immediate emancipation of the mudarib's share, and possibly the entire slave.
The key is that the slave becomes free upon the mudarib because of the closeness of relationship.
2
State the ruling for profit and no-profit scenarios
When there is profit in the mudarabah capital, the mudarib must not purchase such a slave; if he does, the purchase is for himself and he guarantees the capital. When there is no profit, the purchase is valid because the mudarib has no share yet.
Profit means the slave's value exceeds the capital, giving the mudarib a share.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi difference on 'itq
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation is divisible (qabil li al-tajzi), so only the mudarib's share becomes free; the rabb al-mal's share remains his property. The Sahibayn hold that emancipation cannot be split, so the entire slave becomes free immediately.
This difference leads to different consequences for the mudarib's liability.
4
Apply the rulings to the profit scenario
If profit exists and the mudarib buys a relative, both views agree the purchase is invalid for mudarabah. Under Abu Hanifa, the rabb al-mal can choose to free, employ, or seek compensation from the mudarib. Under the Sahibayn, the whole slave is free and the mudarib must compensate the rabb al-mal for his share.
The practical outcome (thamarah al-khilaf) is the mudarib's liability.
5
Apply the rulings to the no-profit scenario with price increase
If initially no profit, the purchase is valid. If later the slave's value increases, creating profit, the mudarib's share becomes free. But he is not liable because the increase happened by legal decree, not his action. The slave must work (sa'y) to pay the rabb al-mal's share.
This is analogous to inheritance, as detailed in the next lesson.

Source Text

كتاب المضاربة
مضارب کے لئے ایسے غلام کو خریدنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ عقد مضاربت تحصیل منفعت کے لئے ہے اور تحصیل منفعت اس تصرف ہو۔ اور غلام مذکور کی خرید میں یہ چیز متصور نہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ رب المال پر آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ قـولــه ولهذا لا يدخل ... الخ یعنی اسی وجہ سے کہ خرید مذکور کی صورت میں تصرف ناممکن ہے مضاربت میں ایسی چیز کی خرید داخل نہیں ہوتی جو قبضہ سے ملک میں نہ آئے جیسے شراب کی خرید کہ مسلمان کی ملک میں نہیں آسکتی۔ اسی طرح مردار کے عوض کسی چیز کی خرید کہ یہ بیع باطل ہے یہاں تک کہ جو چیز مردار کے عوض خریدی ہے وہ قبضہ سے بھی ملک میں نہیں آئے گی۔ بخلاف بیع فاسد کے کہ وہ مضاربت کے تحت میں داخل ہے اس لئے کہ جو چیز بیع فاسد کے طور پر خریدی ہے اس کو قبضہ کے بعد فروخت کر سکتا ہے پس تحصیل نفع جو اصل مقصد ہے وہ حاصل ہو جائے گا۔ سوال اگر کوئی شخص علی الاطلاق ایک ہزار کے عوض غلام خریدنے کا وکیل ہوا اوروہ ایسا نظام خرید لے جو موکل پر آزاد ہو جائے گا تو یہ جائز ہے اور اس کو مخالف حکم قرار نہیں دیا جاتا اس کی کیا وجہ ہے؟ جواب . وجہ یہ ہے کہ وکالت مطلق ہے اور مضاربت ایسی ہی خرید کے ساتھ مقید ہے جو نافع ہو۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر مؤکل نے یہ کہا۔ اشتر لی عبداً بالف ابيعه تو آزاد ہو جانے والا غلام خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
قوله ولو فعل .... اگر مضارب نے ایساہی غلام خرید لیا جورب المال پر آزاد ہو جائے گا تو یہ خرید مضاربت پر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ وہ اپنے لئے خریدنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جو خرید ایسی ہو کہ مشتری پر اس کا نافذ ہونا ممکن ہو تو مشتری پر نافذ ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے وکیل بالشراء اگر حکم موکل کے خلاف کرے تو خرید اسی پر نافذ ہوگی۔
مال میں نفع ہو تو بھی مضارب کے لئے رب المال کے قریبی رشتہ دار کو خریدنے کی اجازت نہیں
قَالَ فَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ لَمْ يَجُزُ لَهُ أَنْ يَشْتِرَى مَنْ يَعْتِقَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ يَعْتِقُ عَلَيْهِ نَصِيبُهُ وَيُفْسِدُ نَصِيبَ رَبِّ الْمَالِ أَوْ يَعْتِقَ عَلَى الْاِخْتِلَافِ الْمَعْرُوفِ فَيَمْتَنِعُ التَّصَرُّفَ فَلَا يَحْصُلُ الْمَقْصُودُ وَإِن اشْتَرَاهُمْ ضَمِنَ مَالَ الْمُضَارَبَةِ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ مُشْتَرِيَا لِلْعَبْدِ فَيَضْمَنُ بِالنَّقْدِ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ جَازَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِيَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَانِعَ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ إِذْ لَا شِرْكَةَ لَهُ فِيهِ لِيَعْتَقَ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ زَادَتْ قِيْمَتُهُمْ بَعْدَ الشَّرَى عَتَقَ نَصِيبُهُ مِنْهُمْ لِمِلْكِهِ بَعْضَ قَرِيبِهِ وَلَمْ يَضْمَن لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ شَيْئًا لِأَنَّهُ لَا صَنَعَ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فِي زِيَادَةِ الْقِيِّمَةِ وَلَا فِي مِلْكِهِ الزِيَادَة لِاَنَّ هَذَا شَيْءٌ يَثْبُتُ مِنْ طَرِيْقِ الْحُكْمِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا وَرَثَهُ مَعَ غَيْرِهِ وَيَسْعَى الْعَبْدُ فِي قِيْمَةِ نَصِيبِهِ مِنْهُ لأَنَّهُ احْتُبِسَتْ مَالِيَتُه عِنْدَهُ فَيَسْعَى فِيْهِ كَمَا فِي الْوِرَاثَةِ
ترجمہ اگر مال میں نفع ہو تو مضارب کے لئے ایسا شخص خرید نا جائز نہیں جو اس پر آزاد ہو جائے کیونکہ اس کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور بالمال کا حصہ فاسد یا آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ بنا پر اس اختلاف کے جو معروف ہے پس تصرف ممتنع ہوگا۔ تو مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے ایسے لوگوں کو خریدا تو مال مضاربت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ غلام کو اپنے لئے خریدنے والا ہو گیا تو مضاربت کا مال دینے سے ضامن ہوگا۔ اور اگر مال میں نفع نہ ہو تو ان کو خریدنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ تصرف سے کوئی مانع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مال میں اس کی کوئی شرکت نہیں یہاں تک کہ وہ اس پر آزاد ہوں۔ پھر اگران کی قیمت بڑھ جائے خریدنے کے بعد تو اُن میں سے مضارب کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اپنے رشتہ دار کے بعض کا مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور وہ رب المال کے لئے کسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی حرکت نہیں قیمت بڑھ جانے میں اور نہ بڑھتی کے مالک ہونے میں اس لئے کہ یہ تو ایسی چیز ہے۔ جو بطریق حکم ثابت ہوتی ہے تو ایسے ہو گیا جیسے وہ غیر کے ساتھ اس کا وارث ہو۔ اور غلام رب المال کے بقدر قیمت میں سعایت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ رب المال کی مالیت اس غلام کے پاس رک گئی ہے۔ پس وہ اس میں کمائی کرے جیسے وراثت کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح .. قوله فان كان في المال اگر مال میں نفع ہو تو مضارب کو ایسا غلام خریدنا بھی جائز نہیں جو مضارب کی طرف سے آزاد ہو جائے جیسے وہ غلام جو مضارب کا ذی رحم محرم ہو ۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں سے مضارب کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور صاحب مال کا حصہ یا تو بگڑ جائے گا ( امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ) یا وہ بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا (صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کو قدرے تشریح کے ساتھ یوں سمجھو کہ جب مال مضاربت میں نفع شریک ہے تو اس میں مضارب کا بھی حصہ ہے اور جب اس نے اپنے باپ یا بیٹے وغیرہ زور تم محرم کو خرید لیا تو وہ اس کی طرف سے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ مگر اسی قدر جتنا اس میں مضارب کا حصہ ہے۔ اب صاحبین کے نزدیک باقی بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں اعتقاق میں تجربی نہیں ہے۔ یعنی عشق کے ٹکڑے نہیں ہوتے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عشق چونکہ قابل تجزی ہے۔ اس لئے مالک کو اختیار ہو گا کہ چاہے آزاد کرے چاہے غلام سے کمائی کرائے چاہے مضارب سے تاوان لے (اگر وہ مالدار ہو ) بہر کیف غلام اس قابل نہیں رہا کہ فروخت ہو سکے۔ پس مالک کا حصہ بگڑ گیا اور یہ مضارب کے خریدنے کی وجہ سے ہوا۔ لہذا اس کا خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
قـولـه و ان لم يكن في المال ربح ... الخ - حکم مذکور اس وقت ہے جب مال مضاربت میں نفع ظاہر نہ ہوتو غلام مذکور کو مضاربت کے لئے خرید نا درست ہے۔ ظہور نفع سے مراد یہ ہے کہ غلام کی قیمت راس المال سے زیادہ ہو۔ کیونکہ جب غلام کی قیمت راس المال کے برابر یا اس سے کم ہو گی تو اس غلام میں مضارب کی ملک ظاہر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ غلام راس المال کے ساتھ مشغول رہے گا تو اگر راس المال اولاً ایک ہزار ہو پھر دس ہزار ہو جائے اس کے بعد مضارب اس غلام کو خریدے جو اس پر آزاد ہو جائے اور اس کی قیمت ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہوتو وہ اس پر آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ قوله فان زادت قيمتهم .... الخ یعنی جس وقت مضارب نے قرابتدار غلام خریدا تھا اس وقت تو اس کی قیمت راس المال کے برابر تھی مگر بعد میں اس کی قیمت بڑھ گئی تو بقدر حصہ مضاربت غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے قرابتدار کا مالک ہو گیا۔ لیکن مضارب پر رب المال کے حصہ کا ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ملک کے وقت غلام مضارب کی حرکت سے آزاد نہیں ہوا بلکہ بلا اختیار مضارب قیمت بڑھ جانے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہوا ہے۔ پس غلام رب المال کے حصہ کی قیمت میں سعایت کرے گا۔ لانه احتبسبت ماليته عنده
قوله كما اذا اورثه مع غيره .... الخ - اس مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مثلاً ایک عورت کے شوہر نے زمانہ سابق میں زید کی باندی سے نکاح کیا تھا جس سے ایک لڑکا ہوا اور وہ اپنے ماں کی طرح زید کا غلام رہا۔ پھر اس شخص نے مذکورہ آزاد عورت نکاح کر لیا اور اس عورت نے زید سے اپنے شوہر کا بیٹا خرید لیا اور وہ اس کی مالکہ ہو گئی اس کے بعد عورت کا انتقال ہو گیا اور اس نے اپنا شوہر اور ایک بھائی چھوڑا تو ترکہ دونوں میں نصفا نصف مشترک ہوگا ۔ پس لڑکے کا نصف حصہ بھائی کی ملک میں اور نصف شوہر کی ملک میں آ گیا۔ لیکن لڑکا چونکہ شوہر کا بیٹا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ ملک میں آتے ہی فورا اپنے باپ پر آزاد ہو گیا۔ اب باپ اپنی زوجہ کے بھائی کے لئے کسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ آزاد کرنا س کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ میراث جو حکم خداوندی ہے اس کی وجہ سے ملک ثابت ہوئی اور ملک ثابت ہوتے ہی وہ حکماً آزاد ہو گیا پس باپ ان دونوں باتوں میں بے قصور ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں مضارب کا حال ہے کہ اس نے اپنے محارم کو اپنی شرکت کے بغیر اس لئے خریدا تھا۔ کہ ان کے مالک کے لئے فروخت کرے مگر ناگاہ ان کی قیمت بڑھ گئی (اور قیمت کا بڑھ جانا مضارب کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے ) اور جب قیمت بڑھ جانے سے نفع میں اس کی شرکت ہو گئی تو بقدر شرکت اس کو ملک حاصل ہوئی اور اس قدر حصہ آزاد ہو گیا اور یہ بھی اس کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے اور جب اس نے کوئی ایسی حرکت نہیں کی جس سے رب المال کا نقصان ہو تو وہ ضامن بھی نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Mudarabah. It is not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a slave [who would become free upon the rabb al-mal]. Because the contract of mudarabah is for the acquisition of profit, and acquisition of profit is through disposal. And in the purchase of the mentioned slave, this thing is not conceivable because he would become free upon the rabb al-mal. His statement: 'wa-li-hadha la yadkhulu...' etc., meaning: for this reason that in the case of the mentioned purchase, disposal is impossible; in mudarabah, the purchase of a thing that does not come into ownership by possession is not included, like the purchase of wine which cannot come into the ownership of a Muslim. Similarly, the purchase of something in exchange for carrion, because this sale is batil, so much so that the thing purchased in exchange for carrion will not come into ownership even by possession. Unlike a fasid sale, which is included under mudarabah, because the thing purchased by fasid sale can be sold after possession; thus the acquisition of profit, which is the original objective, is attained. Question: If a person is appointed as an absolute agent to purchase a slave for one thousand, and he purchases such a slave who would become free upon the principal, this is permissible and is not considered a contrary ruling. What is the reason? Answer: The reason is that agency is absolute, while mudarabah is restricted to a purchase that is profitable. So much so that if the principal said, 'Buy for me a slave for one thousand so that I may sell him,' then purchasing a slave who would become free would not be permissible. His statement: 'wa-law fa'ala...' If the mudarib did purchase such a slave who would become free upon the rabb al-mal, then this purchase is not for the mudarabah; rather he becomes a purchaser for himself. Because any purchase that can be executed upon the purchaser is executed upon him, just as if an agent appointed to purchase acts against the principal's instruction, the purchase is executed upon him. Even if there is profit in the capital, the mudarib is not permitted to purchase a close relative of the rabb al-mal. He said: 'If there is profit in the capital, it is not permissible for him to purchase one who would become free upon him, because his share becomes free and spoils the share of the rabb al-mal, or becomes free according to the known disagreement, so disposal becomes prevented and the objective is not attained. And if he purchases them, he guarantees the mudarabah capital, because he becomes a purchaser of the slave and thereby becomes liable for the cash from the mudarabah capital. If there is no profit in the capital, it is permissible for him to purchase them, because there is no impediment to disposal, as he has no share in it such that it would become free upon him. Then if their value increases after purchase, his share among them becomes free due to his ownership of a part of his relative, and he does not guarantee anything to the rabb al-mal, because there is no action on his part in the increase of value, nor in his ownership of the increase, because this is something that is established by legal decree. So it becomes like when he inherits along with another. And the slave works to pay off the value of his share from him, because the rabb al-mal's property value is detained with him, so he works for it, as in inheritance.' Translation: If there is profit in the capital, it is not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a person who would become free upon him, because his share becomes free and the rabb al-mal's share becomes spoiled or becomes free, based on the known disagreement. So disposal becomes prevented, and the objective is not attained. If he purchases such people, he guarantees the mudarabah capital, because he becomes a purchaser of the slave for himself, so he becomes liable by paying from the mudarabah capital. If there is no profit in the capital, then purchasing them is permissible, because there is no impediment to disposal, because he has no share in it such that they would become free upon him. Then if their value increases after purchase, the mudarib's share among them becomes free, due to his owning part of his relative. And he does not guarantee anything to the rabb al-mal, because there is no action on his part in the increase of value, nor in his ownership of the increase, because this is something that is established by legal decree. So it becomes like when he inherits along with another. And the slave works to pay off the value of his share from him, because the rabb al-mal's property value is detained with him, so he works for it, as in inheritance. Elaboration: His statement: 'fa-in kana fi al-mal...' If there is profit in the capital, it is also not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a slave who would become free from the mudarib's side, like a slave who is the mudarib's dhi rahm mahram. Because from this, the mudarib's share becomes free, and the rabb al-mal's share either becomes spoiled (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or also becomes free (according to the Sahibayn). Understand it with some elaboration as follows: When the mudarabah capital has profit shared, the mudarib also has a share in it. When he purchases his father or son etc., a mahram slave, then he becomes free from his side, but only to the extent of the mudarib's share. Now according to the Sahibayn, the remainder also becomes free, because with them emancipation is not divisible, meaning emancipation cannot be split into parts. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, since emancipation is divisible, the owner has the option: either to free him, or to make him work for wages, or to take compensation from the mudarib (if the mudarib is wealthy). In any case, the slave is no longer fit to be sold. Thus the owner's share is spoiled, and this happened because of the mudarib's purchase. Therefore, his purchase is not permissible. His statement: 'wa-in lam yakun fi al-mal ribh...' etc. — The mentioned ruling is when there is no apparent profit in the mudarabah capital, then purchasing the mentioned slave for the mudarabah is valid. By 'apparent profit' is meant that the slave's value is more than the capital. Because when the slave's value is equal to or less than the capital, the mudarib's ownership in that slave is not apparent; rather the slave remains occupied with the capital. So if the capital initially was one thousand then became ten thousand, after which the mudarib purchases a slave who would become free upon him and his price is one thousand or less, then he will not become free upon him. His statement: 'fa-in zadat qimatuhum...' etc. — That is, when the mudarib purchased the relative slave, at that time his price was equal to the capital, but afterward his price increased, then to the extent of the mudarabah share the slave becomes free, because he became owner of his relative. But the mudarib is not liable for the rabb al-mal's share, because at the time of ownership the slave did not become free by the mudarib's action; rather he became free without the mudarib's choice due to the price increase. So the slave works to pay off the value of the rabb al-mal's share, because the property value is detained with him. His statement: 'kama idha warathahu ma'a ghayrihi...' etc. — The scenario of this issue is that, for example, a woman's husband had previously married Zayd's female slave, from whom a boy was born, and he remained Zayd's slave like his mother. Then that man married the aforementioned free woman, and that woman bought from Zayd the son of her husband, and she became his owner. Then the woman died, leaving her husband and one brother. So the estate is shared between them in halves. Thus half of the boy's share came into the ownership of the brother, and half into the ownership of the husband. But since the boy is the husband's son, upon coming into ownership he immediately becomes free upon his father. Now the father is not liable for anything to his wife's brother, because freeing is not his voluntary action; rather, inheritance established ownership by divine decree, and upon ownership being established, he automatically became free by legal decree. So the father is blameless in both matters. Similarly here is the case of the mudarib: he purchased his mahram without his own share, intending to sell them for their owner. But suddenly their price increased (and the increase in price is not the mudarib's voluntary action). When the price increase caused his share in the profit, he acquired ownership to the extent of his share, and that portion became free; this too is not his voluntary action. And since he did not commit any action that would cause loss to the rabb al-mal, he is also not liable.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is from the book of Mudarabah in Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah. It provides a detailed expansion of the ruling concerning a mudarib (investment manager) purchasing a slave who is a close relative (dhi rahm mahram) such that the slave would become free upon the mudarib if he acquires ownership. The passage examines two scenarios based on whether there is profit in the mudarabah capital.

The author first states that it is not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a slave because the contract of mudarabah aims at profit through disposal (tasarruf), and if the slave would become free, disposal is impossible. The ruling is compared to purchasing wine or carrion—things that cannot come into valid ownership. A contrast is drawn with a fasid (defective) sale, which is included in mudarabah because the item can be sold after possession, so profit is possible.

A question arises: if an absolute agent (wakil) purchases a slave who would become free upon the principal, it is permissible. Why the difference? Because agency is unrestricted, while mudarabah is restricted to profitable purchases. If the principal specifies a condition ('buy for me to sell'), then even an agent cannot purchase such a slave.

If the mudarib nonetheless purchases such a slave, the purchase is considered for himself, not for the mudarabah, and he becomes liable for the capital. This is analogous to an agent who acts contrary to instructions.

The core matn then addresses the situation where there is profit in the capital. The mudarib's purchase of a relative is prohibited because his share would become free, and the rabb al-mal's share would either become spoiled (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or also become free (according to Sahibayn). This prevents further disposal, defeating the purpose of mudarabah. If he does it, he guarantees the capital.

In the situation where there is no profit in the capital (i.e., no surplus beyond the principal), the purchase is permissible because the mudarib has no share yet. His ownership does not trigger emancipation at the time of purchase. However, if after purchase the slave's value increases such that there is profit, then the mudarib's share of the slave becomes free. But the mudarib is not liable for the rabb al-mal's share because the increase is not due to his action—it is a legal consequence. The slave must then work (sa'y) to pay off the value of the rabb al-mal's share, just as in the case of inheritance.

The passage concludes with an elaborate analogy from inheritance: a woman buys her husband's son (who is a slave) and then dies, leaving husband and brother as heirs. The son becomes free upon the husband because he is his father, and the husband is not liable to the brother because the freeing occurred by legal decree, not his action. Similarly, the mudarib is not liable for the increase.

The intra-Hanafi dispute is central: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation can be partial (qabil li al-tajzi), so only the mudarib's share becomes free; the rabb al-mal's share remains and can be dealt with. Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that emancipation is indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free, and the mudarib must compensate the rabb al-mal.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudārib): The investment manager in a mudarabah contract who provides labor and management.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The capital provider in a mudarabah contract.
عتق ('itq): Emancipation, freeing a slave. Here, the issue is whether it can be partial.
ذی رحم محرم (dhī raḥm maḥram): A close blood relative one cannot marry (e.g., father, son, brother). Purchasing such a slave triggers immediate emancipation.
تجزى (tajazzī): Divisibility. Here, whether emancipation can be divided into parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it not permissible for a mudarib to purchase a relative slave when there is profit in the capital?
A) Because the slave cannot be resold at a profit.
B) Because the purchase would cause the slave to become free, preventing disposal and defeating the objective of mudarabah.
C) Because it is a form of riba.
D) Because the mudarib is not allowed to buy any slaves.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib must not purchase a relative who would become free when profit exists; if no profit, it is permissible but with consequences if value later increases.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
10 min
Qiyas from Inheritance: Non-Liability for Involuntary Freeing
Elaboration of the qiyas from inheritance to mudarib's non-liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qiyas from inheritance to explain why a mudarib is not liable for the rabb al-mal's share when a slave's value increase and emancipation occur by legal decree.

Core Idea
Liability only arises from voluntary action; freeing by legal decree (e.g., inheritance, price increase) does not make the owner liable.

This lesson examines the Qiyas (analogy) used in the passage to justify the mudarib's non-liability in the no-profit scenario when the slave's value later increases. The analogy is drawn from a case in inheritance where a woman buys her husband's son (a slave), then dies, and the son becomes free upon the husband by operation of law. The husband is not liable to the co-heirs. Similarly, the mudarib is not liable because the freeing happened without his voluntary action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the asl (original case) in the qiyas
The asl is the inheritance case: a free woman buys her husband's son (who is a slave of another). On her death, the son becomes part of the estate and is inherited by her husband and her brother. The husband inherits a half-share, and upon ownership, the son becomes free immediately because he is the husband's son. The husband is not liable to the brother for the brother's share.
The ruling: no liability because freeing happened by legal decree (inheritance), not by the husband's choice.
2
Identify the far' (new case) in the qiyas
The far' is the mudarib's case: he purchases a relative slave when there is no profit. Later, the slave's value increases, creating profit and giving the mudarib a share. That share becomes free immediately. The mudarib is not liable to the rabb al-mal for the latter's share.
The mudarib's action (purchase) did not directly cause the freeing; the increase and freeing are involuntary.
3
Extract the effective cause (illah)
The common illah is that the freeing (or the acquisition leading to freeing) occurred by legal decree (hukman) without the voluntary action (sun') of the person who becomes the owner. In the asl, inheritance and the freeing are by divine decree; in the far', the price increase and freeing are by external market forces, not the mudarib's action.
The illah is 'shabah' (resemblance) because both involve ownership through a legal cause and subsequent freeing without the owner's choice.
4
Apply the hukm of the asl to the far'
Just as the husband is not liable, the mudarib is not liable to the rabb al-mal. He does not have to compensate for the rabb al-mal's share. Instead, the slave must work (sa'y) to pay off the value of that share.
The slave's work (sa'y) is a method to satisfy the rabb al-mal's right without making the mudarib a guarantor.
5
Recognise the limit of the qiyas
This qiyas only applies when the initial purchase was valid (no profit). It does not apply when the purchase was invalid (with profit). Also, it only applies to the increase; if the slave's value had not increased, the mudarib would have no share, and no freeing would occur.
The analogy is tightly bound to the facts of the far'.
