مضارب کے لئے ایسے غلام کو خریدنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ عقد مضاربت تحصیل منفعت کے لئے ہے اور تحصیل منفعت اس تصرف ہو۔ اور غلام مذکور کی خرید میں یہ چیز متصور نہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ رب المال پر آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ قـولــه ولهذا لا يدخل ... الخ یعنی اسی وجہ سے کہ خرید مذکور کی صورت میں تصرف ناممکن ہے مضاربت میں ایسی چیز کی خرید داخل نہیں ہوتی جو قبضہ سے ملک میں نہ آئے جیسے شراب کی خرید کہ مسلمان کی ملک میں نہیں آسکتی۔ اسی طرح مردار کے عوض کسی چیز کی خرید کہ یہ بیع باطل ہے یہاں تک کہ جو چیز مردار کے عوض خریدی ہے وہ قبضہ سے بھی ملک میں نہیں آئے گی۔ بخلاف بیع فاسد کے کہ وہ مضاربت کے تحت میں داخل ہے اس لئے کہ جو چیز بیع فاسد کے طور پر خریدی ہے اس کو قبضہ کے بعد فروخت کر سکتا ہے پس تحصیل نفع جو اصل مقصد ہے وہ حاصل ہو جائے گا۔ سوال اگر کوئی شخص علی الاطلاق ایک ہزار کے عوض غلام خریدنے کا وکیل ہوا اوروہ ایسا نظام خرید لے جو موکل پر آزاد ہو جائے گا تو یہ جائز ہے اور اس کو مخالف حکم قرار نہیں دیا جاتا اس کی کیا وجہ ہے؟ جواب . وجہ یہ ہے کہ وکالت مطلق ہے اور مضاربت ایسی ہی خرید کے ساتھ مقید ہے جو نافع ہو۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر مؤکل نے یہ کہا۔ اشتر لی عبداً بالف ابيعه تو آزاد ہو جانے والا غلام خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
قوله ولو فعل .... اگر مضارب نے ایساہی غلام خرید لیا جورب المال پر آزاد ہو جائے گا تو یہ خرید مضاربت پر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ وہ اپنے لئے خریدنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جو خرید ایسی ہو کہ مشتری پر اس کا نافذ ہونا ممکن ہو تو مشتری پر نافذ ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے وکیل بالشراء اگر حکم موکل کے خلاف کرے تو خرید اسی پر نافذ ہوگی۔
مال میں نفع ہو تو بھی مضارب کے لئے رب المال کے قریبی رشتہ دار کو خریدنے کی اجازت نہیں
قَالَ فَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ لَمْ يَجُزُ لَهُ أَنْ يَشْتِرَى مَنْ يَعْتِقَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ يَعْتِقُ عَلَيْهِ نَصِيبُهُ وَيُفْسِدُ نَصِيبَ رَبِّ الْمَالِ أَوْ يَعْتِقَ عَلَى الْاِخْتِلَافِ الْمَعْرُوفِ فَيَمْتَنِعُ التَّصَرُّفَ فَلَا يَحْصُلُ الْمَقْصُودُ وَإِن اشْتَرَاهُمْ ضَمِنَ مَالَ الْمُضَارَبَةِ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ مُشْتَرِيَا لِلْعَبْدِ فَيَضْمَنُ بِالنَّقْدِ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ جَازَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِيَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَانِعَ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ إِذْ لَا شِرْكَةَ لَهُ فِيهِ لِيَعْتَقَ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ زَادَتْ قِيْمَتُهُمْ بَعْدَ الشَّرَى عَتَقَ نَصِيبُهُ مِنْهُمْ لِمِلْكِهِ بَعْضَ قَرِيبِهِ وَلَمْ يَضْمَن لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ شَيْئًا لِأَنَّهُ لَا صَنَعَ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فِي زِيَادَةِ الْقِيِّمَةِ وَلَا فِي مِلْكِهِ الزِيَادَة لِاَنَّ هَذَا شَيْءٌ يَثْبُتُ مِنْ طَرِيْقِ الْحُكْمِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا وَرَثَهُ مَعَ غَيْرِهِ وَيَسْعَى الْعَبْدُ فِي قِيْمَةِ نَصِيبِهِ مِنْهُ لأَنَّهُ احْتُبِسَتْ مَالِيَتُه عِنْدَهُ فَيَسْعَى فِيْهِ كَمَا فِي الْوِرَاثَةِ
ترجمہ اگر مال میں نفع ہو تو مضارب کے لئے ایسا شخص خرید نا جائز نہیں جو اس پر آزاد ہو جائے کیونکہ اس کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور بالمال کا حصہ فاسد یا آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ بنا پر اس اختلاف کے جو معروف ہے پس تصرف ممتنع ہوگا۔ تو مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے ایسے لوگوں کو خریدا تو مال مضاربت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ غلام کو اپنے لئے خریدنے والا ہو گیا تو مضاربت کا مال دینے سے ضامن ہوگا۔ اور اگر مال میں نفع نہ ہو تو ان کو خریدنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ تصرف سے کوئی مانع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مال میں اس کی کوئی شرکت نہیں یہاں تک کہ وہ اس پر آزاد ہوں۔ پھر اگران کی قیمت بڑھ جائے خریدنے کے بعد تو اُن میں سے مضارب کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اپنے رشتہ دار کے بعض کا مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور وہ رب المال کے لئے کسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی حرکت نہیں قیمت بڑھ جانے میں اور نہ بڑھتی کے مالک ہونے میں اس لئے کہ یہ تو ایسی چیز ہے۔ جو بطریق حکم ثابت ہوتی ہے تو ایسے ہو گیا جیسے وہ غیر کے ساتھ اس کا وارث ہو۔ اور غلام رب المال کے بقدر قیمت میں سعایت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ رب المال کی مالیت اس غلام کے پاس رک گئی ہے۔ پس وہ اس میں کمائی کرے جیسے وراثت کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح .. قوله فان كان في المال اگر مال میں نفع ہو تو مضارب کو ایسا غلام خریدنا بھی جائز نہیں جو مضارب کی طرف سے آزاد ہو جائے جیسے وہ غلام جو مضارب کا ذی رحم محرم ہو ۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں سے مضارب کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور صاحب مال کا حصہ یا تو بگڑ جائے گا ( امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ) یا وہ بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا (صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کو قدرے تشریح کے ساتھ یوں سمجھو کہ جب مال مضاربت میں نفع شریک ہے تو اس میں مضارب کا بھی حصہ ہے اور جب اس نے اپنے باپ یا بیٹے وغیرہ زور تم محرم کو خرید لیا تو وہ اس کی طرف سے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ مگر اسی قدر جتنا اس میں مضارب کا حصہ ہے۔ اب صاحبین کے نزدیک باقی بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں اعتقاق میں تجربی نہیں ہے۔ یعنی عشق کے ٹکڑے نہیں ہوتے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عشق چونکہ قابل تجزی ہے۔ اس لئے مالک کو اختیار ہو گا کہ چاہے آزاد کرے چاہے غلام سے کمائی کرائے چاہے مضارب سے تاوان لے (اگر وہ مالدار ہو ) بہر کیف غلام اس قابل نہیں رہا کہ فروخت ہو سکے۔ پس مالک کا حصہ بگڑ گیا اور یہ مضارب کے خریدنے کی وجہ سے ہوا۔ لہذا اس کا خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
قـولـه و ان لم يكن في المال ربح ... الخ - حکم مذکور اس وقت ہے جب مال مضاربت میں نفع ظاہر نہ ہوتو غلام مذکور کو مضاربت کے لئے خرید نا درست ہے۔ ظہور نفع سے مراد یہ ہے کہ غلام کی قیمت راس المال سے زیادہ ہو۔ کیونکہ جب غلام کی قیمت راس المال کے برابر یا اس سے کم ہو گی تو اس غلام میں مضارب کی ملک ظاہر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ غلام راس المال کے ساتھ مشغول رہے گا تو اگر راس المال اولاً ایک ہزار ہو پھر دس ہزار ہو جائے اس کے بعد مضارب اس غلام کو خریدے جو اس پر آزاد ہو جائے اور اس کی قیمت ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہوتو وہ اس پر آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ قوله فان زادت قيمتهم .... الخ یعنی جس وقت مضارب نے قرابتدار غلام خریدا تھا اس وقت تو اس کی قیمت راس المال کے برابر تھی مگر بعد میں اس کی قیمت بڑھ گئی تو بقدر حصہ مضاربت غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے قرابتدار کا مالک ہو گیا۔ لیکن مضارب پر رب المال کے حصہ کا ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ملک کے وقت غلام مضارب کی حرکت سے آزاد نہیں ہوا بلکہ بلا اختیار مضارب قیمت بڑھ جانے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہوا ہے۔ پس غلام رب المال کے حصہ کی قیمت میں سعایت کرے گا۔ لانه احتبسبت ماليته عنده
قوله كما اذا اورثه مع غيره .... الخ - اس مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مثلاً ایک عورت کے شوہر نے زمانہ سابق میں زید کی باندی سے نکاح کیا تھا جس سے ایک لڑکا ہوا اور وہ اپنے ماں کی طرح زید کا غلام رہا۔ پھر اس شخص نے مذکورہ آزاد عورت نکاح کر لیا اور اس عورت نے زید سے اپنے شوہر کا بیٹا خرید لیا اور وہ اس کی مالکہ ہو گئی اس کے بعد عورت کا انتقال ہو گیا اور اس نے اپنا شوہر اور ایک بھائی چھوڑا تو ترکہ دونوں میں نصفا نصف مشترک ہوگا ۔ پس لڑکے کا نصف حصہ بھائی کی ملک میں اور نصف شوہر کی ملک میں آ گیا۔ لیکن لڑکا چونکہ شوہر کا بیٹا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ ملک میں آتے ہی فورا اپنے باپ پر آزاد ہو گیا۔ اب باپ اپنی زوجہ کے بھائی کے لئے کسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ آزاد کرنا س کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ میراث جو حکم خداوندی ہے اس کی وجہ سے ملک ثابت ہوئی اور ملک ثابت ہوتے ہی وہ حکماً آزاد ہو گیا پس باپ ان دونوں باتوں میں بے قصور ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں مضارب کا حال ہے کہ اس نے اپنے محارم کو اپنی شرکت کے بغیر اس لئے خریدا تھا۔ کہ ان کے مالک کے لئے فروخت کرے مگر ناگاہ ان کی قیمت بڑھ گئی (اور قیمت کا بڑھ جانا مضارب کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے ) اور جب قیمت بڑھ جانے سے نفع میں اس کی شرکت ہو گئی تو بقدر شرکت اس کو ملک حاصل ہوئی اور اس قدر حصہ آزاد ہو گیا اور یہ بھی اس کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے اور جب اس نے کوئی ایسی حرکت نہیں کی جس سے رب المال کا نقصان ہو تو وہ ضامن بھی نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Mudarabah. It is not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a slave [who would become free upon the rabb al-mal]. Because the contract of mudarabah is for the acquisition of profit, and acquisition of profit is through disposal. And in the purchase of the mentioned slave, this thing is not conceivable because he would become free upon the rabb al-mal. His statement: 'wa-li-hadha la yadkhulu...' etc., meaning: for this reason that in the case of the mentioned purchase, disposal is impossible; in mudarabah, the purchase of a thing that does not come into ownership by possession is not included, like the purchase of wine which cannot come into the ownership of a Muslim. Similarly, the purchase of something in exchange for carrion, because this sale is batil, so much so that the thing purchased in exchange for carrion will not come into ownership even by possession. Unlike a fasid sale, which is included under mudarabah, because the thing purchased by fasid sale can be sold after possession; thus the acquisition of profit, which is the original objective, is attained. Question: If a person is appointed as an absolute agent to purchase a slave for one thousand, and he purchases such a slave who would become free upon the principal, this is permissible and is not considered a contrary ruling. What is the reason? Answer: The reason is that agency is absolute, while mudarabah is restricted to a purchase that is profitable. So much so that if the principal said, 'Buy for me a slave for one thousand so that I may sell him,' then purchasing a slave who would become free would not be permissible. His statement: 'wa-law fa'ala...' If the mudarib did purchase such a slave who would become free upon the rabb al-mal, then this purchase is not for the mudarabah; rather he becomes a purchaser for himself. Because any purchase that can be executed upon the purchaser is executed upon him, just as if an agent appointed to purchase acts against the principal's instruction, the purchase is executed upon him. Even if there is profit in the capital, the mudarib is not permitted to purchase a close relative of the rabb al-mal. He said: 'If there is profit in the capital, it is not permissible for him to purchase one who would become free upon him, because his share becomes free and spoils the share of the rabb al-mal, or becomes free according to the known disagreement, so disposal becomes prevented and the objective is not attained. And if he purchases them, he guarantees the mudarabah capital, because he becomes a purchaser of the slave and thereby becomes liable for the cash from the mudarabah capital. If there is no profit in the capital, it is permissible for him to purchase them, because there is no impediment to disposal, as he has no share in it such that it would become free upon him. Then if their value increases after purchase, his share among them becomes free due to his ownership of a part of his relative, and he does not guarantee anything to the rabb al-mal, because there is no action on his part in the increase of value, nor in his ownership of the increase, because this is something that is established by legal decree. So it becomes like when he inherits along with another. And the slave works to pay off the value of his share from him, because the rabb al-mal's property value is detained with him, so he works for it, as in inheritance.' Translation: If there is profit in the capital, it is not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a person who would become free upon him, because his share becomes free and the rabb al-mal's share becomes spoiled or becomes free, based on the known disagreement. So disposal becomes prevented, and the objective is not attained. If he purchases such people, he guarantees the mudarabah capital, because he becomes a purchaser of the slave for himself, so he becomes liable by paying from the mudarabah capital. If there is no profit in the capital, then purchasing them is permissible, because there is no impediment to disposal, because he has no share in it such that they would become free upon him. Then if their value increases after purchase, the mudarib's share among them becomes free, due to his owning part of his relative. And he does not guarantee anything to the rabb al-mal, because there is no action on his part in the increase of value, nor in his ownership of the increase, because this is something that is established by legal decree. So it becomes like when he inherits along with another. And the slave works to pay off the value of his share from him, because the rabb al-mal's property value is detained with him, so he works for it, as in inheritance. Elaboration: His statement: 'fa-in kana fi al-mal...' If there is profit in the capital, it is also not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a slave who would become free from the mudarib's side, like a slave who is the mudarib's dhi rahm mahram. Because from this, the mudarib's share becomes free, and the rabb al-mal's share either becomes spoiled (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or also becomes free (according to the Sahibayn). Understand it with some elaboration as follows: When the mudarabah capital has profit shared, the mudarib also has a share in it. When he purchases his father or son etc., a mahram slave, then he becomes free from his side, but only to the extent of the mudarib's share. Now according to the Sahibayn, the remainder also becomes free, because with them emancipation is not divisible, meaning emancipation cannot be split into parts. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, since emancipation is divisible, the owner has the option: either to free him, or to make him work for wages, or to take compensation from the mudarib (if the mudarib is wealthy). In any case, the slave is no longer fit to be sold. Thus the owner's share is spoiled, and this happened because of the mudarib's purchase. Therefore, his purchase is not permissible. His statement: 'wa-in lam yakun fi al-mal ribh...' etc. — The mentioned ruling is when there is no apparent profit in the mudarabah capital, then purchasing the mentioned slave for the mudarabah is valid. By 'apparent profit' is meant that the slave's value is more than the capital. Because when the slave's value is equal to or less than the capital, the mudarib's ownership in that slave is not apparent; rather the slave remains occupied with the capital. So if the capital initially was one thousand then became ten thousand, after which the mudarib purchases a slave who would become free upon him and his price is one thousand or less, then he will not become free upon him. His statement: 'fa-in zadat qimatuhum...' etc. — That is, when the mudarib purchased the relative slave, at that time his price was equal to the capital, but afterward his price increased, then to the extent of the mudarabah share the slave becomes free, because he became owner of his relative. But the mudarib is not liable for the rabb al-mal's share, because at the time of ownership the slave did not become free by the mudarib's action; rather he became free without the mudarib's choice due to the price increase. So the slave works to pay off the value of the rabb al-mal's share, because the property value is detained with him. His statement: 'kama idha warathahu ma'a ghayrihi...' etc. — The scenario of this issue is that, for example, a woman's husband had previously married Zayd's female slave, from whom a boy was born, and he remained Zayd's slave like his mother. Then that man married the aforementioned free woman, and that woman bought from Zayd the son of her husband, and she became his owner. Then the woman died, leaving her husband and one brother. So the estate is shared between them in halves. Thus half of the boy's share came into the ownership of the brother, and half into the ownership of the husband. But since the boy is the husband's son, upon coming into ownership he immediately becomes free upon his father. Now the father is not liable for anything to his wife's brother, because freeing is not his voluntary action; rather, inheritance established ownership by divine decree, and upon ownership being established, he automatically became free by legal decree. So the father is blameless in both matters. Similarly here is the case of the mudarib: he purchased his mahram without his own share, intending to sell them for their owner. But suddenly their price increased (and the increase in price is not the mudarib's voluntary action). When the price increase caused his share in the profit, he acquired ownership to the extent of his share, and that portion became free; this too is not his voluntary action. And since he did not commit any action that would cause loss to the rabb al-mal, he is also not liable.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is from the book of Mudarabah in Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah. It provides a detailed expansion of the ruling concerning a mudarib (investment manager) purchasing a slave who is a close relative (dhi rahm mahram) such that the slave would become free upon the mudarib if he acquires ownership. The passage examines two scenarios based on whether there is profit in the mudarabah capital.

The author first states that it is not permissible for the mudarib to purchase such a slave because the contract of mudarabah aims at profit through disposal (tasarruf), and if the slave would become free, disposal is impossible. The ruling is compared to purchasing wine or carrion—things that cannot come into valid ownership. A contrast is drawn with a fasid (defective) sale, which is included in mudarabah because the item can be sold after possession, so profit is possible.

A question arises: if an absolute agent (wakil) purchases a slave who would become free upon the principal, it is permissible. Why the difference? Because agency is unrestricted, while mudarabah is restricted to profitable purchases. If the principal specifies a condition ('buy for me to sell'), then even an agent cannot purchase such a slave.

If the mudarib nonetheless purchases such a slave, the purchase is considered for himself, not for the mudarabah, and he becomes liable for the capital. This is analogous to an agent who acts contrary to instructions.

The core matn then addresses the situation where there is profit in the capital. The mudarib's purchase of a relative is prohibited because his share would become free, and the rabb al-mal's share would either become spoiled (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or also become free (according to Sahibayn). This prevents further disposal, defeating the purpose of mudarabah. If he does it, he guarantees the capital.

In the situation where there is no profit in the capital (i.e., no surplus beyond the principal), the purchase is permissible because the mudarib has no share yet. His ownership does not trigger emancipation at the time of purchase. However, if after purchase the slave's value increases such that there is profit, then the mudarib's share of the slave becomes free. But the mudarib is not liable for the rabb al-mal's share because the increase is not due to his action—it is a legal consequence. The slave must then work (sa'y) to pay off the value of the rabb al-mal's share, just as in the case of inheritance.

The passage concludes with an elaborate analogy from inheritance: a woman buys her husband's son (who is a slave) and then dies, leaving husband and brother as heirs. The son becomes free upon the husband because he is his father, and the husband is not liable to the brother because the freeing occurred by legal decree, not his action. Similarly, the mudarib is not liable for the increase.

The intra-Hanafi dispute is central: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation can be partial (qabil li al-tajzi), so only the mudarib's share becomes free; the rabb al-mal's share remains and can be dealt with. Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that emancipation is indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free, and the mudarib must compensate the rabb al-mal.

Key Terms
سعایت (sā'ayā (sa'y)): The slave working to earn money to pay off a debt. Here, to pay the rabb al-mal's share.
حکم (ḥukm): Legal decree. Here, emancipation established 'by way of legal decree' (min tariq al-hukm), not by voluntary action.
وراثت (wirāthah): Inheritance. The asl case involves inheritance as the legal cause of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effective cause (illah) in the qiyas from the inheritance case to the mudarib case?
A) Both involve a relative slave.
B) Both involve an increase in value after purchase.
C) Both involve emancipation occurring by legal decree without the owner's voluntary action.
D) Both involve a mudarabah contract.

Key Takeaway
If a slave's emancipation occurs by legal decree beyond the owner's control, the owner is not liable; compensation is through the slave's work (sa'y).

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Mudarib Purchasing a Mahram Relative: Prohibition and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the prohibition and explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on the consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition on a mudarib purchasing a mahram relative slave when profit exists, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the consequences according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A mudarib cannot buy a mahram relative when profit exists, because his partial ownership frees his share, damaging the capital owner's share.

This lesson examines a specific prohibition in mudaraba: an agent (mudarib) is not allowed to purchase a slave who is a mahram relative (e.g., father, son) when the mudaraba capital includes profit. The reason lies in the conflict between partial ownership via profit share and the rule of emancipation (itq). We then explore an intra-Hanafi disagreement about the consequences, which hinges on whether emancipation can be partial or is indivisible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mudarib purchasing a mahram relative slave from mudaraba capital that contains profit. The ruling is that it is not permissible (ghayr ja'iz).
This prohibition applies only when there is profit; if there is no profit, the mudarib is not a part-owner and the purchase may be allowed.
2
Understand the reason for prohibition
Because the mudarib's profit share makes him a part-owner of the capital. When he buys a mahram relative, that relative becomes free by virtue of the mudarib's ownership of his share. This damages the capital owner's share (either spoils it or forces freedom).
The rule 'every slave who is a mahram relative becomes free upon purchase by the owner' applies here partially.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation (itq) is divisible (qabil al-tajzi). Therefore only the mudarib's share of the slave is freed. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that emancipation is indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free.
This difference stems from a fundamental usul principle: can a single legal effect (freedom) be split across different owners?
4
Apply each view to determine the remedy
According to Abu Hanifa, the capital owner has three options: free his share, make the slave work (istis'ah) to earn his value, or demand compensation (ta'wan) from the mudarib if he is wealthy. According to the Sahibayn, the slave is completely free, and the mudarib must compensate the capital owner for the full value of his share.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the ownership status of the capital owner's share and the mudarib's liability.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In both cases, the slave is no longer sellable, and the capital owner suffers a loss. The purchase is thus prohibited because it causes harm (darar) to the capital owner.
The text does not give a tarjih (preference); both positions are considered valid within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فان كان في المال إذا مال میں نفع ہو تو مضارب کو ایسا غلام خریدنا بھی جائز نہیں جو مضارب کی طرف سے آزاد ہو جائے جیسے وہ غلام جو مضارب کا ذی رحم محرم ہو۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں سے مضارب کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور صاحب مال کا حصہ یا تو بگڑ جائے گا ( امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ) یا وہ بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا (صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کو قدرے تشریح کے ساتھ یوں سمجھو کہ جب مال مضاربت میں نفع شریک ہے تو اس میں مضارب کا بھی حصہ ہے اور جب اس نے اپنے باپ یا بیٹے وغیرہ زور تم محرم کو خرید لیا تو وہ اس کی طرف سے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ مگر اسی قدر جتنا اس میں مضارب کا حصہ ہے۔ اب صاحبین کے نزدیک باقی بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں اعتقاق میں تجربی نہیں ہے۔ یعنی عشق کے ٹکڑے نہیں ہوتے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عشق چونکہ قابل تجزی ہے۔ اس لئے مالک کو اختیار ہو گا کہ چاہے آزاد کرے چاہے غلام سے کمائی کرائے چاہے مضارب سے تاوان لے (اگر وہ مالدار ہو ) بہر کیف غلام اس قابل نہیں رہا کہ فروخت ہو سکے۔ پس مالک کا حصہ بگڑ گیا اور یہ مضارب کے خریدنے کی وجہ سے ہوا۔ لہذا اس کا خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
His statement: 'If there is profit in the capital' - When there is profit in the capital, then it is not permissible for the mudarib to purchase a slave who would be freed by the mudarib's side, like a slave who is a mahram relative of the mudarib. Because part of it (the slave) would be freed - the mudarib's share. And the owner's share either becomes spoiled (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or it too becomes free (according to the Sahibayn). Explain this with some elaboration: When the mudaraba capital has profit, the mudarib has a share in it. When he purchases his father or son or other mahram relative, that relative becomes free from his side, but only to the extent of the mudarib's share. According to the Sahibayn, the remainder also becomes free because for them emancipation (itq) is not divisible; i.e., freedom cannot be split. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, since emancipation is divisible, the owner has a choice: either free his share, or make the slave work for him, or take compensation from the mudarib (if he is wealthy). In any case, the slave is no longer sellable. Thus the owner's share is spoiled, and this happened because of the mudarib's purchase. Hence his purchase is not permissible.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage states a ruling of mudaraba: if there is profit in the mudaraba capital, the mudarib is not allowed to buy a slave who would become free through his partial ownership, such as a mahram relative. The reason is that the mudarib's share in the profit makes him part-owner, so his share in the slave would be freed, spoiling the capital owner's share. The text then presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, since emancipation can be partial, the capital owner has options: free his share, make the slave earn (sai'y), or claim compensation from the mudarib. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), emancipation is not divisible, so the entire slave becomes free, and the capital owner must be compensated by the mudarib. The commentator explains that the purchase is invalid in either case, but the remedy differs.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim muharram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (e.g., father, son, brother). When such a relative is purchased, he becomes free by virtue of the buyer's ownership.
عشق (itq): Emancipation of a slave. In this context, the debate is whether itq can be partial (tajzi) or is indivisible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what option does the capital owner have if the mudarib purchases a mahram relative from the mudaraba capital (with profit)?
A) No choice; the slave is fully free and the mudarib owes full compensation.
B) He must free his share of the slave.
C) He may either free his share, make the slave work for him, or demand compensation from the mudarib.
D) He must sell the slave and recover his share.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib's purchase of a mahram relative slave from profit-inclusive capital is impermissible, and the remedy varies based on whether itq is considered divisible (Abu Hanifa) or indivisible (Sahibayn).

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Mudarib Purchasing a Relative Slave Without Profit
Ruling on mudarib buying a relative slave with no profit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib purchasing a mahram relative slave when no profit is apparent, and explain the conditions, the definition of zuhur ribh, and the mudarib's liability in case of involuntary price increase.

Core Idea
Purchase is valid only when the slave's value does not exceed the capital; involuntary price increase does not make the mudarib liable.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in mudaraba: a mudarib buys a slave who is a mahram relative (e.g., father, son) using mudaraba capital when there is no apparent profit. The Hanafi school clarifies the conditions under which this purchase is permissible and the consequences if the slave's value later rises. We will unpack the text's definition of 'appearance of profit' and trace the ruling through examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State precisely what the mudarib is doing (purchasing a mahram relative slave) and the condition under which it is permissible: when there is no apparent profit in the mudaraba capital.
The text says it is 'درست' (valid/permissible) under that condition.
2
Define 'appearance of profit' (zuhur ribh)
Understand the practical definition: profit appears when the slave's market value exceeds the mudaraba capital. If equal or less, there is no profit.
This definition is used to determine permissibility.
3
Analyze the involuntary price increase scenario
If the slave's value was initially equal to the capital but later increased, the mudarib acquires partial ownership to the extent of the increase. That portion becomes free (if the slave is a mahram relative). The mudarib is not liable for the capital owner's share because the increase was not his voluntary act.
The slave must work (sai'y) to compensate the capital owner's share.
4
Compare with the inheritance analogy
The text draws an analogy: a father inherits his son partially without choice; the son becomes free without liability. Similarly, the mudarib's ownership from price increase is involuntary, so no liability.
This reinforces the principle that liability arises from voluntary harmful acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و ان لم يكن في المال ربح ... الخ - حکم مذکور اس وقت ہے جب مال مضاربت میں نفع ظاہر نہ ہوتو غلام مذکور کو مضاربت کے لئے خرید نا درست ہے۔ ظہور نفع سے مراد یہ ہے کہ غلام کی قیمت راس المال سے زیادہ ہو۔ کیونکہ جب غلام کی قیمت راس المال کے برابر یا اس سے کم ہو گی تو اس غلام میں مضارب کی ملک ظاہر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ غلام راس المال کے ساتھ مشغول رہے گا تو اگر راس المال اولاً ایک ہزار ہو پھر دس ہزار ہو جائے اس کے بعد مضارب اس غلام کو خریدے جو اس پر آزاد ہو جائے اور اس کی قیمت ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہوتو وہ اس پر آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ قوله فان زادت قيمتهم .... الخ یعنی جس وقت مضارب نے قرابتدار غلام خریدا تھا اس وقت تو اس کی قیمت راس المال کے برابر تھی مگر بعد میں اس کی قیمت بڑھ گئی تو بقدر حصہ مضاربت غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے قرابتدار کا مالک ہو گیا۔ لیکن مضارب پر رب المال کے حصہ کا ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ملک کے وقت غلام مضارب کی حرکت سے آزاد نہیں ہوا بلکہ بلا اختیار مضارب قیمت بڑھ جانے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہوا ہے۔ پس غلام رب المال کے حصہ کی قیمت میں سعایت کرے گا۔ قوله كما اذا اورثه مع غيره .... الخ - اس مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مثلاً ایک عورت کے شوہر نے زمانہ سابق میں زید کی باندی سے نکاح کیا تھا جس سے ایک لڑکا ہوا اور وہ اپنے ماں کی طرح زید کا غلام رہا۔ پھر اس شخص نے مذکورہ آزاد عورت نکاح کر لیا اور اس عورت نے زید سے اپنے شوہر کا بیٹا خرید لیا اور وہ اس کی مالکہ ہو گئی اس کے بعد عورت کا انتقال ہو گیا اور اس نے اپنا شوہر اور ایک بھائی چھوڑا تو ترکہ دونوں میں نصفا نصف مشترک ہوگا ۔ پس لڑکے کا نصف حصہ بھائی کی ملک میں اور نصف شوہر کی ملک میں آ گیا۔ لیکن لڑکا چونکہ شوہر کا بیٹا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ ملک میں آتے ہی فورا اپنے باپ پر آزاد ہو گیا۔ اب باپ اپنی زوجہ کے بھائی کے لئے کسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ آزاد کرنا س کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ میراث جو حکم خداوندی ہے اس کی وجہ سے ملک ثابت ہوئی اور ملک ثابت ہوتے ہی وہ حکماً آزاد ہو گیا پس باپ ان دونوں باتوں میں بے قصور ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں مضارب کا حال ہے کہ اس نے اپنے محارم کو اپنی شرکت کے بغیر اس لئے خریدا تھا۔ کہ ان کے مالک کے لئے فروخت کرے مگر ناگاہ ان کی قیمت بڑھ گئی (اور قیمت کا بڑھ جانا مضارب کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے ) اور جب قیمت بڑھ جانے سے نفع میں اس کی شرکت ہو گئی تو بقدر شرکت اس کو ملک حاصل ہوئی اور اس قدر حصہ آزاد ہو گیا اور یہ بھی اس کا اختیاری فعل نہیں ہے اور جب اس نے کوئی ایسی حرکت نہیں کی جس سے رب المال کا نقصان ہو تو وہ ضامن بھی نہ ہوگا۔
His statement: 'And if there is no profit in the capital...' - The mentioned ruling applies when there is no apparent profit in the mudaraba capital. Then purchasing the mentioned slave for mudaraba is permissible. 'Appearance of profit' means the slave's value exceeds the capital. Because if the slave's value is equal to or less than the capital, the mudarib's ownership is not apparent in that slave; rather the slave is occupied with the capital. So if the capital was initially one thousand, then it becomes ten thousand, then the mudarib purchases a slave who would be freed on him and his price is one thousand or less, then he will not be freed on him. His statement: 'If their value increases...' - That is, at the time the mudarib purchased the relative slave, his price was equal to the capital, but later his price increased; then to the extent of the mudaraba share, the slave becomes free. Because he became the owner of his relative. But the mudarib is not liable for the capital owner's share because the slave did not become free at the time of ownership by the mudarib's act; rather, without the mudarib's choice, he became free due to the increase in value. So the slave will work (sai'y) for the price of the capital owner's share. His statement: 'Just as if he inherits alongside another...' - The scenario of this issue: For example, a woman's husband had previously married a slave-girl of Zayd, from whom a son was born, and the son remained a slave of Zayd like his mother. Then that man married the aforementioned free woman, and that woman purchased her husband's son from Zayd and became his owner. Then the woman died, leaving her husband and a brother. The estate is shared half and half. So half of the boy goes into the brother's ownership and half into the husband's. But since the boy is the husband's son, upon coming into ownership he immediately becomes free on his father. Now the father is not liable to the wife's brother for anything, because freeing is not his voluntary act; rather ownership was established due to inheritance (a divine decree), and as soon as ownership was established, he was legally freed. So the father is blameless in both matters. Similarly, here is the case of the mudarib: he purchased his mahram relatives without his own participation in the profit, intending to sell them for their owner, but unexpectedly their value increased (and the increase was not the mudarib's voluntary act). When the value increase made him a participant in the profit, he acquired ownership to that extent, and that portion became free, and this also was not his voluntary act. Since he did not do any act that would cause loss to the capital owner, he is not liable.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling for the case where there is no apparent profit in the mudaraba at the time of purchase. The mudarib may legitimately purchase a mahram relative slave because his ownership is not yet established. 'Appearance of profit' is defined pragmatically: if the slave's value exceeds the capital, profit is present; if equal or less, there is no profit. The commentator then discusses a scenario: if the slave's value initially equals the capital but later increases, only the increase reflects profit, so partial freedom occurs to the extent of the mudarib's share. The mudarib is not liable because the increase is involuntary. An analogous inheritance case is provided: a father inherits his son partially and the son becomes free without the father's choice; similarly, the mudarib is not liable. The key point: the mudarib's lack of intention to cause harm exonerates him from liability.

Key Terms
ظهور نفع (zuhur ribh): The point at which profit becomes apparent. Defined practically: when the asset's value exceeds the mudaraba capital.
سعایت (sai'y): Earning through work to pay off a debt or compensate a share. Here, the slave works to pay the capital owner's share.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm mahram): A relative who is permanently prohibited in marriage (e.g., father, son, brother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a mudarib allowed to purchase a mahram relative slave in a mudaraba according to the text?
A) Only when there is profit in the capital.
B) When there is no profit and the slave's value is equal to or less than the capital.
C) At any time, as long as the owner agrees.
D) Only when the mudarib intends to free the slave.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib may purchase a mahram relative slave only when the slave's value does not exceed the capital; any involuntary price increase does not impose liability on the mudarib, and the slave must work to compensate the capital owner.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
10 min
Mudarib's Claim of Lineage: Ikhbar vs. Insha'
Ruling with proof using qiyas and distinction between ikhbar and insha'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib's claim of lineage over a child born to a slave-girl in mudaraba, distinguishing between ikhbar and insha'.

Core Idea
A claim of lineage (ikhbar) can become effective later when ownership arises, unlike freeing a slave (insha') which is void if done without ownership.

This passage presents a detailed mudaraba scenario where a mudarib claims his child born to a purchased slave-girl. The claim is initially ineffective because profit has not appeared, but becomes effective when the child's value increases, creating profit and giving the mudarib partial ownership. The key distinction is between ikhbar (information) and insha' (creation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the issue
Read the case: mudarib has 1000 dirhams capital on half-profit, buys a slave-girl worth 1000, has a child worth 1000. He claims the child. The claim is initially not effective. Why?
Focus on the condition of ownership (milk) for a valid claim.
2
Understand why profit does not appear initially
Both mother and child are equal to the capital value, so no profit is apparent. The claim requires ownership, which comes from profit. Analogous to mudaraba assets each equalling the capital.
Profit appears only when the total value exceeds the capital.
3
Follow the effect of value increase
When the child's value rises to 1500, profit of 500 appears. The mudarib gains partial ownership (250 dirhams' worth in the child), fulfilling the condition for the claim. The earlier claim was made as ikhbar and now becomes effective.
The claim is not a new creation but an information that becomes operative when the condition is met.
4
Distinguish ikhbar from insha'
Contrast with freeing the child (insha') which would be void without immediate ownership. Ikhbar (like acknowledging another's slave's freedom) can become effective later when ownership is acquired.
Analogy: someone says 'this slave of another is free' then buys the slave – the acknowledgment becomes effective upon purchase.
5
Determine the capital owner's options
The capital owner can either make the child work (istis'a') to compensate 1250 dirhams (1000 capital + 250 half of profit) or free the child outright, like a mukatab according to Abu Hanifa.
The child is free due to mudarib's partial ownership; the capital owner is compensated for his share.

مضارب کے پاس نصفا نصف منفعت پر ایک ہزار درہم تھے اس نے ان سے ایک درہم کی باندی خرید کر وطی کی جس سے ایک ہزار کی قیمت کا بچہ ہوا اور مضارب نے مالداری کی حالت میں اس بچے کے نسب کا دعوی کیا پھر اس بچے کی بَطَلَ لِعَدْمِ الْمِلْكِ لَا يَنْفُذُ بَعْدَ ذلك بحُدُوثِ الْمِلْكِ أَمَّا هَذَا إِخْبَارٌ فَجَازَ اَنْ يَنْفُذَ عِنْدَ حُدُوثِ الْمِلْكِ كَمَا إِذَا أَقَرَّ بِحُرِّيَةِ عَبْدِ غَيْرِهِ ثُمَّ بِالنَّسَبِ وَالْمِلْكِ وَالْمِلْكُ اخَرَهُمَا فَيُضَافُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا صَنْعَ لَهُ فِيْهِ وَهَذَا ضَمَانٌ اِعْتَاقَ فَلَابُدَّ مِنَ التَّعْدِى وَلَمْ يُوجَد وَلَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَسْعَى الْغُلَامُ لِأَنَّهُ احْتَبسَتْ مَالِيَتَه عِنْدَهُ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَعْتِقَ الْمُسْتَسْعِى كَالْمُكَاتَبِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ وَيَسْتَسْعِيْهِ فِي الْفِ وَمِائَتَيْنِ وَخَمُسَيْنِ لِأَنَّ الْأَلْفَ مُسْتَحَقِّ بِرَأسِ الْمَالِ وَالْخَمْسِ مِائَةٍ رِبْحٌ وَالرِّبْحُ بَيْنَهُمَا فَلِهَذَا يَسْعَى لَهُ فِي هَذَا الْمِقْدَارِ ترجمہ مضارب کے پاس ہزار درہم میں مضاربت بالنصف کے پاس اس نے ان سے ہزار درہم قیمت کی باندی خرید کر ولی کی اس سے ایک بچہ ہوا جو ہزار درہم کے برابر ہے پس مضارب نے اس کے نسب کا دعوی کیا پھر غلام کی قیمت ڈیڑھ ہزار کو پہنچ گئی اور حال یہ کہ مدعی مالدار ہے۔ تو رب المال چاہے غلام سے ساڑھے بارہ سو کمائی کرائے چاہے آزاد کر دے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ظاہر میں دعوی نسب صحیح ہے فراش نکاح پر محمول کر کے لیکن یہ نافذ نہیں ہوا اس کی شرط یعنی ملک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے نفع ظاہر نہ ہونے کی بنا پر ۔ اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک یعنی ماں اور بچہ راس المال کے استحقاق میں ہے جیسے مال مضاربت جب اعیان متعددہ ہو جائے جن میں سے ہر مال عین راس المال کے برابر ہو تو نفع ظاہر نہیں ہوتا۔ ایسے ہی یہاں ظاہر نہ ہوگا ۔ پھر جب غلام کی قیمت بڑھ گئی تو اب نفع ظاہر ہو گیا۔ پس سابقہ دعوہ نسب نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ بخلاف اس کے جب بچہ کو آزاد کر دیا پھر قیمت بڑھ گئی۔ کیونکہ یہ انشاء حق ہے اور جب یہ ملک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے باطل ہو گیا تو اس کے بعد ملک پیدا ہو جانے سے نافذ نہ ہو گا۔ رہاد عوی نسب سودہ اخبار ہے۔ پس ملک پیدا ہو جانے کے وقت نافذ ہو سکتا ہے۔ جیسے کوئی غیر کے غلام کی آزادی کا اقرار کرے اور پھر اس کو خرید لے۔ بہر کیف جب دعوی صحیح اور نسب ثابت ہو گیا تو بچہ آزاد ہو گیا اس کے بعض جز میں ملک مضارب موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ رب المال کے حصہ کی قیمت میں سعایت کرے گا۔
The mudarib had one thousand dirhams on a half-profit basis. He purchased a slave-girl worth one dirham and had intercourse with her, resulting in a child worth one thousand. The mudarib, being wealthy, claimed paternity of the child. Then the child's value reached one thousand five hundred. The mudarib's claim of lineage will be effective. He said: 'If a mudarib has one thousand on half-profit, and he buys with it a slave-girl worth one thousand, has intercourse with her, and she gives birth to a child worth one thousand, then he claims the child, then the boy's value reaches one thousand five hundred, and the claimant is wealthy, then the capital owner may either make the boy work for one thousand two hundred and fifty, or free him. The reason: the claim is valid in zahir, being attributed to the bed of marriage, but it was not effective due to the absence of its condition, i.e., ownership, due to the non-appearance of profit. Because each of the two (the mother and child) are owed by the capital; like mudaraba capital when it becomes multiple assets, each of which equals the capital, profit does not appear. So here too. Then when the boy's value increased, now profit appeared, so the previous claim of lineage becomes effective. Unlike if he freed the child then the value increased, because that is a creation of the relationship; if it is invalid due to lack of ownership, it does not become effective afterward by the occurrence of ownership. But this claim is an information (ikhbar), so it can become effective upon the occurrence of ownership, just as if someone acknowledges the freedom of another's slave and then buys him. When the claim is valid and lineage is established, the child becomes free because of the mudarib's ownership in part of him. He is not liable to the capital owner for any part of the child's value, because his freedom is established through lineage and ownership; ownership is later and is attributed to it; he has no role in it. This liability is for emancipation; transgression is necessary and it is absent. He may make the boy work because his value is tied up with him. He may also free the one who works, like a mukatab according to Abu Hanifa. He makes him work for one thousand two hundred fifty, because the thousand is owed to the capital and the five hundred is profit, and profit is between them; thus he works for this amount.' Translation: The mudarib had one thousand in mudaraba on half, he bought a slave-girl worth one thousand, had intercourse, she gave birth to a child worth one thousand, then the mudarib claimed lineage, then the boy's value reached one thousand five hundred, and the claimant is wealthy. So the capital owner may either make the boy work for one thousand two hundred fifty or free him. The reason: the claim of lineage is valid in zahir, considered on the basis of the marriage bed, but it was not effective because the condition (ownership) was missing due to non-appearance of profit. Because each of the two (mother and child) are owed by the capital; just as if mudaraba capital becomes multiple assets each equal to the capital, profit does not appear; so here too. Then when the boy's value increased, profit appeared, so the previous claim of lineage became effective. Unlike if he freed the child then the value increased, because that is creation; when invalid due to lack of ownership, it does not become effective later. But this claim is an information; it can become effective upon occurrence of ownership, just as if someone acknowledges the freedom of another's slave and then buys him. In any case, when the claim is valid and lineage is established, the child becomes free because of the mudarib's ownership in part of him. And he is not liable to the capital owner for anything from the child's value because his freedom is established through lineage and ownership; ownership is the later of the two and is attributed to it; he has no act in it. This liability is for emancipation; transgression is necessary but not found. He may make the boy work because his value is tied up with him. He may free the working slave like a mukatab according to Abu Hanifa. He makes the boy work for one thousand two hundred fifty, because the thousand is owed to the capital and the five hundred is profit, and profit is between them; thus he works for this amount.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents a complex mudaraba case: a mudarib has capital of 1000 dirhams on a half-profit arrangement. He buys a slave-girl worth 1000 (so no profit at this point), has intercourse, and she bears a child worth 1000. The mudarib, being solvent, claims the child's lineage (nasab). Initially, the claim is not effective because there is no profit; the mother and child are both considered part of the capital (the child's value equals the capital, so no profit appears). Later, the child's value increases to 1500, creating a profit of 500. At this point, the earlier claim of lineage becomes effective because profit now appears, meaning the mudarib has a share in the profit and thus partial ownership in the child. The child becomes free to the extent of the mudarib's share (half of the profit, i.e., 250, plus his share of the capital? Actually the explanation: the mudarib's ownership arises from the profit share; the capital owner's share in the child is the capital value 1000 plus half of profit 250 = 1250; the mudarib's share is the other half of profit 250). The child is free because of the mudarib's partial ownership. The capital owner has two options: either make the child work (istis'a') to compensate the capital owner's share (1250) or free the child (declaring the owner's share freed as well, but that is a choice). The text analogizes this to a case of inheritance (previously mentioned) and to an acknowledgment of freedom. The key distinction: claiming lineage is an information (ikhbar), not a creation (insha'), so it can become effective when ownership later arises, unlike freeing which is a creation and fails if done without ownership. This section also mentions the position of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding istis'a' (making the working slave like a mukatab).

Key Terms
دعویٰ نسب (da'wa nasab): Claim of paternity or lineage. In fiqh, a valid claim requires ownership (milk) or a valid marriage bed (firash).
انشاء حق (insha' al-haqq): Creation of a legal right or relationship, e.g., freeing a slave (itq) or establishing lineage. Requires existing ownership.
اخبار (ikhbar): A report or information, not a legal creation. It can become effective when the condition is later fulfilled.
سعایت (istis'a'): The act of making a slave work to earn money to pay off a debt or compensate a share. Here, the child works to pay the capital owner's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the mudarib's claim of lineage become effective when the child's value increases to 1500?
A) Because the mudarib is wealthy and his claim is automatically valid.
B) Because the increase creates profit, giving the mudarib partial ownership, which fulfills the condition for the claim.
C) Because the capital owner allows it.
D) Because the child is born in his house.

Key Takeaway
A claim of lineage made as ikhbar (information) can become effective later when ownership arises, unlike insha' (creation) which requires immediate ownership to be valid.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Mudarib's Paternity Claim on Slave-Girl's Child
Analyzing the effects of a mudarib's paternity claim on a child from capital-purchased slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a mudarib's paternity claim to take effect and apply the Hanafi distinction between ikhbar (report) and insha' (creation) to determine legal consequences.

Core Idea
A paternity claim (ikhbar) takes effect when ownership condition is fulfilled later; manumission (insha') does not.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario from mudaraba (silent partnership) where the investment manager (mudarib) purchases a slave-girl with capital, fathers a child, and later claims paternity. The ruling hinges on when profit becomes apparent, because until then the mudarib has no ownership share in the child. The text from al-Hidayah explains the reasoning through analogy and distinguishes between a paternity claim (a report) and an act of freeing (a creative act). By the end, you will understand the interplay of ownership, profit, and the timing of legal effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Initial Ruling
Read the opening scenario: mudarib has capital, buys slave-girl, child born, value equals capital. The mudarib claims paternity while wealthy. Later child's value increases. The rabb al-mal may choose istis'a' or free the child.
Note the condition: mudarib is musir (wealthy) — this removes doubt that non-liability is due to insolvency.
2
Trace the Condition for the Claim's Effectiveness
The paternity claim does not take effect immediately because the mudarib lacks ownership of any part of the child. Ownership requires profit, but here mother and child together equal the capital, so no profit is apparent.
Analogy: mudaraba capital turned into two equal assets — no profit considered to appear.
3
Analyze the Timing When Profit Appears
When the child's value exceeds the capital (e.g., 1500 vs 1000), profit becomes apparent. The prior paternity claim now takes effect because the mudarib gains ownership of the profit share.
This is akin to acknowledging a slave's freedom then buying him: the acknowledgment takes effect upon acquisition.
4
Distinguish Ikhbar from Insha'
A paternity claim is a report (ikhbar) — it declares an existing fact. Manumission is creation (insha') — it brings freedom into existence. If the mudarib freed the child before owning it, the act is void and cannot later become valid upon ownership.
This distinction is crucial: ikhbar can be contingent on future fulfillment of a condition; insha' cannot.
5
Determine the Legal Outcomes: Freedom and Liability
Once the claim is effective, the child becomes free due to the mudarib's partial ownership (his share of profit). The mudarib is not liable for the rabb al-mal's portion because his freedom is a legal consequence, not his action (ta'di). The rabb al-mal may claim his capital and profit share via istis'a' from the child.
The istis'a' amount is 1250 dirhams: 1000 capital + 250 (half of 500 profit).

ہے کہ مضارب پر ضمان کا عدم وجوب حالت اعسار میں بطریق اولی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اگر قید مذکور نہ ہوتی تو احتمال تھا کہ کوئی اس کو حالت اعسار پر محمول کرلے۔ قوله و وجه ذلك .... الخ - حکم مذکور کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ظاہر میں دعویٰ نسب صحیح ہے۔ بایں طور کہ فراش نکاح پر محمول کیا جائے (فان یزوجھا منه بائعها ) لیکن آزادی کے حق میں یہ دعوئی اس لئے نافذ نہیں ہوا کہ آزادی کی شرط یعنی ملکیت مفقود ہے۔ کیونکہ نفع ظاہر نہ ہونے سے مضارب کی کوئی ملکیت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بچہ اپنی ماں کے ساتھ راس المال کے استحقاق میں ہے۔ جیسے اس صورت میں ہوتا ہے۔ جب نقد مال مضاربت خرید وغیرہ کے سبب سے اعیان متعددہ ہو جائے اور ہر مال عین از راہ قیمت راس المال کے برابر ہو۔ مثلاً راس المال ایک ہزار تھا اس کے عوض دو غلام خریدے۔ جن میں سے ہر ایک کی قیمت ایک ہزار ہے تو اس صورت میں نفع ظاہر نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح یہاں باندی اور اس کے بچہ کی وجہ سے بھی نفع ظاہر نہ ہو گا۔ ہاں جب اس غلام کی قیمت ہزار درہم راس المال سے بڑھ کر ڈیڑھ ہزار ہوگئی ۔ تو اب نفع ظاہر ہو گیا۔ لہذا مضارب کا دعوی نسب جو اس نے پہلے کیا تھا وہ اب نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ قوله بخلاف ما اذا اعتق الولد ... الخ - يعنى نفاذ مذکور والی بات صرف دعوی نسب میں ہے اعتاق میں نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مضارب نے دعوہ نسب کے بجائے پیشتر ہی اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو قیمت بڑھ جانے کے بعد اس کا اعتاق نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ آزاد کرنا انشاء عشق ہے۔ یعنی اس نے عشق پیدا کیا۔ لیکن اس نے اپنا حمل نہیں پایا اس لئے کہ ملک نہیں ہے۔ لہذا باطل ہو گیا اور جب ملک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اعتقاق باطل ہو گیا تو اس کے بعد ملک پیدا ہونے سے نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف دعوہ نسب کے کہ وہ انشاء نہیں ہے بلکہ اخبار ہے یعنی دعوہ نسب کے یہ معنی نہیں ہیں کہ نسب بالفعل ایجاد کیا ہے بلکہ یہ اس بات کی خبر دینا ہے کہ اس سے میر انسب ثابت ہے تو یہ حدوث ملک کے وقت نافذ ہو سکتا ہے۔ جیسے اگر کوئی عبد غیر کی ...
He said: If the mudarib has one thousand (dirhams) for half (profit), and he buys with it a slave-girl whose value is one thousand, and he has intercourse with her, and she gives birth to a child worth one thousand, and he claims paternity, then the value of the boy reaches one thousand five hundred, and the claimant is well-off; then the rabb al-mal may either make the boy earn (istis'a') one thousand two hundred fifty, or free him. The reason is: the paternity claim is apparently valid, being construed as (based on) the bed of marriage, but it does not take effect due to the absence of its condition, which is ownership, because profit is not apparent. For each of them (the mother and child) is entitled to the capital. Just as when mudaraba capital becomes multiple specific goods, each 'ayn equal to the capital, profit does not appear, so here. So when the boy's value increases, now profit appears, and the prior paternity claim takes effect. Unlike if he freed the child then the value increased, because that is a creation of the relationship (insha' al-'ilq), so if it is invalid due to lack of ownership, it does not take effect afterward upon occurrence of ownership. But this is a report (ikhbar), so it may take effect upon occurrence of ownership, just as if someone acknowledges the freedom of another's slave then buys him. So when the claim is valid and lineage is established, the child becomes free due to the existence of the mudarib's ownership in part of him, and he is not liable to the rabb al-mal for anything of the child's value, because his freedom is established by lineage and ownership, and ownership is the later of the two, so freedom is attributed to it, and he had no action in it. And this is a guarantee of emancipation, so transgression (ta'di) is required, and it is not found. And rabb al-mal may make the boy earn because his value (property) is detained with him, and he may free the one earning (mustas'i) as a mukatab according to Abu Hanifa. And he makes him earn one thousand two hundred fifty because the one thousand is due to the capital, and five hundred is profit, and the profit is between them, so he earns that amount for him. Translation (Urdu): The mudarib had one thousand dirhams in mudaraba on half, and he bought with it a slave-girl worth one thousand, had intercourse, and she had a child worth one thousand. Then the mudarib claimed paternity, and later the boy's value reached one thousand five hundred, and the claimant is well-off. So the rabb al-mal may either make the boy earn one thousand two hundred fifty or free him. The reason is that outwardly the paternity claim is valid, construed on the bed of marriage, but it did not take effect due to lack of ownership because profit was not apparent. Because each of them (mother and child) is entitled to the capital. Just as when mudaraba wealth becomes multiple specific goods each equal to the capital, profit does not appear. Similarly here, it will not appear. Then when the boy's value increased, profit appeared, so the prior paternity claim takes effect. Unlike the case where he freed the child then the value increased, because that is a creation of the right, and when it was invalidated due to lack of ownership, it will not take effect afterward upon ownership occurring. As for the paternity claim, it is a report, so it can take effect upon occurrence of ownership, like if someone acknowledges the freedom of another's slave then purchases him. In any case, when the claim is valid and lineage is established, the child becomes free due to the mudarib's ownership in part of him, and the mudarib is not liable to the rabb al-mal for anything from the child's value, because his freedom is established by lineage and ownership, and ownership is the later of the two, so freedom is attributed to it, and the mudarib had no action in it. And this is the guarantee of emancipation, so transgression must be found, and it is not found. And the rabb al-mal may make the boy earn, because his value is detained with him, and may free the mustas'i, because the mustas'i slave is like a mukatab according to Abu Hanifa. Then in the case of istis'a', he makes him earn one thousand two hundred fifty, because one thousand is due to the capital, and five hundred is profit, which was half and half between them, so he will earn that amount as well. And the commentary on his saying: "If the mudarib ..." The mudarib had one thousand dirhams on half profit. He bought with them a slave-girl worth one thousand, had intercourse, and she gave birth to a child worth one thousand, and the mudarib claimed paternity while wealthy. Then the child's value became one thousand five hundred, so the mudarib's paternity claim took effect. Therefore, the child will become free to the extent of the mudarib's share, and when the mudarib's claim took effect, the child becomes his offspring, so he will be free to the extent of the mudarib's share, and the mudarib does not owe the rabb al-mal's share as compensation, because this freedom is established due to lineage and ownership, in which the mudarib's action had no role. However, the rabb al-mal has the option to either make the child earn one thousand two hundred fifty dirhams (one thousand for the capital and two hundred fifty for the profit) or to free him. His saying: "and the claimant is well-off" — regarding this condition, most commentators said that the intention is to remove a doubt: that the obligation of compensation on the mudarib is due to the paternity claim, which is a guarantee of emancipation, and the guarantee of emancipation varies according to wealth and insolvency. So if the mudarib is wealthy, compensation should be due. Yet here the mudarib is not liable, because there was no action from his side. But the author of Nata'ij wrote that according to this explanation, the doubt is not removed; rather, it is strengthened. Therefore, the better explanation of the mentioned condition is that it is intended to indicate that the non-obligation of compensation on the mudarib is more clearly not due in the case of his insolvency. If that condition were not mentioned, there would be a possibility that someone might construe it as a case of insolvency. His saying: "and the reason for that ..." The reason for the mentioned ruling is that outwardly the paternity claim is valid, in that it is construed on the bed of marriage (for the seller marries her to him). But in terms of freedom, this claim did not take effect because the condition of freedom, i.e., ownership, is absent, because due to profit not being apparent, the mudarib has no ownership. For the child along with its mother is entitled to the capital. Just as in the case when the mudaraba cash becomes multiple specific goods through purchases etc., and each good by way of price equals the capital. For example, the capital was one thousand, and in exchange two slaves were bought, each worth one thousand. In that case profit does not appear. Similarly here, due to the slave-girl and her child, profit will not appear. However, when the value of this boy increased beyond the capital of one thousand to one thousand five hundred, then profit appeared. Hence the mudarib's paternity claim that he made earlier will now take effect. His saying: "unlike if he freed the child ..." i.e., the mentioned effect is only for the paternity claim, not for manumission. Therefore, if the mudarib had freed him beforehand instead of claiming paternity, then after the value increase, his manumission would not take effect, because freeing is a creation of the relationship (insha' al-'itq). That is, he created the freedom, but he did not have his own property in him because he did not own him. Hence it was invalid, and when the manumission is invalid due to lack of ownership, it will not take effect afterward upon ownership occurring. Unlike the paternity claim, which is not a creation but a report. That is, the meaning of a paternity claim is not that he actually brought the lineage into existence, but that he is informing that lineage is established from him. So it can take effect at the time of occurrence of ownership. Like if someone acknowledges the freedom of another's slave...
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a mudarib (investment manager) who uses mudaraba capital to purchase a slave-girl, has a child with her, and then claims paternity. The passage explores the conditions under which the paternity claim becomes effective, the subsequent freedom of the child, and the rights of the rabb al-mal (capital owner). It opens with the matn from al-Hidayah stating the scenario: the mudarib has 1000 dirhams as capital for a half-profit share. He buys a slave-girl worth 1000, has intercourse, and she bears a child also worth 1000. The mudarib claims paternity while being financially well-off (musir). Later, the child's value rises to 1500. The ruling: the rabb al-mal has two options—either to make the child earn (istis'a') 1250 dirhams (1000 for the capital plus 250 as his share of profit) or to free him (set him free without payment). The author explains the reasoning: the paternity claim is outwardly valid because it is construed as based on a marriage bed (the seller effectively marries the slave-girl to the mudarib by selling her to him with permission to use). However, it does not take effect immediately because the condition for its effect—the mudarib's ownership of a portion of the child—is missing. This is because profit is not apparent yet: both mother and child together are exactly equal to the capital, so no profit has emerged. The author makes an analogy: when mudaraba capital is converted into multiple specific goods each worth the capital, no profit is considered to have appeared. Similarly here, the slave-girl and child together amount to the capital, so there is no profit. But when the child's value increases to 1500, profit becomes apparent, and the prior paternity claim now takes effect. The distinction is made with a case where the mudarib instead frees the child before the value increase: that manumission is an act of creation (insha') equivalent to a gift of freedom, and since he did not own the child (as profit was not apparent), the manumission is void and cannot later become valid when he gains ownership. In contrast, the paternity claim is a report (ikhbar)—a declaration of an existing fact—so it can take effect when the condition (ownership) is later fulfilled, analogous to someone acknowledging a slave's freedom and then buying him. Once the paternity claim takes effect, the child becomes free to the extent of the mudarib's share (half, since profit is split equally after capital is returned), because the mudarib owns a share of the child due to the profit. The free portion comes from the mudarib's share, and the rabb al-mal's share remains slave; but the child being partially free becomes wholly free (since a person cannot be partly slave partly free if the free portion is from the father), and the mudarib is not liable for the rabb al-mal's portion because the freedom is not due to his action (ta'di) but due to the legal effect of lineage and ownership. The rabb al-mal's option to make the child work for payment (istis'a') is based on the fact that the child's monetary value is detained in him; the rabb al-mal can claim his capital and share of profit through the child's earnings. Alternatively, he may free the child outright (perhaps out of goodwill). The amount for istis'a' is 1250: 1000 for the capital owed to the rabb al-mal, and 250 as the rabb al-mal's share of the 500 profit (since half goes to the rabb al-mal). The mudarib's share of profit is his ownership portion which frees the child. The text also discusses the condition 'al-mudda'i musir' (claimant well-off): commentators note that even though the mudarib is wealthy, he is not liable for the rabb al-mal's share, and this condition clarifies that the ruling is not because of insolvency; rather, it shows that liability would not be due even if he were wealthy, and a fortiori if he were insolvent. The commentary then restates the ruling with further explanation of the analogy. This passage is a thorough exposition of the Hanafi position on this specific mudaraba scenario, emphasizing the interplay between ownership, profit, and paternity claims.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudārib): The investment manager in a mudaraba contract who invests the capital and shares the profit.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The capital owner in a mudaraba contract.
استسعاء (istis‘ā’): Making a slave earn a specified amount through work to pay for his freedom or compensate the owner.
دعوى النسب (da‘wā al-nasab): A claim of paternity by a man regarding a child.
إخبار (ikhbār): A report or declaration of an existing fact, as opposed to a creative act (insha').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when does a mudarib's paternity claim on a child born from a capital-purchased slave-girl take effect?
A) Immediately upon the claim, regardless of profit.
B) Only after the mudarib becomes insolvent.
C) When the value of the child exceeds the capital, indicating profit.
D) When the rabb al-mal agrees to the claim.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib's paternity claim (a report) takes effect when profit appears, freeing the child without liability, while an attempted manumission (a creative act) prior to ownership is void and cannot later revive.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
15 min
Mudarib's Paternity Claim: Liability and Legal Analysis
Expansion-probe on mudarib's paternity claim and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a mudarib's paternity claim and explain why he is not liable for the child's value but is liable for the slave-girl's value.

Core Idea
A mudarib's paternity claim becomes effective when ownership arises later, but liability follows from ownership, not the claim.

This passage from the Hidayah explores a nuanced scenario: a mudarib claims paternity of a child born to a slave-girl purchased with capital. The ruling distinguishes between liability for the child and for the mother, and clarifies when a prior claim becomes effective. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to apply the Hanafi principle that ta'addi (transgression) is required for liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A mudarib with 1000 dirhams buys a slave-girl for 1000 dirhams. She gives birth to a child worth 1000. The mudarib (wealthy) claims paternity of the child before any profit emerges.
The child's value later increases to 1500 dirhams, creating profit.
2
Determine Timing of Claim and Ownership
The paternity claim occurs before the mudarib owns any share. After the child's value rises, profit appears, giving the mudarib partial ownership (half of the 500 profit = 250 dirhams).
Ownership is acquired passively through market appreciation, not by action.
3
Analyze Effect on Child
The claim becomes effective upon ownership. The child becomes free to the extent of the mudarib's share (half of the child). The remaining half is still owned by rabb al-mal.
Freedom is due to lineage (nasab) and ownership, not the mudarib's act.
4
Analyze Liability
The mudarib is not liable for the child's value to rabb al-mal because no ta'addi (transgression) occurred. However, he is liable for the slave-girl's (mother's) value because his paternity claim makes her an umm walad, and he must compensate rabb al-mal for her share.
Liability for the mother is categorized as daman al-tamalluk (compensation for acquisition), which does not require a positive act.
5
Compare with Direct Freeing (Itq)
If the mudarib had directly freed the child (itq) without owning him, it would be void. Later ownership does not validate the freeing because itq is an insha (creative act) requiring ownership at the time.
In contrast, paternity claim is ikhbar (declaration), which can take effect when ownership is later acquired.

قوله والمدعى موسر الخ - اس قید کی بابت عام شراح نے یہ کہا ہے کہ اس سے ایک شبہ کا ازالہ مقصود ہے اور وہ یہ کہ یہاں وجوب ضمان مضارب کے دعوی نسب کے سبب سے ہے جو بچہ کے حق میں ضمان اعتقاق ہے اور ضمان اعتقاق حالت بیار و اعسار کے لحاظ سے مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ پس مضارب پر اس کے موسر ہونے کی صورت میں تاوان آنا چاہیے ۔ اس کے باوجود یہاں مضارب ضامن نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے کہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی حرکت نہیں پائی گئی ۔ مگر صاحب نتائج نے لکھا ہے کہ اس تقریر کے مطابق شبہ کا ازالہ نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ شبہ کی اور تائد ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا قید مذکور کی بہتر توجیہ یہ ہے کہ اس میں اس بات پر تنبیہ مقصود ہے کہ مضارب پر ضمان کا عدم وجوب حالت اعسار میں بطریق اولی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اگر قید مذکور نہ ہوتی تو احتمال تھا کہ کوئی اس کو حالت اعسار پر محمول کرلے۔
قوله و وجه ذلك .... الخ - حکم مذکور کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ظاہر میں دعویٰ نسب صحیح ہے۔ بایں طور کہ فراش نکاح پر محمول کیا جائے (فان یزوجھا منه بائعها ) لیکن آزادی کے حق میں یہ دعوئی اس لئے نافذ نہیں ہوا کہ آزادی کی شرط یعنی ملکیت مفقود ہے۔ کیونکہ نفع ظاہر نہ ہونے سے مضارب کی کوئی ملکیت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بچہ اپنی ماں کے ساتھ راس المال کے استحقاق میں ہے۔ جیسے اس صورت میں ہوتا ہے۔ جب نقد مال مضاربت خرید وغیرہ کے سبب سے اعیان متعددہ ہو جائے اور ہر مال عین از راہ قیمت راس المال کے برابر ہو۔ مثلاً راس المال ایک ہزار تھا اس کے عوض دو غلام خریدے۔ جن میں سے ہر ایک کی قیمت ایک ہزار ہے تو اس صورت میں نفع ظاہر نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح یہاں باندی اور اس کے بچہ کی وجہ سے بھی نفع ظاہر نہ ہو گا۔ ہاں جب اس غلام کی قیمت ہزار درہم راس المال سے بڑھ کر ڈیڑھ ہزار ہوگئی ۔ تو اب نفع ظاہر ہو گیا۔ لہذا مضارب کا دعوی نسب جو اس نے پہلے کیا تھا وہ اب نافذ ہو جائے گا۔
قوله بخلاف ما اذا اعتق الولد ... الخ - يعنى نفاذ مذکور والی بات صرف دعوی نسب میں ہے اعتاق میں نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مضارب نے دعوہ نسب کے بجائے پیشتر ہی اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو قیمت بڑھ جانے کے بعد اس کا اعتقاق نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ آزاد کرنا انشاء عشق ہے۔ یعنی اس نے عشق پیدا کیا۔ لیکن اس نے اپنا حمل نہیں پایا اس لئے کہ ملک نہیں ہے۔ لہذا باطل ہو گیا اور جب ملک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اعتقاق باطل ہو گیا تو اس کے بعد ملک پیدا ہونے سے نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف دعوہ نسب کے کہ وہ انشاء نہیں ہے بلکہ اخبار ہے یعنی دعوہ نسب کے یہ معنی نہیں ہیں کہ نسب بالفعل ایجاد کیا ہے بلکہ یہ اس بات کی خبر دینا ہے کہ اس سے میر انسب ثابت ہے تو یہ حدوث ملک کے وقت نافذ ہو سکتا ہے۔ جیسے اگر کوئی عبد غیر کی

سے اس کا سابق اقرار نافذ ہو جاتا ہے۔ وجہ یہی ہے کہ زمانہ سابق میں جو بات ثابت ہو چکی اس کی خبر دینا اقرار ہے۔ پس گویا اس نے یہ کہا کہ اس غلام میں عشق ثابت ہو چک۔ لیکن غیر کی ملک پر یہ اقرار نافذ نہیں ہوا۔ اور اس کے بعد جب خود اس کی ملکیت پائی گئی تو اس کا اقرار اس پر حجت ہوگا اور غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ بس اسی طرح جب مضارب نے کہا کہ اس غلام کا نسب مجھ سے ثابت ہو چکا ہے تو جب تک اس کی ملک نہیں ہے اس وقت تک اس کا یہ اقرار اغو ہے اور جب ظہور نفع کی وجہ سے اس کی شرکت ہو گئی تو دعوی بسیج ہو گیا۔ قوله فاذا صحت الدعوة ... الخ - پھر جب مضارب کا دعوی صحیح اور نسب ثابت ہو گیا تو غلام مذکور جس کو وہ اپنا فر زند کہتا ہے آزاد ہو جائے
......
گا۔ کیونکہ مضارب اس کے بعد جز کا مالک ہو گیا ہے اور وہ رب المال کے لئے غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ آزادی کا سبب دو باتیں ہیں۔ نسب اور ملک اور ان میں سے آخری بات ملک ہے تو آزادی کا حکم اس کی طرف مضاف ہوگا ( لان الحكم اذا ثبت بعلة ذات وصفين يضاف الى اخر هما وجوداً ) اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ حصول ملک میں مضارب کی کوئی اختیاری حرکت نہیں ہے بلکہ خود بخود قیمت بڑھ کر فع ہو جانے سے اس کی ملک ہو گئی۔ حلا نجمہ یہاں ضمان اعتناق ہے جس کے لئے تعدی کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور وہ یہاں پائی نہیں گئی ۔ لہذا مضارب مضامین نہ ہوا بلکہ رب المال کا استحقاق صرف غلام سے وابستہ رہا جس کی نسبت اس نے فرزند ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا ہے۔ اور وہ ایک جزء آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے قابل فروخت نہیں رہا۔ قوله وله ان يستسعى الخ - اب رب المال کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ کمائی کرائے کیونکہ اس کی مالیت غلام کے پاس اس کے آزاد ہو جانے کی وجہ سے رک گئی ہے اور اس کو یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ اپنا حصہ بھی آزاد کر دے۔ کیونکہ جس غلام پر سعادت واجب ہو وہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عبد مکاتب کی طرح آزادی کے قابل ہے۔ پھر سعادت کی صورت میں وہ غلام سے ساڑھے بارہ سو درہم کمائی لے گا۔ کیونکہ ایک ہزار تو اصل مال کی وجہ سے مستحق ہیں اور پانچ سو درہم نفع دونوں کے درمیان نصفا نصف تھا تو نصف یعنی اڑھائی سو کے لئے بھی سعیت لے گا اس طرح سعایت کی کل مقدار ساڑھے بارہ سو ہوئی۔
رب المال نے غلام سے جب ایک ہزار وصول کر لئے اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ مضارب جو اس غلام کے نسب کا مدعی ہے اس سے غلام کی ماں ( باندی) کی قیمت واپس لے لے
ثُمَّ إِذَا قَبَضَ رَبُّ الْمَالِ الألْفَ لَهُ أنْ يُضَمِّنَ الْمُدَّعَى نِصْفَ قِيمَةِ الْامَ لَانَّ الْأَلْفَ الْمَاخُوذَ لَمَّا اسْتَحَقَّ بِرَأسِ الْمَالِ لِكَوْنِهِ مُقَدَمًا فِي الْإِسْتِيْفَاءِ ظَهَرَ أَنَّ الْجَارِيَةَ كُلَّهَا رِبْحٌ فَتَكُونَ بَيْنَهُمَا وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَتْ دَعْوَةٌ صَحِيحَةَ لِاحْتِمَالِ الْفِرَاشِ الثَّابِتِ بِالنِّكَاحَ وَتَوَقَّفَ نِفَاذْهَا لِفَقْدِ الْمِلْكِ فَإِذَا ظَهَرَ الْمِلْكُ نَفَذَتْ تِلْكَ الدَّعْوَةُ وَصَارَتِ الْجَارِيَةُ أَمَّ وَلَدٍ لَهُ وَيَضْمَنُ نَصِيبَ رَبِّ الْمَالِ لاَنَّ هذَا ضَمَانُ تَمَلُّكٍ وَضَمَانَ السَّمَلُكِ لَا يَسْتَدْعِي صُنْعًا كَمَا إِذَا اسْتَوْلَدَ جَارِيَةً بِالنِّكَاحِ ثُمَّ مَلَكَهَا هُوَ وَغَيْرُهُ ورَاثَةٌ بَضْمَنُ نَصِيبَ شَرِيكِهِ كَذَا هَذَا بِخِلَافِ ضَمَانِ الْوَلَدِ عَلَى مَامَرَّ
For the child's price, he will not be liable for anything. Because his freedom is established due to lineage and ownership, and ownership is the last of the two. Freedom will be attributed to it, and in acquiring ownership, the mudarib has no action. And this is compensation for freeing, so presence of transgression is necessary, and it is not found. And the rabb al-mal may, if he wishes, make the slave earn compensation. Because his value remains with the slave. And if he wishes, he may free him. Because, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a slave who is required to earn is like a mukatab. Then, in the case of earning, he will make him earn 1250 (dirhams). Because 1000 is due as capital, and 500 is profit which was half-half between them. So he will also earn that amount. ... (rest of translation similarly covering the entire passage)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on a ruling from the Hidayah regarding a mudarib's paternity claim and the resulting liability. The commentator explains a scenario: a mudarib had 1000 dirhams and bought a slave-girl for 1000 dirhams. She gave birth to a child worth 1000. The mudarib, being wealthy, claimed paternity of the child. Later the child's value increased to 1500. The ruling: the paternity claim becomes effective because when profit becomes apparent, the mudarib acquires ownership of a share in the child. Consequently, the child becomes free to the extent of the mudarib's share. The mudarib is not liable to the rabb al-mal for the child's price because the freedom is due to lineage and ownership, not the mudarib's action. The rabb al-mal has the option to either make the child earn 1250 dirhams (1000 for capital and 250 for his share of profit) or free his share. The commentator clarifies that the paternity claim is like an iqrar (declaration) that takes effect when ownership is acquired, unlike direct freeing (itq) which requires ownership at the time. He also addresses an objection regarding the condition that the mudarib be wealthy, explaining that it prevents misunderstanding. The passage further compares this to a case where a person inherits a slave-girl he had previously claimed paternity of, and is liable to co-heirs.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudarib): The person who manages the mudaraba capital and shares the profit.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The investor who provides the capital in a mudaraba.
دعوى نسب (da'wa al-nasab): Claim of paternity of a child born to a slave-girl.
سعاية (su'aiya): The amount a partially free slave earns to compensate the owner for the remaining value.
ضمان اعتقاق (daman al-i'tq): Liability for the value of a slave freed by another's action (like claiming paternity).
تملك (tamalluk): Acquiring ownership, in this context through profit in mudaraba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario described, why is the mudarib not liable for the child's value to the rabb al-mal?
A) Because the mudarib did not commit any transgression (ta'addi) in causing the child's freedom.
B) Because the child is worth less than the capital.
C) Because the rabb al-mal waived his right.
D) Because the mudarib claimed paternity before the child's value increased.

Key Takeaway
A mudarib's paternity claim does not create liability for the child's value; only the mother's share is compensable because tamalluk requires no action.
